Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
6 min
Condition for Qiyas: Original's Evidence Must Not Cover Branch
Condition for valid qiyas regarding original's evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a qiyas is invalid because the original's textual evidence already covers the branch case, and apply this condition to analogical reasoning.

Core Idea
Qiyas is invalid if the original's text already applies to the branch — it becomes unnecessary.

This lesson introduces a crucial condition for valid analogical reasoning (qiyas) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: the evidence (dalil) that establishes the ruling of the original case must not also explicitly cover the branch case. If it does, using qiyas is arbitrary and superfluous. We will examine the rationale, a concrete example, and how this condition ensures that qiyas is used only where the text is silent.

Guided Path
1
State the condition
Identify the condition: the proof of the original (dalil al-asl) must not include the ruling of the branch (hukm al-far).
This is one of several conditions for qiyas in Hanafi methodology.
2
Analyze the consequence of violation
If the original's proof does cover the branch, then establishing the branch ruling by qiyas instead of directly by that proof is arbitrary (tahakkum) and unnecessarily lengthy (tatwil bi la taa'il).
The goal is to avoid redundancy in legal reasoning.
3
Examine the example
The text gives an example: performing qiyas of gypsum (jiss) on rice (dhurra) based on the shared cause of standard measure (kayl) for the ruling of riba. The hadith 'Do not sell a dirham for two dirhams nor a sa' for two sa's' is the original's proof. Since this hadith already prohibits all items sold by measure (including gypsum), qiyas is unnecessary.
The original's proof (the hadith) covers gypsum, so qiyas is invalid.
4
Understand the deeper principle
The author notes that when the proof of the cause (dalil al-illa) is a text (nass), it must not verbally include the branch case. Otherwise, the qiyas is wasted (daa'a al-qiyas). This ensures that qiyas is only used where no direct textual ruling exists.
This principle safeguards the priority of textual evidence over reasoning.
5
Apply the condition to new cases
Given a proposed qiyas, first check if the original's dalil (Qur'an, Sunnah, Ijma) already applies to the branch case. If it does, the qiyas is invalid and you must use the text directly.
Practice with examples to internalize this condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها أن لا يكون دليله أي حكم الأصل شاملاً لحكم الفرع وإلا وإن كان شاملاً كان إثباته بالقياس دون دليل الأصل تحكماً وتطويلاً بلا طائل مثلاً إذا قاس الجص على الذرة بجامع الكيل في حكم الربوية ثم أثبت ربوية الذرة بحديث لا تبيعوا الدرهم بدرهمين، ولا الصاع بالصاعين فيمكن أن يثبت ربوية الجص الحديث ويكون القياس تطويلاً من غير طائل ومن ههنا يعلم أن دليل العلة إذا كان نصاً وجب أن لا يتناول الفرع لفظاً بحيث يخرج حكمه منه وإلا ضاع القياس ويكون تطويلاً من غير طائر فافهم
And among them is that its proof, i.e., the proof of the original ruling, should not include the ruling of the branch. Otherwise, if it does include it, then establishing it by qiyas instead of the proof of the original is arbitrary and unnecessarily lengthy. For example, if one performs qiyas of the gypsum upon rice due to the shared cause being standard measure in the ruling of riba, and then establishes the riba of rice by the hadith 'Do not sell a dirham for two dirhams nor a sa' for two sa's', then it is possible to establish the riba of gypsum by the hadith, and the qiyas becomes unnecessarily lengthy. And from here it is known that when the proof of the cause is a text, it must not verbally include the branch such that its ruling issues from it; otherwise, the qiyas is wasted and becomes unnecessarily lengthy. So understand.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage states a condition for the validity of qiyas: the evidence for the original case (دليل الأصل) must not already cover the branch case (الفرع). If it does, then using qiyas is superfluous and arbitrary. The example given is qiyas of gypsum (جص) on rice (ذرة) based on the common cause (جامع) of standard measure (الكيل) in the law of riba. However, the hadith itself explicitly prohibits trading in standard measures, so it already covers gypsum as well. Thus, qiyas is unnecessary. The author further emphasizes that if the textual evidence for the cause (دليل العلة) is a text (نص), it must not verbally include the branch; otherwise, qiyas is pointless. This condition is specific to Hanafi usul methodology, ensuring that qiyas is only used where the original's proof does not directly apply.

Key Terms
دليل الأصل (dalīl al-aṣl): The textual or consensus-based evidence that establishes the ruling of the original case in qiyas.
دليل العلة (dalīl al-ʿilla): The evidence that establishes the effective cause (ʿilla) in qiyas.
القياس (al-qiyās): Analogical reasoning extending a ruling from an original case to a branch case due to shared cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is qiyas of gypsum on rice considered invalid in the given example?
A) Because the original's evidence already includes gypsum via the hadith on riba.
B) Because gypsum and rice are not the same substance.
C) Because the hadith does not mention gypsum.
D) Because qiyas is always invalid in transactions.

Key Takeaway
For valid qiyas, the original's textual evidence must not already cover the branch; otherwise the reasoning is superfluous and arbitrary.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate

Condition: The Original Must Not Be a Branch of Another Original
Stating and arguing a condition of qiyas with counterarguments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition regarding qiyas on a branch original, explain the rationale, and evaluate the opposing view's weakness.

Core Idea
The cause in qiyas must be identical — if the original is itself a branch, its cause differs, breaking qiyas.

This passage from al-Fawatih al-Rahamut discusses a subtle condition for valid qiyas: the original case must not be a branch of another original. The Hanafis argue that if the original's own ruling is based on a different cause, then equality of cause is lost, invalidating the qiyas. The Hanabila and al-Basri disagree, but the author considers their view weak. Understanding this condition sharpens your ability to evaluate qiyas arguments in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition in dispute
What is the condition being argued? The original must not be a branch of another original. This means the ruling of the original should not itself be derived through qiyas from a different original.
The dispute is only when the cause in the two originals differs.
2
State the Hanafi position and its proof
Hanafis hold that if the original is a branch, qiyas is invalid because equality of cause is required. The cause in the branch-original is different from the cause used in the current qiyas, breaking the necessary equality.
Example: qiyas of wudu on tayammum for intention (cause: purification) vs. qiyas of tayammum on prayer (cause: worship).
3
Identify the opposing view
The Hanabila and Abu Abdullah al-Basri argue that equality of cause is not required. They claim the ruling in the original is established by text/consensus, while the branch uses qiyas, so evidence can differ.
They analogize: just as evidence (dalil) need not be the same, cause need not be the same.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The author calls their view weak (ولا يخفى ضعفه). Qiyas is defined as equality in ruling through equality in cause; if cause differs, it is not true qiyas. The original's ruling may be from text/consensus, but the cause that made it applicable to the branch must be the same.
The text emphasizes that the ruling in both original and branch ultimately comes from the text or consensus of the original, and qiyas only shows inclusion.
5
Determine the practical consequence for debate
If the opponent concedes the original but not the cause, the qiyas fails. The proponent must establish the cause by its methods. Conceding only the ruling does not suffice; the cause must be identical.
The Shafi'i example of killing a Muslim by a dhimmi illustrates how conceding the original but not the cause leads to invalidity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها أن لا يكون) حكم الأصل (فرعاً) لأصل آخر (خلافاً للحنابلة وأبي عبد الله البصري) من المعتزلة والنزاع) إنما هو (مع اختلاف العلة) في الأصلين (كقياس الوضوء على التيمم في وجوب النية (لأنه طهارة) مثله وقياس التيمم على الصلاة لأنه عبادة مثلها، فقد اختلف العلة (وأما) القياس على أصل هو فرع لأصل آخر بناء على اتفاقها أي اتفاق العلة في الأصلين كقياس الخل على الزيت بجامع الوزن وقياس الزيت على الملح بذلك الجامع ، فاتفاق على جوازه لكن فيه تطويل المسافة، فينبغي أن يقاس على أصل الأصل أوّلاً لنا : لا مساواة في العلة بين الفرع وأصله، لأنه ثبت الحكم في الأصل الذي هو فرع لعلة أخرى غير العلة التي يقاس بها، ولا قياس بدون المساواة، الحنابلة والبصري (قالوا: لا يجب المساواة في الدليل بين الأصل والفرع، فإن الحكم في الأصل يثبت بنص أو إجماع، وفي الفرع بالقياس (فكذا) لا يجب المساواة (في العلة) فيجوز أن يثبت الحكم في الأصل لعلة وفي الفرع الأخرى (ولا يخفى ضعفه) فإن بين الصورتين بوناً بعيداً، فإن القياس هو المساواة في الحكم بالتساوي في العلة، وقد انعدمت، وأما الدليل، فهو أمارة دالة على الحكم، فيجوز نصب أمارتين مختلفتين في الأصل والفرع، بل نقول : التحقيق أن الحكم في الأصل والفرع بنص الأصل أو إجماعه وإنما القياس يظهر تضمنه حكم الفرع واندماجه فيه، فثبت المساواة في الدليل أيضاً فافهم ((وهذا الاختلاف (إذا كان الأصل فرعاً سلمه المستدل دون المعترض وأما العكس وهو ما إذا سلمه المعترض دون المستدل (ففاسد اتفاقاً، كقول شافعي: قتل المسلم بالذمي تمكنت فيه شبهة هي عدم المساواة فإن المسلم معصوم الدم، وكفر الذمي مبيح، إلا أنه سقط بعارض العهد فلا يقتص كالمثقل) فإنه لا يقتص إذا قتل به للشبهة من جهة الآلة فعدم القصاص في القتل بالمثقل لا يراه الشافعي (وذلك) أي فساده لاعترافه ببطلان (دليله أي القياس باعتراف بطلان مقدّمته وهي حكم الأصل (ولو أراد) المستدل (الإلزام) بهذا القياس (لم يتم أيضاً لأن المسلم إنما هو الحكم لا العلة) فللمعترض أن العلة فلا يتجه الإلزام، وهذا يدل على انتهاضه الزاماً بعد إثباته العلة بطرقها ولجواز اعترافه بالخطأ في الأصل فقط أو في أحدهما أي الأصل أو العلة (لا على التعيين كذا في شرح المختصر) فلا يلزم منه الإلزام بثبوت الفرع ، وهذا لو تم لدل على عدم الانتهاض مطلقاً، ولو أثبت العلة بدليلها
And among them is that the ruling of the original should not be a branch of another original, contrary to the Hanabila and Abu Abdullah al-Basri from the Mu'tazila. The dispute is only when the cause differs in the two originals, like qiyas of wudu upon tayammum in the obligation of intention because both are purification, and qiyas of tayammum upon prayer because it is worship like it; here the cause differs. As for qiyas on an original that is a branch of another original based on the agreement of the cause in the two originals, like qiyas of vinegar upon oil by the common cause of weight and qiyas of oil upon salt by that same cause, they agree on its permissibility but it involves lengthening the path; it is better to make qiyas on the original of the original first. We argue: there is no equality of cause between the branch and its original, because the ruling in the original that is a branch is established by another cause different from the cause by which one makes qiyas, and there is no qiyas without equality. The Hanabila and al-Basri said: Equality in evidence between original and branch is not required, for the ruling in the original is established by text or consensus, while in the branch by qiyas; likewise, equality in cause is not required, so it is permissible that the ruling in the original is for one cause and in the branch for another. Its weakness is not hidden, for there is a great distance between the two situations. Qiyas is equality in ruling through equality in cause, and that is absent. As for evidence, it is an indicator of the ruling, so it is permissible to set up two different indicators in original and branch. Rather, we say: In truth, the ruling in both original and branch is by the text or consensus of the original; qiyas only shows the inclusion of the branch's ruling in it. So equality in evidence is also established, so understand. This dispute, when the original is a branch which the proponent concedes but the opponent does not, and the opposite when the opponent concedes but the proponent does not, is invalid by agreement, like the Shafi'i saying: Killing a Muslim by a dhimmi involves a doubt of inequality, for the Muslim's blood is inviolable and the dhimmi's disbelief permits it, but it is removed by the prevenient covenant, so there is no retaliation, like the heavy object; for there is no retaliation when killed with a heavy object due to doubt from the instrument. The Shafi'i does not see the absence of retaliation in killing with a heavy object. That is, its invalidity because he admits the invalidity of his evidence, i.e., the qiyas, by admitting the invalidity of its premise which is the ruling of the original. And if the proponent intends to compel by this qiyas, it would also not succeed because what is conceded is only the ruling, not the cause. So the opponent can deny the cause, so compulsion is not effective. This indicates its effectiveness as compulsion after establishing the cause by its methods, and because he may admit error in the original only or in one of them, i.e., original or cause, not specifically, as in Sharh al-Mukhtasar. So compulsion to establish the branch does not follow. If this were valid, it would indicate absolute ineffectiveness, even if he established the cause by its evidence.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage presents a condition for qiyas: the original case (الأصل) must not itself be a branch (فرع) of another original. The Hanafi position is that if the original is a branch of another original, the cause (علة) in that original may differ from the cause used in the current qiyas, breaking the required equality of cause. The Hanabila and Abu Abdullah al-Basri disagree, allowing qiyas on a secondary original even if the cause differs, but the author considers their view weak. The text then discusses scenarios when the opponent concedes the original or the cause, and the effect on the validity of qiyas in debate. The example of a Shafi'i qiyas regarding retaliation for a Muslim killed by a dhimmi illustrates how conceding the original but not the cause renders the qiyas ineffective. The author concludes that the proponent must establish the cause by its proper methods, and if the opponent admits error only in the original, the qiyas fails. This condition is crucial for the proper application of qiyas in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
العلة (al-ʿilla): The effective cause that justifies the extension of a ruling from the original to the branch in qiyas.
الأصل (al-aṣl): The case whose ruling is established by text or consensus and serves as the basis for qiyas.
الفرع (al-farʿ): The branch case to which the ruling is extended via qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi position on qiyas using an original that is itself a branch of another original?
A) It is always valid if the cause is the same.
B) It is invalid if the cause in the branch-original differs from the cause in the qiyas.
C) It is valid according to all scholars.
D) It is invalid even if the cause is the same.

Key Takeaway
For valid qiyas, the original must not be a branch of another original with a different cause; equality of cause is essential.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Compound Qiyas: Definition and Types
Defining compound qiyas and its two types with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define compound qiyas, distinguish its two types (murakkab al-asl and murakkab al-wasf), and explain why it is not accepted as sound proof in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Compound qiyas relies on opponent's concession, not textual evidence — weak in establishing rulings.

This lesson examines a nuanced concept in Hanafi usul: compound qiyas (القياس المركب). Unlike regular qiyas which builds on an original established by text or consensus, compound qiyas depends solely on the opponent's agreement. Understanding this distinction is crucial for grasping the limitations of qiyas in dialectical argumentation and why Hanafis require independent proof of the original.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Locate the definition of compound qiyas in the Arabic text: it is qiyas where the original is established only by the opponent's agreement, not by text or consensus.
The Hanafis do not consider this a condition for the validity of qiyas itself, but for its effectiveness in debate.
2
Distinguish the two types
Note the two subtypes: compound of the original (مركب الأصل) where the opponent prevents the cause (علة), and compound of the description (مركب الوصف) where the opponent prevents the existence of the description used as cause.
The key difference lies in what is prevented: the cause itself versus the factual description serving as cause.
3
Analyze the examples
Study the example of the mukatib for compound of the original: the Shafi'i likens a free man killing a slave to a mukatib case; the Hanafi prevents the cause (slavery) pointing to uncertainty of the guardian. For compound of the description, examine the divorce suspension case: the opponent claims the description 'suspension' exists; the Hanafi says it is immediate execution.
These examples illustrate how the Hanafi rebuttal operates by blocking the opponent's line of analogy.
4
Understand the evidentiary requirement
The passage concludes that mere agreement on the original is insufficient; the proponent must independently prove the original by text or consensus to complete the debate.
This underscores that compound qiyas is not accepted as conclusive proof; it only serves a dialectical purpose.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تسليم إحدى المسلمات ولم تكن القضايا المسلمة من مقاطع البحث) إذ يبقى البحث بمنعها (والكل باطل على ما نقرر في محله وهو كتاب الجدل من المنطق والحق أن المسلم كالمفروض في حكم الضروري لا يصح إنكاره (فإنكاره أشد من الإلزام) فحينئذٍ يصح الإلزام بالقياس على فرع سلمه الخصم لكن بعد إثبات العلة بالدليل أو التسليم (ومنها) أي من شروط الأصل، لكن لا لصحة القياس في نفسه بل للانتهاض على المناظر) ولذا لم يذكره الحنفية في كتبهم أن لا يكون الأصل (ذا) قياس مركب وهو القناعة بالموافقة) أي موافقة الخصم (فقط) من غير إثباته بنص أو إجماع ( بأن يقول كل بقياس في إثبات الأصل (ومن ثمة يسمى مركباً وقيل : إنما سمي مر مركباً للاختلاف في ترتب الحكم على العلة في الأصل، ويكون الخصم الموافق في الأصل (مانعاً علة الآخر أي مانعاً عليه الوصف الذي ادعاه وإن سلم وجوده في الأصل (أو وجودها في الأصل، ويحتمل أن يقع حالاً من فاعل الموافقة المقدر، أو من فاعل يقول (والأول) وهو الذي منع فيه العلة (مركب الأصل كالشافعية) يقولون : المقتول الذي قتله الحر ( عبد فلا يقتل به الحر) الذي قتله ( كالمكاتب) الذي قتله الحر وترك وفاء، والورثة لا تقتل الحر به اتفاقاً، فيقول الحنفي: لا نسلم أن العلة) في عدم قتل الحر بالمكاتب الرق)، بل جهالة المستحق الوالي للقصاص من السيد والورثة لاختلاف الصحابة في عبديته وحرته فإن كان عبداً فالولي السيد وإن كان حرّاً فالأولياء الورثة (فقال زيد) ابن ثابت (عبد) وهو (و) قال ابن مسعود (حر) هو إن ترك ما يفي بكتابته في «التيسير»، روي البيهقي عن الشعبي : كان زيد يقول : المكاتب عبد ما بقي عليه درهم، لا يرث ولا يورث، وكان علي رضي الله عنه يقول إذا مات المكاتب وترك مالاً قسم ماله على ما أدى وعلى ما بقي فما أصاب ما أدى فللورثة وما أصاب ما بقي فلمواليه، وكان عبد الله يقول يؤدي إلى مواليه ما بقي من مكاتبته ولورثته ما بقي فإن صحت علتي) هذه (بطل إلحاقك) لعدم وجودها في الفرع (وإلا) تصح علتي (فيمتنع حكم الأصل لظهور فساد ما كنت بنيته عليه (ولا يتأتى مثل هذا الجواب إلا) من (مجتهد) فإنه يقدر على منع حكم الأصل (فاستبان عدم كفاية الموافقة) في الأصل (فللمستدل إثباتها إتماماً للمناظرة في الصحيح) من المذهب خلافاً للبعض (والثاني) هو الذي منع فيه وجود الوصف الذي علل به مركب الوصف، كما في مسألة تعليق الطلاق بالنكاح إنه (تعليق فلا يصح كزينب التي أتزوجها طالق) فإنه لا ويلغو (فيقول) الحنفي (لا) تعليق في الأصل بل تنجيز فلم يوجد الوصف الذي علل به (فإن صح هذا (بطل الإلحاق أي إلحاق عدم صحة التعليق به ( وإلا) أي وإن لم يصح فتمنع فلا نسلم (الأصل من عدم صحة زينب التي أتزوجها طالق بل تطلق عند وجود النكاح (أقول في هذا أي في مركب الوصف (منع العلية) ففي المثال المذكور منع علية التعليق لعدم الصحة (إذ لا معنى لمنع الأصل مع تقدير وجودها فيه وتسليم (اعتبارها وإيجابها الحكم فما في شرح المختصر أن الثاني اتفقا فيه على الوصف الذي يعلل به المستدل محل نظر) إذ لا فيه (إلا) أن يقال : الخصم في (الأول أي في مركب للأصل يدير الحكم على علته) أي على
Conceding one of the premises, and the conceded propositions are not from the subjects of research, because research remains by denying them, and all is invalid according to what we establish in its place, which is the book of dialectic from logic. The truth is that the conceded is like the assumed in the ruling of the necessary, its denial is not valid; its denial is stricter than compulsion. Then compulsion by qiyas on a branch conceded by the opponent is valid, but after establishing the cause by evidence or concession. (And among them) i.e., among the conditions of the original, but not for the validity of qiyas itself, rather for effectiveness in debate, and therefore the Hanafis did not mention it in their books: that the original should not be a compound qiyas, which is being satisfied with the opponent's agreement alone, without establishing it by text or consensus, by saying everything by qiyas in establishing the original. Hence it is called compound; and it was said: it is called compound due to the difference in the arrangement of the ruling on the cause in the original. And the opponent who agrees on the original is a preventer of the other's cause, i.e., he prevents the description he claimed even if he concedes its existence in the original, or its existence in the original. It is possible that it is a circumstantial accusative from the implied subject of 'agreement' or from the subject of 'says'. And the first, where the cause is prevented, is compound of the original, like the Shafi'is say: the killed person whom a free man killed is a slave, so the free man is not killed for him, like the mukatib whom a free man killed and he left a fulfillment, and the heirs do not kill the free man for him by agreement. So the Hanafi says: We do not concede that the cause for not killing the free man for the mukatib is slavery, rather it is the ignorance of the one entitled to retaliation between the master and the heirs, due to the Companions' disagreement on his slave status and freedom: if he was a slave, the master is the guardian, and if free, the heirs are the guardians. So Zaid ibn Thabit said he is a slave, and Ibn Mas'ud said he is free if he left enough to fulfill his kitabah. Al-Taysir related from al-Shu'bi: Zaid used to say: The mukatib is a slave as long as a dirham remains upon him, he does not inherit nor is inherited. And Ali ibn Abi Talib said: When the mukatib dies and leaves wealth, his wealth is divided based on what he paid and what remains: what corresponds to what he paid goes to the heirs, and what corresponds to what remains goes to his patrons. And Abdullah used to say: he pays to his patrons what remains of his kitabah and his heirs take what remains. So if my cause is valid, your inclusion is invalid due to its absence in the branch. Otherwise, my cause is valid, so the ruling of the original is prevented due to the apparent corruption of what you built upon it. And such a response can only come from a mujtahid, for he is able to prevent the ruling of the original. So it became clear that agreement on the original is insufficient; so the proponent must establish it to complete the debate according to the sound view of the madhhab, contrary to some. And the second is where the existence of the description used as cause is prevented, as in the issue of suspending divorce upon marriage: it is a suspension, so it is not valid, like saying 'Zaynab whom I marry is divorced'; for it is invalid. So the Hanafi says: No, in the original it is not a suspension but immediate execution, so the description used as cause does not exist. If this is valid, the inclusion is invalid, i.e., including the invalidity of suspension to it. Otherwise, if it is not valid, then you prevent and we do not concede the original that 'Zaynab whom I marry is divorced' is invalid; rather it takes effect upon the existence of marriage. I say: In this, i.e., in compound of description, prevention of causality, in the mentioned example prevention of causality of suspension due to invalidity, for there is no meaning for prevention of the original while assuming its existence in it and conceding its consideration and effect. So what is in Sharh al-Mukhtasar that in the second both agree on the description used by the proponent as cause is open to consideration, for there is nothing in it except that it is said: the opponent in the first, i.e., in compound of the original, bases the ruling on its cause, i.e., on
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage discusses compound qiyas (القياس المركب), which is a qiyas where the original is not established by text or consensus but only by the opponent's agreement for the sake of debate. The Hanafis do not usually mention this as a condition for qiyas itself, but for effectiveness in debate (الانتهاض على المناظر). Compound qiyas is divided into two types: compound of the original (مركب الأصل) and compound of the description (مركب الوصف). In compound of the original, the opponent prevents the cause (يمنع العلة) that the proponent claims, even while conceding the original. Example: the Shafi'i claims that a free man who kills a slave is not killed because the slave is similar to a mukatib, but the Hanafi responds by preventing the cause (slavery) and pointing to ignorance of the right guardian. In compound of the description, the opponent prevents the existence of the description (وصف) that is used as the cause, e.g., in suspending divorce upon marriage: the opponent claims the description 'suspension' exists, but the Hanafi says it is immediate execution, not suspension. The passage emphasizes that mere agreement on the original is insufficient; the proponent must still provide evidence for it. This section is essential for understanding the limitations of qiyas in disputation.

Key Terms
القياس المركب (al-qiyās al-murakkab): A qiyas where the original case is not proven by text or consensus but only by the opponent's agreement, thus considered weak in debate.
مركب الأصل (murakkab al-aṣl): Type of compound qiyas where the opponent prevents the cause (علة) claimed by the proponent.
مركب الوصف (murakkab al-waṣf): Type of compound qiyas where the opponent prevents the existence of the description (وصف) used as the cause.
مكاتب (mukātib): A slave who has entered a contract with his master to purchase his freedom by paying installments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main characteristic of compound qiyas (قياس مركب)?
A) The original is established by text or consensus.
B) The original is established only by the opponent's agreement.
C) The cause is always agreed upon by both parties.
D) It is the strongest form of qiyas.

Key Takeaway
Compound qiyas is not a valid proof; the original must be independently established by text or consensus.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
15 min
Condition That the Original Should Not Be Composite Qiyas
Explains condition for qiyas in debate and its two types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify qiyas murakkab (composite qiyas), distinguish its two types, and apply the condition that the original must not be composite for valid argument in debate.

Core Idea
Qiyas fails in debate if the original itself relies on qiyas—composite qiyas leads to regress and weakens the argument.

In Hanafi usul, qiyas is a valid source of law, but when engaging in debate (munazara), there is an important condition: the original (asl) must not be established by another qiyas. This condition is not about the validity of qiyas itself, but about the strength of the argument. The passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut explains this condition and its two types: composite original (murakkab al-asl) and composite attribute (murakkab al-wasf). Understanding this distinction is crucial for constructing sound analogical arguments in scholarly debate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
The passage states that for a strong debate, the original (asl) should not be a composite qiyas. This means the asl must be proven by text or consensus, not by another qiyas. If it is composite, the opponent can refute by challenging the asl's establishment.
Hanafis do not mention this condition in their usul works because it pertains to debate protocol, not validity of qiyas itself.
2
Distinguish the two types
Murakkab al-asl (composite original): the opponent attacks the cause (illa) of the asl, denying that the claimed cause is the actual cause. Murakkab al-wasf (composite attribute): the opponent denies the existence of the claimed attribute (wasf) in the asl.
In both cases, the opponent prevents the analogy from proceeding by undermining the asl's foundation.
3
Analyze the example of murakkab al-asl
The Shafi'i argument: a free man who kills a mukatab (slave on contract) should not be executed, analogizing to a full slave. The Hanafi responds: the cause is not slavery but uncertainty of the guardian due to the mukatab's mixed status. Thus the Hanafi attacks the Shafi'i's cause in the asl.
This shows prevention of cause (man' al-illa).
4
Analyze the example of murakkab al-wasf
The case: 'Zaynab whom I marry is divorced' – the opponent claims it is a suspension (ta'liq) and thus invalid. The Hanafi says: in the original, it is immediate (tanjiz), not suspension, so the claimed attribute does not exist in the asl.
This shows prevention of existence of the attribute (man' al-wasf).
5
Understand the debate implication
The condition ensures the asl is independently established. If the opponent concedes the asl but challenges the cause or its existence, the proponent must prove his cause with evidence, not rely on mere agreement.
The passage clarifies that assuming the cause's effect is hypothetical; the opponent likely denies causation entirely.

بدليل ما وينتهض عليه، لأنه معترف بصحة الموجب لأن الكلام على تقدير تسليم الإيجاب (وقد ثبت وجوده بالدليل فلزم) القول بموجبه ومعلوله (لأن المناظر تلو الناظر) فكما أنه يقول بما أدى إليه الدليل، كذلك المناظر (هكذا ينبغي أن يفهم هذا المقام لكن يجب يعلم أن فرض تسليم صحة إيجاب الوصف الذي ادعاه الحكم المتفق عليه من قبيل المحال، كيف لا والخصم يقول بعليته وإيجاب نقيض ذلك الحكم، فلا يمكن تسليم إيجاب عينه، وهل هذا إلا تهافت؟ فينبغي أن يقول : فإذا بين بالدليل علية ما ادعى وأثبت وجوده بدليل ينتهض، لأن ما ثبت بالدليل يجب الاعتراف به ولا مرد له فافهم
And among them (i.e., the conditions of the original [asl]), not for the validity of qiyas itself but for strong argument against the opponent—therefore the Hanafis did not mention it in their books—is that the original should not be a composite qiyas, which is satisfaction with agreement (i.e., the opponent's agreement) only, without proving it by text or consensus, by each one saying by qiyas in proving the original. Hence it is called 'composite'. And it is said it is called composite due to the difference in the arrangement of the ruling on the cause in the original, and the opponent who agrees on the original becomes a preventer of the other's cause, i.e., preventing the attribute he claimed, even if he acknowledges its existence in the original, or its existence in the original. It is possible that it is a circumstantial accusative from the assumed agent of agreement, or from the agent of 'he said'. The first, which is prevention of the cause, is 'composite original', like the Shafi'is say: the killed person who is killed by a free man is a slave, so the free man is not killed for him, like a mukatab who is killed by a free man and leaves enough to pay his kitaba, and the heirs do not kill the free man by agreement. The Hanafi says: We do not accept that the cause for not killing the free man for the mukatab is slavery; rather it is ignorance of the entitled guardian of retaliation from the master and the heirs due to difference of the Companions regarding his being a slave or free. For if he is a slave, the guardian is the master, and if free, the guardians are the heirs. Zaid ibn Thabit said he is a slave, and Ibn Mas'ud said he is free if he left what suffices his kitaba in al-Taysir. al-Bayhaqi narrated from al-Sha'bi: Zaid used to say: the mukatab is a slave as long as one dirham remains upon him, he does not inherit nor is inherited. And 'Ali (RA) used to say: when the mukatab dies and leaves property, his property is divided according to what he paid and what remained; whatever corresponds to what he paid is for the heirs, and whatever corresponds to what remained is for his masters. And 'Abdullah used to say: he pays to his masters what remains of his kitaba, and his heirs get what remains. If my cause (this) is correct, your analogy fails due to its absence in the branch; otherwise, if my cause is correct, the ruling of the original is prevented due to the apparent corruption of what you built upon it. Such a response only comes from a mujtahid, for he is able to prevent the ruling of the original. So it becomes clear that mere agreement on the original is insufficient; the proponent must prove it to complete the debate according to the sound position of the school, contrary to some. The second is prevention of the existence of the attribute which was the cause—composite attribute—as in the case of suspending divorce upon marriage: it is a suspension and thus invalid, like 'Zaynab whom I marry is divorced', for it does not become void. The Hanafi says: there is no suspension in the original but rather instant, so the attribute (causation) did not exist. If this is correct, the analogy fails; otherwise, if it is not correct, then prevention: we do not accept the original of the invalidity of 'Zaynab whom I marry is divorced'; rather she is divorced upon the existence of marriage. I say in this (i.e., composite attribute) is prevention of causation. In the mentioned example, prevention of causation of suspension for lack of validity, for there is no meaning to prevention of the original while its existence is assumed and its consideration and effect are acknowledged. So what is in Sharh al-Mukhtasar that the second case is agreed upon concerning the attribute which the proponent causes is subject to consideration, for there is nothing in it except to say: the opponent in the first (i.e., composite original) directs the ruling on his cause, i.e., on the cause of the cause which the opponent himself presented, and negates the causation of the proponent's cause. In the second, he directs it on his opponent's negation and says: your cause, if found in the original, would prevent its ruling and require its opposite. So the intended meaning of both agreeing on the causation of the attribute absolutely for the original, as according to the proponent, or its opposite as according to the opponent, makes prevention of the original's ruling valid when it exists. And the intended meaning of its being conceded is conceding the soundness of its effect on the agreed ruling. Thus the commentator of al-Mukhtasar said: when the cause is conceded—i.e., the soundness of its effect on the agreed ruling—then the proponent can prove its existence by some evidence and be stringent against him, because he acknowledges the soundness of the effective cause, as the discussion is on the assumption of acknowledging the effect. And its existence has been proven by evidence, so he must accept its implications. For the opponent is a follower of the proponent: just as he says what evidence leads to, so does the opponent. This is how this passage should be understood. But one must know that assuming the soundness of the effect of the attribute he claimed on the agreed ruling is impossible; how could it not be, since the opponent claims its causation and the opposite effect? So it is impossible to concede the effect of the same; is this not contradiction? So one should say: when he demonstrates by evidence the causation of what he claimed and proves its existence by evidence, he is stringent, because what is proven by evidence must be acknowledged and cannot be rejected. So understand.
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut explains a condition of the original (asl) in qiyas for debate (munazara): the asl must not itself be established by qiyas (composite qiyas). The condition is not for the validity of qiyas itself but for the argument to be strong against an opponent. The Hanafis did not mention this in their usul books because it pertains to debate protocol. Two types are discussed: (1) murakkab al-asl where the opponent attacks the cause (illa) of the proponent's asl, and (2) murakkab al-wasf where the opponent challenges the existence of the claimed attribute (wasf) in the asl. The example for the first is the dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding killing a free man for a mukatab (slave on contract). The Hanafi asserts that the cause for not executing the free man is not slavery but the ignorance of the rightful claimant (wali) due to disagreement among Companions on the mukatab's status. The opponent claims slaves (including mukatab) do not die for free men, but the Hanafi shows the asl (killing a free man for a slave) is not a settled ruling, so the qiyas is composite and invalid. The second example is suspending divorce upon marriage: 'Zaynab whom I marry is divorced.' The Hanafi says this is a conditional sentence, but the asl (suspension) is not present; rather it is immediate (tanjiz). Thus the claimed cause (ta'liq) does not exist in the asl. The passage also clarifies that the opponent's concession of the cause's effect (tasleem al-illa) is a hypothetical step; in reality, the opponent denies causation. The proponent must prove causation by evidence, not merely rely on the opponent's assumption.

Key Terms
مركب الأصل (murakkab al-asl): A type of composite qiyas where the opponent prevents the cause (illa) of the proponent's asl, i.e., denies that the cause the proponent claims for the asl is the actual cause.
مركب الوصف (murakkab al-wasf): A type of composite qiyas where the opponent denies the existence of the claimed attribute (wasf) in the asl.
القياس المركب (al-qiyas al-murakkab): A qiyas in which the original (asl) itself is established by qiyas, or where the opponent agrees on the asl but disputes the cause (illa) or its existence in the asl. It is insufficient for debate because it leads to regress or contradiction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the condition of the original (asl) discussed in this passage regarding qiyas in debate?
A) The asl must be established by qiyas to be strong.
B) The asl must not be based on qiyas (i.e., should not be composite).
C) The asl must be agreed upon by both parties without proof.
D) The asl must be a simple qiyas without conditions.

Key Takeaway
For a qiyas to be persuasive in debate, the original (asl) must be independently established by text or consensus, not by another qiyas.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate

The Conditions of the Original (Asl) in Qiyas: Dispute and Certainty
Discussing the acceptance of proving the asl by text when disputed, and that the asl need not be qat'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether a disputed or zanni original is valid for qiyas, and explain the logical argument for its acceptance.

Core Idea
A disputed original is acceptable in qiyas; certainty is not required — conjecture suffices for practical rulings.

In qiyas (analogical reasoning), the original case (asl) must be established. But what if the ruling of the asl itself is disputed? And must the asl be absolutely certain? This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut addresses these two conditions. The Hanafi school takes a practical approach: even a disputed or speculative original can serve as the basis for qiyas in matters of practice ('amaliyyat).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two issues
The passage discusses two separate conditions of the asl: (a) can the asl be proven by text after qiyas is presented, and (b) must the asl be certain?
2
State the opinion of the objectors
Some scholars say that if the asl is disputed, it must be agreed upon by consensus before qiyas; otherwise, the debate becomes too lengthy.
This is the 'qil' position.
3
Explain the Hanafi response
The sound position (al-ashah) is that such proof is accepted, because refusing it would lead to an infinite regress — any premise can be challenged and require proof, and the asl being a legal ruling does not make it special.
The distinction that the asl is a legal ruling is considered weak.
4
Analyse the argument for accepting zanni asl
The author asserts that certainty (qat') is not a condition; rather, conjecture (zann) suffices in all practical matters. This reflects the Hanafi recognition that in fiqh, most rulings are based on zanni evidence.
The phrase 'وليس منها قطيعته على المذهب المختار' is key.
5
Note the practical consequence
This ruling widens the scope of qiyas: scholars can use rulings based on strong probability (e.g., from ahad hadith) as originals for analogy.
It prevents paralysis in legal argumentation.

ولو كان حكم الأصل مختلفاً بينهما فحاول إثباته بنص) بعد ترتيب القياس أولاً ( ثم) إثبات علته (بطريقها ثانياً (قيل : لا يقبل هذا النحو في المناظرة (بل لا بد من الإجماع على الأصل (إما مطلقاً أو بينهما وذلك لضم نشر الجدال) إذ لا بد لإثبات الأصل لكونه حكماً شرعياً مثل ما لا بد منه لأجل إثبات المطلوب، فتطول المناظرة ويكبر الجدال ( والأصح القبول) أي قبول هذا النحو من الإثبات لأنه لو لم يقبل) هذا لم يقبل في المناظرة مقدمة تقبل (المنع وحاول المستدل إثباتها بدليل لأن) المانع وهو تسلسل البحث) وتكثر الجدال (عام) في الصورتين فإنه لا بد لإثبات هذه المقدمة ما لا بد منه لأصل المطلوب، فيلزم التطويل في المناظرة والفرق بأنه أي الأصل (حكم شرعي مثل المطلوب (الأول يستدعي ما يستدعيه فيلزم تسلسل البحث بخلاف المقدمات الأخرى) فإنها لا تستدعي ما يستدعيه المطلوب الأول (ضعيف) لأنه قد يكون مقدّمة الدليل حكماً شرعياً، وأيضاً لا دخل لكونه حكماً شرعياً، فإن تسلسل البحث كما يلزم في الحكم الشرعي، كذا في غيره (أقول: الأولى أن يقال : لو أثبت الأصل أولاً ثم قاس قبل اتفاقاً، فكذا العكس) وهو أن يقيس أوّلاً ثم يثبت الأصل كما هو فيما نحو فيه (لأن المسافة واحدة (صاعداً كما فيما نحن فيه (ونازلاً) كما إذا أثبت الأصل أوّلاً وتعيين الطريق ليس من دأب المناظرين) لعله ردّ لما في «شرح المختصر أن هذا أمر اصطلاحي فلا مشاحة فيه فافهم ، وليس منها) أي من شروط الأصل (قطعيته) على المذهب (المختار بل يكفي الظن في العمليات كلها، فكذا
And if the ruling of the original was disputed between them, and he attempted to prove it by text after arranging the qiyas first, then prove its cause by its method second, it was said: this manner is not accepted in debate; rather consensus on the original is necessary, either absolutely or between them, because it spreads dispute. For proving the original, being a legal ruling, requires what is necessary for proving the desired, so the debate becomes long and the dispute increases. The correct view is acceptance—i.e., acceptance of this manner of proof—because if this were not accepted, a premise could be accepted for prevention in debate, and the proponent would attempt to prove it by evidence, because the preventer (i.e., the chain of inquiry and increased dispute) is general in both cases. For proving this premise requires what is necessary for the original desired, leading to prolongation. The distinction that the original is a legal ruling like the first desired, requiring what it requires, thus leading to chain of inquiry unlike other premises which do not require what the first desired requires, is weak, because a premise of evidence may be a legal ruling. Also, being a legal ruling has no bearing, for chain of inquiry occurs with legal rulings and otherwise. I say: the better is to say: if he proved the original first then analogized, it is agreed; similarly the reverse—i.e., that he analogizes first then proves the original as in our case—because the distance is the same, ascending as here or descending. Determining the method is not the habit of debaters. Perhaps this is a response to what is in Sharh al-Mukhtasar that this is a conventional matter, so no dispute. So understand. And it is not among the conditions of the original that it be certain (qat'i) according to the chosen position; rather conjecture is sufficient in all practical matters. Likewise.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on conditions of the original (asl) in qiyas for debate. It addresses the case where the ruling of the asl itself is disputed between the two debaters. The proponent may present the qiyas first and then try to prove the asl by textual evidence (nass) and its cause by its method. Some say this is not permissible because it leads to excessive dispute; rather consensus on the asl is required. However, the sound position (al-ashah) is that it is accepted, because the alternative (forcing consensus) leads to impossibility. The claim that the asl being a legal ruling would cause a regress is weak, since any premise can be a legal ruling. The commentator (Mulla Jiwan?) suggests that the order (proving asl first or after qiyas) does not matter because the distance to proof is the same; it is merely conventional. Finally, the passage states that the asl does not need to be certain (qat'i); it is sufficient that it is overwhelmingly likely (zanni) in practical matters ('amaliyyat). This is the chosen Hanafi position. This aligns with the Hanafi view that qiyas is valid even if based on speculative evidence.

Key Terms
قطعية الأصل (qat'iyyat al-asl): The certainty of the original ruling. The Hanafi chosen position is that the asl need not be qat'i; zanni (conjecture) suffices in practical matters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the chosen Hanafi position regarding the certainty (qat'iyya) of the original (asl) in qiyas?
A) The asl must be qat'i in all cases.
B) The asl must be qat'i only in matters of 'ibadat.
C) The asl need not be qat'i; zanni is sufficient in practical matters.
D) The asl must be based on consensus.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts a disputed or speculative original (asl) in qiyas to avoid infinite regress, and holds that certainty is not required in practical matters.

Certainty of the Original Ruling in Qiyas is Not Required
Debating whether the asl must be qat'i or zanni suffices

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi position that zann in the asl suffices for qiyas and evaluate the opposing claim about dissipation of conjecture.

Core Idea
Conjecture in the original does not dissipate; it remains as a necessary consequence of the premises.

This passage from Fawātih al-Rahamūt addresses a key condition in qiyas: must the original ruling (al-asl) be certain (qat'i) or can it be based on conjecture (zann)? The Hanafi school firmly holds that zann suffices in all practical matters. The author refutes an opposing view that multiple zanni premises would cause conjecture to completely dissipate, using a logical argument that the conjecture about the sought ruling is an inseparable necessary consequence of the conjecture about the premises. Understanding this ruling is essential for proper legal analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed condition
Is qat'iyyat al-asl a condition for qiyas? The matn says no: certainty is not among the conditions of the original.
2
State the opponents' objection
Opponents claim that with multiple zanni premises, conjecture weakens until it completely dissipates in the branch.
This is the claim of 'al-idmiḥlāl'.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
The author rebuts that weakening does not necessitate complete dissipation; the lāzim argument prevents it.
The response is from the original author (مصنف) and the super-commentator (أقول).
4
Understand the lāzim proof
Conjecture about the conclusion is a necessary consequence (lāzim) of conjecture about the premises; it cannot separate or dissipate.
This is a rational proof: if the premises are conjectured, the conclusion is necessarily conjectured as well.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليس منها أي من شروط الأصل قطعيته أي قطعية الأصل على المذهب المختار بل يكفي الظن في العمليات كلها، فكذا هي في الأصل خلافاً للبعض زعماً منهم بأن الأصل لو كان مظنوناً فيضعف الظن بكثرة المقدمات المظنونة حتى يضمحل في الفرع، وأشار المصنف إلى دفعه بقوله (وكون الظن يضعف بكثرة المقدمات التي يتوقف عليها القياس لا يستلزم الاضمحلال بالكلية حتى لا يبقى في الفرع أصلاً) أقول: بل لا يجوز الاضمحلال فإن اللازم واجب الثبوت عند ثبوت الملزوم والظن بالمطلوب لازم للظن بالمقدمات فلا ينفك عنه فتدبر
And among them (i.e., the conditions of the original) is not its certainty—i.e., the certainty of the original—according to the chosen school; rather, conjecture (zann) suffices in all practical matters. Thus it is in the original, contrary to some who claim that if the original were conjectural, then conjecture would weaken due to the many conjectural premises until it dissipates in the branch. The author indicated its refutation by his saying: 'And the fact that conjecture weakens due to the many premises upon which qiyas depends does not necessitate complete dissipation such that nothing remains in the branch at all.' I say: Rather, dissipation is not permissible, for the necessary (lāzim) is necessarily established when the necessary condition (malzūm) is established, and conjecture about the sought ruling is necessary for conjecture about the premises, so it does not separate from it—so understand.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the sharh (commentary) on the matn, discussing a condition of qiyas: whether the original ruling (al-asl) must be certain (qat'i) or whether conjecture (zann) suffices. The matn states that, according to the chosen school of the Hanafis, certainty is not a condition; conjecture is sufficient in all practical matters (al-'amaliyāt). The author then reports an opposing view: some scholars argue that if the asl itself is conjectural, then the many conjectural premises in qiyas will weaken the conjecture to the point of extinction in the branch. The author of the sharh refutes this by citing the original author's argument: that weakening does not entail complete dissipation. The super-commentator (likely the author of Fawātih al-Rahamūt) adds a rational proof: the necessary (lāzim) is necessarily established when its necessary condition (malzūm) is established; the conjecture about the sought ruling (al-maṭlūb) is a necessary consequence of the conjecture about the premises, so it cannot separate from it. This firmly supports the chosen Hanafi position that zann in the asl does not invalidate qiyas.

Key Terms
قطعية الأصل (qat'iyyat al-asl): The condition that the original ruling in qiyas be certain (qat'i).
الظن (al-zann): Conjecture or preponderant belief, sufficient for practical legal reasoning.
الاضمحلال (al-idmiḥlāl): Complete dissipation of conjecture, argued by opponents to occur in qiyas with multiple zanni premises.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, the original must be certain.
B) No, conjecture suffices in practical matters.
C) Only in matters of belief (`aqida).
D) Only if the far' is also certain.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school does not require certainty in the original for qiyas; conjecture suffices, and the conjecture about the branch is a necessary consequence that cannot dissipate.

Equality of 'Illa and Hukm in Qiyas: Identity or Genus
Condition that 'illa and hukm equal either identically or by genus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between equality of the cause ('illa) by identity ('ayn) and by genus (jins), and evaluate whether a given qiyas satisfies this Hanafi condition.

Core Idea
In Hanafi qiyas, the cause can be shared identically or by genus; each allows valid analogy.

This passage explains a key condition for qiyas: the 'illa (cause) and hukm (ruling) in the branch must equal those in the original. The Hanafi school permits equality either as an identical specific cause ('ayn) or as a generic cause (jins). Through examples, the author shows how generic causes accommodate diversity of rulings across different loci.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of equality
The text explains that the 'illa in the branch can equal the original's 'illa either in identity (ʿayn) or in genus (jins).
2
Examine the example of ʿayn
Wine and nabīdh share the exact same cause: intoxication and pleasure, even if intensity differs.
Equality is in the essence, not quantity.
3
Examine the example of jins
Injury is a genus cause common to soul and limbs; retaliation diversifies accordingly.
The cause is general, ruling specifics depend on locus.
4
Understand the diversification (tanawwu')
When the cause is a genus, it yields a general ruling that takes different forms in different loci, e.g., death for soul, amputation for limb.
5
Confirm the same logic applies to the ruling
The ruling too can be identical or generic, e.g., guardianship is a genus with subcategories.
The condition of equality applies to both cause and ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها أي من الشروط للفرع كما في الأحكام أن تساوي علته علة الأصل أي تكون العلة علة الأصل فيما يقصد فيه المساواة من عين من العلة كالنبيذ للخمر يتساويان في الشدة المطربة وهي بعينها مشتركة فيهما ولو اختلفا قوة وضعفاً إذ لم يقصد المساواة في القدر أو جنس من العلة كالأطراف الفرع للنفس في حق القصاص بالجناية المشتركة بينهما والجناية جنس وكذلك يجب المساواة في الحكم من عين كالقتل بالمثقل يقاس عليه أي على القتل بالمحدد في القصاص بجامع القتل العمد العدوان عندهما، فعين الحكم تعدى إلى الفرع، وهو قصاص النفس وكالولاية على الصغيرة في إنكاحها يقاس على ولاية مالها بجامع الصغر، فقد تعدى نفس الولاية في الفرع وهو جنس تحته ولاية المال وولاية النفس أقول: معنى كون العلة جنساً أنها بعمومها تقتضي حكماً أعم مما في الفرع والأصل فإذا تنوعت بتنوع المحل اقتضت في كل محل نوعاً من الحكم مناسباً إياه كالجناية فإنها بعمومها تقتضي المساواة، وهي في النفس قتل وفي الطرف قطع فقد تنوعت في كل منهما واقتضت نوعاً مناسباً من الحكم وفي العينية لما تقتضي حكماً لا اختلاف فيه إلا بالعدد باعتبار المحل فقط لا غير، ولا يمكن تنوعها ولا تنوع الحكم فاندفع ما في التحرير أن العلة في القياس لا تكون إلا عين ما علل به حكم الأصل فلا تكون المساواة إلا في عين العلة ولو كان ما في الفرع جنساً لما علل به الأصل لكان جزءاً للعلة فلا تكون العلة موجودة في الفرع وجه الاندفاع ظاهر وكذلك الكلام في الحكم سؤالاً وجواباً فالسؤال أن الموجود في الفرع عين حكم الأصل ولو كان جنساً كان جزء الحكم والجواب معنى كون الحكم جنساً أنه أمر يتنوع حسب تكثر المحل
And among them (i.e., the conditions) for the branch—as in the rulings—is that its cause ('illa) equals the cause of the original, i.e., the cause of the original (in what is intended for equality) from an identical cause (ʿayn), like wine and nabīdh: they are equal in intoxication and pleasure, and it is the very same [cause] common in both, even if they differ in strength and weakness, for equality in quantity is not intended; or a genus of the cause like the limbs: the branch [limb] is [measured] against the soul in the right of retaliation for injury common between them, and injury is a genus. Similarly, equality in the ruling is necessary: from an identical [ruling] like killing with a heavy object, it is measured upon it (i.e., upon killing with a sharp instrument) in retribution, by the common factor of intentional transgressive killing according to them, so the identical ruling is transmitted to the branch—that is retaliation of the soul; and like guardianship over a minor girl in marrying her, it is measured upon guardianship of her property by the common factor of minority, so the very guardianship has been transmitted to the branch, and it is a genus under which are guardianship of property and guardianship of the self. I say: The meaning of the cause being a genus is that it, by its generality, necessitates a ruling more general than that in the branch and original; so when it is diversified by the diversification of the locus, it necessitates in each locus a type of ruling appropriate to it—like injury, for by its generality it necessitates equality; and it is in the soul killing, and in the limb amputation—so it has diversified in each of them and necessitated an appropriate type of ruling. But in the identical cause, it necessitates a ruling with no difference except in number by consideration of the locus only, and no diversification of it or of the ruling is possible. Thus the objection in al-Tahrīr is repelled: that the cause in qiyas can only be the very same as what the original ruling was based on, so equality can only be in the identical cause; if what is in the branch is a genus of what the original was based on, it would be part of the cause, so the cause would not exist in the branch. The repulsion is obvious. Similarly the discussion applies to the ruling in question and answer: the question is that what exists in the branch is the identical ruling of the original; if it were a genus, it would be part of the ruling. The answer: the meaning of the ruling being a genus is that it is a matter that varies according to the multiplicity of loci.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the condition that the 'illa (cause) in the branch (far') must equal the 'illa in the original (asl) in qiyas. The author explains that this equality can be of two types: either identical (ʿayn) like the intoxicating effect in wine and nabīdh, even if different in intensity, or generic (jins) like 'injury' which is common to the soul (for retaliation) and limbs (for amputation). Similarly, the ruling must be equal: either identical (e.g., retaliation for killing with a heavy object is the same as for a sharp instrument) or generic (e.g., guardianship over a minor in marriage is a type of guardianship, encompassing financial and personal guardianship). The commentator then clarifies that when the cause is a genus, it entails a general ruling that diversifies according to the locus: injury demands equality, which in the soul is death, in the limb is amputation. In contrast, an identical cause produces a uniform ruling varying only in quantity. This refutes an objection from al-Tahrīr that would require the 'illa to be identical. The same reasoning applies to the ruling: if the ruling in the branch appears to be a genus, it is actually a matter that takes different forms in different loci. Thus the Hanafi position that equality can be in genus is defended.

Key Terms
عين العلة (ʿayn al-'illa): The identical specific cause, shared exactly between asl and far'.
جنس العلة (jins al-'illa): A genus cause that generalizes over multiple specific causes.
التنوع (al-tanawwu'): Diversification of the ruling according to locus when the cause is a genus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi qiyas, how must the 'illa in the branch relate to the 'illa in the original?
A) It must be exactly identical (ʿayn).
B) It must be either identical or of the same genus (jins).
C) It must be of a higher category.
D) It must be broader in scope.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates qiyas when the 'illa and hukm are equal either in identity (ʿayn) or in genus (jins), allowing flexibility through diversification.

Condition of the Original: Limited Number in Qiyas
Dispute over whether the original must be from a limited number in qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position regarding the condition of the original in qiyas being limited to a number, and apply the Hanafi rebuttal to objections based on the concept of number.

Core Idea
The original in qiyas need not be from a limited number; the count is virtually preserved.

In this passage, we confront a key dispute in usul al-fiqh: does the original case (asl) in qiyas have to be a ruling that is tied to a specific, limited number? The Hanafi school takes a permissive stance, while the author of al-Hidayah disagrees. By analyzing the arguments and counterarguments, you will understand how the Hanafi school defends the validity of qiyas even when the text mentions a specific count. This lesson sharpens your ability to evaluate objections and appreciate the flexibility of Hanafi method.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core condition under dispute
Determine what exactly is being contested: is it a condition that the original (al-asl) be a ruling related to a limited number (al-‘adad al-mahsur)? Read the passage to see both sides.
The dispute is introduced with 'ولا عدم الحصر بالعدد' meaning 'and not lack of limitation to a number is a condition'.
2
State the Hanafi position and its evidence
According to the chosen school (المذهب المختار), it is not a condition. The evidence is the hadith 'Five are killed...' and the principle that 'the measured is the measure in ruling, so the number is as if preserved.' Identify the hadith and the reasoning.
The hadith mentions five animals; Hanafis extend the ruling to similar animals via qiyas without breaking the count.
3
Analyze the opposing view from al-Hidayah
The author of al-Hidayah (صاحب الهداية) stipulates that the original must be from a limited number. His justification: extending the ruling by qiyas to unspecified cases invalidates the mentioned number. Why does he think that?
His concern is that adding cases beyond the stated number contradicts the numerical specification.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi rebuttal and the concept of number
The author rebuts by saying the number is preserved 'as if' (كأنه محفوظ) because the branch is identical in ruling. Then an objection is raised: adding a case makes it a sixth, breaking the count. The response hinges on the concept of number (مفهوم العدد): does mentioning a number negate what is above it? Hanafis say no—the number may be for specifying examples, not for numerical exclusivity. Understand this critical nuance.
This shows that the Hanafi school does not treat a limited number as a barrier to qiyas; the count is not the basis of prohibition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هي في الأصل خلافاً للبعض زعماً منهم بأن الأصل لو كان مظنوناً فيضعف الظن بكثرة المقدّمات المظنونة حتى يضمحل في الفرع ، وأشار المصنف إلى دفعه بقوله (وكون الظن يضعف بكثرة المقدمات التي يتوقف عليها القياس (لا يستلزم الاضمحلال بالكلية حتى لا يبقى في الفرع أصلاً (أقول : بل لا يجوز الاضمحلال فإن اللازم واجب الثبوت عند ثبوت الملزوم والظن بالمطلوب لازم للظن بالمقدّمات فلا ينفك عنه فتدبر، ولا عدم الحصر بالعدد) أي ليس من شروط الأصل عدم كونه حكماً متعلقاً بعدد محصور (على) المذهب (المختار كقوله) صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم: خمس يقتلن في الحل والحرم وميل صاحب «الهداية» إلى الاشتراط، ووجهه أن تعدي الحكم بالقياس إلى غير المنصوص يبطل العدد المذكور والتعليل بوجه يستلزم بطلان ما علل به باطل واستدل المصنف على ما اختاره بوجه لو تم اندفع هذا الوجه أيضاً، وقال لأن المقيس هو المقيس عليه حكماً، فالعدد كأنه محفوظ) فلا إبطال فيه (فافهم) ولعلك تقول : إن المسكوت غير المذكور البتة، وإذا أخذ مع المذكور وقع سادساً فقد بطل العدد قطعاً، وكونه هو المقيس عليه حكماً إنما يوجب ثبوت حكمه إياه ولا يلزم منه أن تبقى الخمسة خمسة بعد زيادته وكيف يقول به عاقل، فالأولى أن يبني على مفهوم العدد، فمن قال ذكر العدد للنفي عما فوقه منع ومن لا فلا بل يقول : ذكر العدد قد يكون لتعيين المقيس عليه حتى يلحق بحكم كل واحد منها ما يناسبه فافهم
This is in the original, contrary to some who claim that if the original is conjectural, conjecture weakens with many conjectural premises until it disappears in the branch. The author indicated its refutation by his statement: 'The fact that conjecture weakens due to the many premises on which qiyas depends does not necessitate complete disappearance so that nothing remains in the branch.' I say: Rather, disappearance is not permissible, for the necessary is necessarily established when the necessitator is established, and conjecture about the desired is necessary for conjecture about the premises, so it is not separated from it. So reflect. 'And not lack of limitation to a number' means that it is not a condition of the original that it be a ruling related to a limited number, according to the chosen school, like his statement (peace be upon him and his family and companions): 'Five are killed in the state of Ihram and the Sacred Precinct.' The author of al-Hidayah inclined to stipulating it. Its justification is that extending the ruling by qiyas to what is not stated invalidates the mentioned number, and reasoning in a way that necessitates the invalidation of what is reasoned with it is invalid. The author argued for his choice with a proof that, if sound, also refutes this justification, and he said: 'Because the measured is the measure in terms of ruling, so the number is as if preserved'—so there is no invalidation in it. 'So understand.' Perhaps you say: The omitted is absolutely not mentioned, and if taken with the mentioned, it becomes a sixth, so the number is definitely invalidated. That it is the measure in terms of ruling only necessitates the establishment of its ruling for it, and it does not require that the five remain five after its addition; how can a rational person say that? So it is better to build upon the concept of number. One who says that mentioning the number is for negation of what is above it prohibits, while one who does not say that says: Mentioning the number may be for specifying the measured so that what is appropriate to each of them is attached to its ruling. So understand.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage is a dispute (ikhtilaf) regarding a condition of the original (asl) in qiyas: whether the original must be a ruling related to a limited number. The author refutes the claim that conjecture weakens with multiple premises, affirming that the conclusion is inseparable from the premises. The chosen Hanafi position is that the original need not be limited to a specific count; the hadith about five creatures killed in Ihram and the Haram shows that qiyas can extend to other animals without breaking the count, because the measured (branch) is considered identical to the measure (original) in ruling, preserving the number virtually. The author of al-Hidayah disagrees, arguing that extending the ruling beyond the enumerated cases nullifies the count. The author counters that the number is preserved 'as if' intact. Then a hypothetical objection is raised: adding an unmentioned case makes it a sixth, breaking the count explicitly. The author responds that the count is not for numerical exclusivity but for specifying the measured items, so each similar case can be attached to its appropriate ruling. The dispute hinges on the concept of number (مفهوم العدد): does it negate what is above it? Hanafis do not hold that; thus, qiyas is valid even when the original is from a limited number.

Key Terms
العدد المحصور (al-‘adad al-mahsur): A number that is limited and specified in the text.
المقيس عليه (al-maqīs ‘alayh): The original case (asl) upon which qiyas is based.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi text, is it a condition for the original in qiyas that its ruling be related to a limited number?
A) Yes, it is a necessary condition.
B) No, it is not a condition.
C) Yes, according to al-Hidayah only.
D) Only if the ruling is wajib.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school does not require that the original in qiyas be from a limited number; the count is preserved virtually.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
12 min
Conditions of the Branch: Illa, Hukm, and No Change
Explaining conditions for the branch in qiyas: illa and hukm equality, and no change in hukm nature

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the three Hanafi conditions for the branch in qiyas and evaluate whether a given analogy violates them by identifying changes in illa equality or hukm nature.

Core Idea
For qiyas to be valid, the branch must share the exact illa and hukm nature — any change invalidates it.

In Hanafi usul, qiyas is not a free extension of rulings; it is tightly constrained by the structural integrity of the original ruling. The branch (far‘) must meet specific conditions: its illa must equal the original's illa, its hukm must equal the original's hukm, and the hukm's essential nature must not change. This lesson unpacks these conditions through classical examples and the Hanafi critique of Shafi‘i analogies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three conditions of the branch
The passage lists: (1) equality of illa (essence or genus), (2) equality of hukm (essence or genus), and (3) no change in the nature of the hukm.
These conditions ensure the structural integrity of qiyas.
2
Distinguish 'ayn and jins for illa
The illa can be identical in essence (e.g., intoxicating potency for wine and nabidh) or only share a genus (e.g., jinaya for murder and amputation). Understanding this flexibility prevents over-restrictive readings.
Genus-based illa still suffices because it necessitates a ruling appropriate to each locus.
3
Apply the conditions to the examples
For nabidh/wine, the illa (intoxicating potency) is identical in essence; for limbs/self, the illa (jinaya) is a genus. Verify that the hukm also transfers correctly (retaliation for both).
Equality in hukm can also be in essence or genus.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i analogies using the no-change condition
The Shafi'i qiyas of dhimmi's zihar to Muslim's zihar fails because the original's prohibition is terminable by kaffarah, but in the branch it becomes permanent (dhimmi cannot perform kaffarah). Similarly, spot salam lacks the substitute (term) that justified the original's permissibility.
Changing the nature of the hukm invalidates qiyas even if the illa is common.
5
Note the Hanafi response to objections
The passage refutes objections against Hanafi positions (e.g., paying value in zakat, pure liquids for purification) by showing they preserve the hukm's nature, unlike the criticized analogies.
This reinforces the centrality of hukm integrity.

بالكفارة) بالنص (وهي في الفرع مؤبدة) غير متناهية بالكفارة (بخلاف العبد فإنه أهل لها لكنه عاجز كالفقير) وتحقيقه أن الكفارة عبادة ساترة للذنب والكافر ليس أهلا لها أي لأدائها، لأنه إما أن يؤدي حال الكفر غير. والجواب : «إنه روي في السنن الأربعة عن ابن عباس أن رجلاً ظاهر من امرأته ثم وقع عليها قبل أن يكفر فقال : عليه السلام ما حملك على هذا؟ قال رأيت خلخالها في ضوء القمر فقال: «فاعتزلها حتى تكفر» وفيه تنصيص على الحرمة إلى التكفير ، وقوله تعالى: وَالَّذِينَ يُظْهِرُونَ مِن نِّسَآبِهِمْ ثُمَّ يَعُودُونَ لِمَا قَالُوا فَتَحْرِيرُ رَقَبَةٍ مِّن قَبْلِ أَن يَتَمَاسَاً ﴾ [المجادلة : ٣] يدل على أن كل من يصح ظهاره، فأثره تحرير رقبة الخ فافهم (وكقوله) أي كقول الشافعي (السلم الحال كالمؤجل) فإن كليهما لدفع الحرج فيصح مع أن الأجل المنصوص في السلم خلف عن الملك والقدرة الواجبين) في المبيع (بالنص) وهو النهي
