Classification of Appropriate Descriptions: Mu'aththir, Mula'im, Gharib, and Mursal
Definition and exemplification of the four types of appropriate descriptions in qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the four types of appropriate descriptions (mu'aththir, mula'im, gharib, mursal) and apply the Hanafi criteria for determining the strength of qiyas based on each type.

Core Idea
The strength of a qiyas depends on how directly the description is considered by text or consensus — from mu'aththir (strongest) to mursal (weakest).

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, not every suitable description can serve as the effective cause (illa) for qiyas. This passage introduces a classification system that ranks descriptions based on the degree to which they are supported by explicit text or consensus. Understanding this hierarchy is essential for correctly applying qiyas and assessing the strength of analogical arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basis of classification
The classification depends on whether the description's exact self and type are considered in the exact ruling or in the genus of the ruling.
The key is the level of consideration: exact ruling vs. genus of ruling.
2
Define mu'aththir
A description whose exact self and type are considered in the exact ruling by text or consensus. Example: intoxication in analogizing nabidh to wine, though note the Hanafi disagreement.
The passage suggests a better example is tawaf in purity of cat's leftover.
3
Define mula'im
A description whose exact self is considered in the genus of the ruling. Example: minority in guardianship of marriage, because minority is considered in the genus of guardianship (property).
This is when the exact description is not in the exact ruling but in a similar ruling genus.
4
Define gharib and mursal
Gharib: appropriate but not explicitly considered; Mursal: based on general benefit. The passage alludes to these but does not fully define them.
These are weaker types and require additional justification.
5
Apply the classification
Understand how each type affects the validity of qiyas. Mu'aththir is strongest, then mula'im, then gharib, then mursal.
In practice, a mufti prefers mu'aththir or mula'im for solid analogy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يصح التقسيم: الثالث» المناسب مؤثر وملائم وغريب ومرسل إذ (الوصف إن اعتبر عينه ونوعه في عين الحكم بنص أو إجماع كالإسكار في حمل النبيذ على الخمر) وهذا لا على رأي الشيخين فإن حرمة الخمر عندهما بعينها غير معللة بالسكر، والأولى أن يمثل بالطواف في طهارة سؤر الهرة فهو المؤثر : وإن اعتبر ثبوت الحكم معه) أي مع الوصف (في الأصل أي في أصل ما من غير اعتبار عينه في عينه فإن ثبت بنص أو إجماع اعتبار عينه) أي عين الوصف (في جنس الحكم كحمل الثيب الصغيرة في ولاية النكاح) على البكر الصغيرة (بالصغر لاعتباره في ولاية (المال التي هي نوع من مطلق الولاية ( إجماعاً) فقد اعتبر الصغر في جنس الحكم، وهو مطلق الولاية أو بالعكس) وهو أن يعتبر جنس الوصف في عين الحكم كقياس الحضر مع المطر على السفر في جواز الجمع بين المكتوبتين لعلة الحرج فإن حرج
The third division is valid: the appropriate is: effective (mu'aththir), suitable (mula'im), strange (gharib), and sent (mursal). For (the description) if its exact self and its type are considered in the exact ruling by text or consensus, like intoxication in analogizing nabidh to wine — but this is not according to the view of the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf?), for the prohibition of wine according to them is exactly not caused by intoxication. Better to exemplify with tawaf in the purity of the leftover of a cat — that is the effective (mu'aththir). And if the establishment of the ruling with it (i.e., with the description) in the origin (i.e., in some origin) without considering its exact self in the exact ruling; then if it is established by text or consensus to consider its exact self (i.e., the exact description) in the genus of the ruling, like analogizing the minor non-virgin in the guardianship of marriage to the minor virgin by virtue of minority because it is considered in the guardianship of property which is a type of absolute guardianship by consensus — then minority is considered in the genus of the ruling, which is absolute guardianship. Or the opposite, which is to consider the genus of the description in the exact ruling, like analogizing residence with rain to travel in the permissibility of combining the two obligatory prayers due to the cause of hardship (haraj) — for hardship...
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage presents a foundational classification in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: the four types of appropriate descriptions (المناسب) used as effective causes (علل) in qiyas. The classification depends on the level at which the description and its type are considered by text or consensus in the ruling or its genus. 1) مؤثر (effective): when both the exact description and its type are considered in the exact ruling by explicit text or consensus. The example given is using intoxication ('iskar) as the cause to analogize nabidh (date-wine) to wine in prohibition. However, the author notes this example is disputed by the 'two shaykhs' (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) who do not consider the prohibition of wine as being caused by intoxication (they base it on the substance itself). So a better example is the tawaf (circumambulation) as a cause for the purity of the leftover water of a cat (sawr al-hirra). 2) ملائم (suitable): when the exact description is considered in the genus of the ruling by text or consensus, not in the exact ruling. Example: using minority (sughr) as the description to give guardianship over a minor non-virgin in marriage, because minority is already considered in the guardianship of property (which is a genus of guardianship). 3) غريب (strange): (not explicitly defined here, but in full texts it means the description is not explicitly considered by text or consensus but is still suitable). 4) مرسل (sent/mursal): (defined as a description whose appropriateness is not supported by specific textual evidence but is based on general maslaha). The passage ends while giving an example for the opposite case (considering genus of description in exact ruling) with analogy of combining prayers in rain due to hardship. These categories are crucial for determining the validity of qiyas in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
مؤثر (mu'aththir): A description whose exact self and type are considered by text or consensus in the exact ruling.
ملائم (mula'im): A description whose exact self is considered in the genus of the ruling by text or consensus.
غريب (gharib): A description that is appropriate but not explicitly considered in any ruling or its genus by text or consensus.
مرسل (mursal): A description based on general benefit (maslaha) without specific textual support.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the classification in this passage, what makes a description 'mu'aththir' (effective)?
A) It is considered in the genus of the ruling by text or consensus.
B) Its exact self and type are considered in the exact ruling by text or consensus.
C) It is based solely on general benefit without specific text.
D) It is suitable but not explicitly mentioned in any text.

Key Takeaway
The effectiveness of a description in qiyas depends on the level of textual consideration, with mu'aththir being the strongest and mursal the weakest.

Classification of Suitable Causes: Muʾaththir, Mulāʾim, and Gharīb
Classification of ʿillal based on textual or consensus support

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify an ʿilla as muʾaththir, mulāʾim, or gharīb based on its support from text/consensus and apply this classification in analyzing qiyas arguments.

Core Idea
A cause in qiyas is classified by how it is supported—muʾaththir (explicit text/consensus), mulāʾim (partial support), or gharīb (suitable but unsupported).

The Hanafi school recognizes three levels of suitability (munāsaba) for causes in qiyas. The strength of a cause depends on whether its specific or genus has been considered by explicit text (naṣṣ) or consensus (ijmāʿ). In this passage, the author defines muʾaththir, mulāʾim, and gharīb, using examples from retribution and inheritance to illustrate how differences in support affect the validity of analogy. Understanding these categories is essential for evaluating the strength of qiyas arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Read the definitions: Muʾaththir has its specific or genus considered by text/consensus. Mulāʾim has some level of consideration (genus or specific), but not necessarily by direct text. Gharīb has no textual or consensual support but is rationally suitable.
Focus on the terms 'عين' (specific) and 'جنس' (genus).
2
Analyze the muʾaththir example
The example is killing with a heavy object analogized to killing with a sharp instrument for retribution. The cause is intentional transgressive killing; its genus (aggression against the body) is considered in the genus of retribution (limbs) by consensus. Note Abu Hanifa's dissent is about the realization of intentionality, not the validity of the cause itself.
The passage rebuts al-Taftazani's claim that there is no text/consensus for this cause.
3
Distinguish mulāʾim from gharīb
The 'fār' (husband divorcing when terminally ill to disinherit wife) is an example of gharīb: the cause (act with corrupt purpose) has no text/consensus supporting its consideration, yet it is suitable (munāsib) for deterrence. A mulāʾim cause would have some but not full support.
The gharīb is accepted in Hanafi usul only if it is suitable and not contradicted by a stronger principle.
4
Apply the classification to a new scenario
Given a description of a cause (e.g., 'the cause for prohibiting wine is intoxication'), determine whether it is muʾaththir (text cites intoxication), mulāʾim (genus of intoxication considered in other rulings), or gharīb (no textual support but rational).
Check if the specific or genus of the description appears in any textual evidence or consensus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثبت اعتبار (جنسه في جنسه أي جنس الوصف في جنس الحكم كالقتل بالمثقل) يقاس (عليه) أي على القتل ( (بالمحدد في القصاص) معللاً (بالقتل العمد العدوان وجنسه الجناية على البنية) على سبيل التعدي (قد اعتبر في جنس القصاص حتى وجب قصاص الأطراف ولو بالمثل إجماعاً ( والأظهر أنه أي هذا المثال (تقديري للنص والإجماع أي لوجودهما (على) اعتبار (العين في العين) فإن قلت: لم يوجب أبو حنيفة القصاص في القتل بالمثقل فعلم أنه لم يجعل العلة نفس القتل العمد العدوان فلا اعتبار له عنده فأين الإجماع : قال : (وإنما خالف أبو حنيفة في تحقق العمدية في المثقل) نظراً إلى أن الآلة غير موضوعة للقتل، ففيه شبهة الخطأ فخلافه إنما في تحقق العلة لا في كونها علة فافهم (وقول التفتازاني : لا نص ولا إجماع على أن العلة ذلك) أي القتل عمداً عدواناً (وحده أو مع قيد كونه بالمحدد فلم يعتبر العين في العين لا نصاً ولا إجماعاً (ليس بشيء للزوم انتفاء أكثر (المؤثرات الجواز كون المحل داخلاً في العلة فافهم (فهو) أي الذي اعتبر ثبوت الحكم معه مع ثبوت اعتبار عينه أو جنسه في جنس الحكم أو جنسه في عين الحكم الملائم (وإلا أي وإن لم يثبت اعتباره لا عيناً في عين أو جنس جنس ولا جنساً في جنس أو عين بنص ولا إجماع فهو الغريب كحمل الفار) هو الزوج الذي طلق امرأته عند إياسه عن حياته على قاتل المورث في المعارضة بنقيض قصده معللاً (بكونه) أي تطليقه المفهوم من الفار (فعلاً لغرض (فاسد هو الإضرار للزوجة بحرمان الميراث، ولم يعتبر عينه ولا جنسه بنص أو إجماع لكنه مناسب له لحصول الزجر به كذا قالوا . فتدبر
It is established that considering its genus in its genus—meaning the genus of the description in the genus of the ruling, like killing with a heavy object, is analogized to killing with a sharp instrument in the case of retribution, with the cause being intentional, transgressive killing, and its genus is aggression against the body, which has been considered in the genus of retribution so that retribution for limbs is obligatory even if by the same means, by consensus. And the apparent view is that this example is a hypothetical one for the text and consensus, i.e., for their existence on considering the specific in the specific. If you say: Abu Hanifa did not make retribution obligatory in the case of killing with a heavy object, so it is known that he did not make the cause itself intentional transgressive killing; so there is no consideration of it according to him, so where is the consensus? He said: Abu Hanifa only differed regarding the realization of intentionality in a heavy object, considering that the instrument is not designed to kill, so there is an element of mistake. So his difference is only in the realization of the cause, not in it being a cause. Understand. And the statement of al-Taftazani: There is no text or consensus that the cause is that—i.e., intentional transgressive killing alone or with the restriction of being with a sharp instrument—so the specific is not considered in the specific, neither by text nor by consensus. This is nothing, because it necessitates the negation of many effective causes, and because the locus may be included in the cause. Understand. So it is that which has the ruling established with it along with the established consideration of its specific or genus in the genus of the ruling, or its genus in the specific of the ruling, and it is the suitable cause (mulāʾim). Otherwise, if its consideration is not established neither as specific in specific nor genus in genus nor genus in specific nor specific in genus, by text or consensus, then it is the strange cause (gharīb), like the case of the 'fār' (the escaping husband). He is the husband who divorced his wife when he became hopeless of his life, analogized to the killer of the testator in counteracting the opposite of his intent, with the cause being that his divorce—understood from the term 'fār'—is an act with a corrupt purpose, which is harming the wife by depriving her of inheritance. Its specific nor its genus has been considered by text or consensus, but it is suitable (mulāʾim) because deterrence is achieved by it. That is what they said. So ponder.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage defines three categories of causes (ʿillal) in qiyas based on how they are supported by text (naṣṣ) or consensus (ijmāʿ). First is the muʾaththir (effective cause) where the specific or genus of the description is clearly considered in the specific or genus of the ruling by explicit text or consensus. The example given is the analogy between killing with a heavy object (muthaqqal) and killing with a sharp instrument (muḥaddad) for retribution. The cause is intentional, transgressive killing, and its genus (aggression against the body) is considered in the genus of retribution (limbs) by consensus. However, Abu Hanifa's dissent on retribution with a heavy object is explained: he doubts the realization of intentionality because the heavy object is not typically used to kill, so the cause is not fully realized; he does not deny the principle that intentional killing is a cause. The passage refutes al-Taftazani's claim that there is no text or consensus supporting this cause. Second is the mulāʾim (suitable cause), where the consideration is established at some level (genus or specific) but not necessarily by direct text. Third is the gharīb (strange cause), where no consideration is established by text or consensus, yet it is rationally suitable (munāsib). The example is the 'fār' (the husband who divorces when terminally ill to deprive his wife of inheritance). His act is motivated by a corrupt purpose (harm), and it is suitable to deprive him of inheritance even though no specific text or consensus considers this exact cause. This demonstrates that a cause can be gharīb and still be used if it is suitable.

Key Terms
المؤثر (al-muʾaththir): A cause whose specific or genus is considered by explicit text or consensus.
الملائم (al-mulāʾim): A cause that has some level of consideration (genus or specific) by text/consensus, but not necessarily at the specific level.
الغريب (al-gharīb): A cause that is rationally suitable but has no textual or consensual support.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) A mulāʾim cause is always specific, while gharīb is generic.
C) A mulāʾim cause is rejected in Hanafi usul, while gharīb is accepted.
D) There is no difference; they are synonyms.

Key Takeaway
A cause in qiyas is classified as muʾaththir, mulāʾim, or gharīb based on whether its specific or genus is supported by text or consensus; the gharīb is accepted if suitable and not contradicted.

The Mursal Cause: Definition and Types
Definition and subdivision of mursal cause

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the mursal cause and distinguish between its two subdivisions: what is known to be nullified and what is not known to be nullified (the strange mursal).

Core Idea
A mursal cause lacks explicit support—if its nullification is known, it is rejected; if not, it becomes the disputed maslaha mursalah.

The mursal cause is a key category in qiyas. This lesson unpacks its definition and the two subdivisions outlined in the passage: causes known to be nullified by text or consensus, and causes whose nullification is unknown—the latter forming the basis for maṣāliḥ mursalah. The examples of hardship in expiation and paternity illustrate the first type; the second type leads to the famous debate between the Hanafi and Maliki schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of mursal cause
The passage states that a cause is mursal if it is not considered along with the ruling in any case, nor is it effective. It is not mentioned in the text nor established by consensus. In other words, it is a cause with no explicit or consensual support.
This is the default category for causes that fail to meet the conditions of a valid cause.
2
Distinguish the two subdivisions
The mursal cause is divided into (1) what is known to be nullified (mā ʿulima ilghāʾuhu) by definitive evidence, and (2) what is not known to be nullified. The first is unanimously rejected; the second is the strange mursal, which is the basis for maṣāliḥ mursalah.
The first subdivision is agreed upon; the second is where the schools differ.
3
Understand the example of known nullification
The text gives the example of using 'deterrent hardship' as a cause to skip freeing a slave in expiation. The Lawgiver prescribed freeing a slave; hardship is not considered because the text specifies the expiation. Similarly, paternity is based on the marriage bed, not biological fact, as per the hadith 'al-walad li-l-firāsh'.
These examples show how a cause can be known to be nullified by explicit text.
4
Recognize the strange mursal (maṣāliḥ mursalah)
If no consideration of type or genus is known, and nullification is also not known, then it is the strange mursal. This is what the Maliki school calls maṣāliḥ mursalah, which they accept as a source. The Hanafi school rejects it because there is no divine consideration (iʿtibār) from the Lawgiver.
This division sets the stage for the intra-Islamic debate on public interest.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن لم يعتبر لا مع الحكم ولو في صورة ما ولا مؤثراً فيه فهو المرسل، وينقسم إلى ما علم الغاؤه) بنص أو جماع كإيجاب الصوم على الملك دون الإعتاق في الكفارة للظهار أو اليمين أو غيرهما (تحصيلاً للمشقة الزاجرة) التي شرعت الكفارة لأجلها ليحصل الزجر وهذه الحكمة ملغاة في اعتبار الشرع بالنص والإجماع. وكذا إثبات النسب ممن خلق من مائه حقيقة، لكن يكون في فراش الغير فإنه ملغى بالنص الولد للفراش وللعاهر الحجر ولذا الحق الإمام ولد المغربية بزوجها المشرقي دون من هي تحته لعدم كونها فراشاً هو عاهر (وهو) أي ما علم الغاؤه (مردود اتفاقاً، ومن ثم أنكر على يحيى بن يحيى (تلميذ مالك) وهو الذي جمع «الموطأ» (افتاؤه بالصوم) في الكفارة لبعض ملوك الغرب معللا بالمشقة بخلاف الإمام عيسى بن أبان منا) فإنه لم ينكر عليه (حيث أفتى والي خراسان (به أي بالصوم (معللاً بفقره لتبعاته التي على ذمته، فأصل فالمال كله مشغول بها فيكون فقيراً فصار غير واجد للعبد ،وغيره، فوجب الصوم بالنص، وليس فيه اعتبار ما علم الغاؤه وإلى ما لم يعلم) عطف على قوله : إلى ما علم فإن لم يعلم فيه أحد اعتبارات الملائم من اعتبار نوعه أو جنسه في جنس الحكم، أو جنسه في عين الحكم ، لكن لم يعلم الغاؤه أيضاً فهو الغريب من المرسل، وهو المسمى بالمصالح المرسلة حجة عند مالك رحمه الله (والمختار عند الجمهور) من أهل الأصول والفقهاء (رده لنا لا دليل بدون الاعتبار من الشارع (وإن كان على سنن العقل فلا يعتبر أصلاً، وهذا لا يتأتى ممن يقول بالإحالة إذ الإخالة تفيد العلية ههنا أيضاً فافهم أصحاب المصالح المرسلة (قالوا : أولاً: لو لم تعتبر المصالح المرسلة (الخلت الوقائع من الأحكام وهو باطل، فوجب قبولها (قلنا) لنا : أن نمنع الملازمة لأن العمومات من الكتاب والسنة (والأقيسة) المأخوذة من المؤثرات والملائمات عامة ) للوقائع كلها على ما يظهر بالاستقراء وأيضاً : عدم المدرك) للحكم بخصوصه في واقعة واقعة مدرك للاباحة الشرعية لدلالة الدليل السمعي عليه كما مر في الأحكام فتذكر (و) قالوا :(ثانياً : الصحابة كانوا يقنعون برعاية المصالح) ولم ينكر عليهم فصار إجماعاً (قلنا) كونهم قانعين عليها ممنوع (بل) إنما اعتبروا من العلل ما اطلعوا على اعتبار نوعه أو جنسه في نوع الحكم أو جنسه (هذا) وعليك بالاستقراء حتى يظهر لك جلية الحال
And if it is not considered along with the ruling even in a single case, nor is it effective, then it is the mursal (unrestricted). It is divided into what is known to be nullified (malghā) by text or consensus, like imposing fasting on the master rather than freeing a slave in expiation for ẓihār or an oath or other things, to achieve a deterrent hardship. The expiation was prescribed for that purpose, but this wisdom (hikmah) is nullified in the consideration of the Lawgiver by text and consensus. Similarly, establishing lineage from someone whose fluid actually created it, but if it is in the bed of another, it is nullified by the text: 'The child belongs to the bed, and the fornicator gets the stone.' Therefore, the imam attributed the child of the Moroccan woman to her eastern husband, not to the one under her because she is not a bed; he is a fornicator. And this type (known nullification) is rejected unanimously. Hence, objection was made to Yaḥyā ibn Yaḥyā (a student of Mālik), who compiled the Muwaṭṭaʾ, for his fatwa of fasting in expiation for some king of the West, citing hardship, unlike Imam ʿĪsā ibn Abān from us, for he was not objected to when he gave a fatwa to the governor of Khurāsān with fasting, citing his poverty due to debts on his liability. Since all his wealth is occupied by debts, he is poor, so he is not possessor of a slave, etc., so fasting became obligatory by text. And in that, there is no consideration of what is known to be nullified. And that which is not known (to be nullified) is an attachment to his statement: 'to what is known.' So if none of the considerations of the suitable cause (mulāʾim) are known—neither consideration of its type or genus in the genus of the ruling, nor its genus in the specific of the ruling—but its nullification is also not known, then it is the strange type of mursal, called maṣāliḥ mursalah (unrestricted interests). It is a proof according to Mālik (may Allah have mercy on him). The chosen view according to the majority of usul scholars and jurists is its rejection, because there is no proof without consideration from the Lawgiver. Even if it is in accordance with reason, it is not considered at all. This is not from those who claim suitability (īḥāla), because suitability indicates causality here as well. So understand. The proponents of maṣāliḥ mursalah said: First, if maṣāliḥ mursalah are not considered, many events would be left without rulings, which is false. Therefore, they must be accepted. We (Hanafis) say: We deny the implication, because the general texts of the Quran and Sunnah, and the analogies based on effective (muʾaththir) and suitable (mulāʾim) causes, are general for all events, as appears by induction. Also, the lack of a specific source (madrak) for a ruling in a particular event is itself a source for permissibility (ibāḥa) according to the evidence of the textual proof, as previously mentioned in the rulings. So remember. And they said: Secondly, the Companions used to act according to interests (maṣāliḥ) and were not criticized, so it became a consensus. We say: That they acted on them is denied; rather, they considered among the causes only those whose type or genus they knew to be considered in the type or genus of the ruling. This is it, and you must through induction until the reality becomes clear.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage discusses the mursal (unrestricted) cause in qiyas. A mursal cause is one that is not explicitly mentioned in the text nor established by consensus, yet it is not known to be invalidated. It is divided into two types: (1) What is known to be nullified (malghā) by definitive evidence, such as using 'hardship' as a cause to skip freeing a slave in expiation, while the text prescribes freeing a slave; or establishing lineage based on biological fact if the child is born in a valid marriage bed. Such causes are unanimously rejected. Examples include Yaḥyā ibn Yaḥyā's fatwa to fast in expiation citing hardship, which was criticized, versus ʿĪsā ibn Abān's similar fatwa based on poverty, which was not criticized because poverty is a valid legal cause (the person is not capable of freeing a slave). (2) What is not known to be nullified, and also no consideration of its type or genus is known: this is called maṣāliḥ mursalah (unrestricted public interest). It is accepted by the Mālikī school but rejected by the majority (including Hanafis). The Hanafi response to the Mālikī arguments is given: first, the general texts and analogies cover all events, so no gap; second, if no specific text, the default is permissibility (ibāḥa). Regarding the claim of Companion practice, the Hanafis argue that the Companions only considered causes that had some textual/consensual support at a general level, not unrestricted interests.

Key Terms
المرسل (al-mursal): A cause that is not considered along with the ruling in any specific case, nor is it effective, and lacks explicit textual or consensual support.
ما علم إلغاؤه (mā ʿulima ilghāʾuhu): A mursal cause whose nullification is known by definitive evidence (text or consensus).
المصالح المرسلة (al-maṣāliḥ al-mursalah): The strange mursal cause where nullification is not known, also called unrestricted public interests.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following best describes the 'known nullification' (mā ʿulima ilghāʾuhu) type of mursal cause?
A) It is rejected unanimously because there is clear evidence that the cause is not considered.
B) It is accepted by all schools as a valid source of law.
C) It is the same as maṣāliḥ mursalah.
D) It is used by Hanafis but not by Malikis.

Key Takeaway
The mursal cause is a cause without textual support; it is either definitely nullified (unanimously rejected) or uncertain (the disputed maṣāliḥ mursalah).

The Hanafi Refutation of Maṣāliḥ Mursalah
Dispute over maṣāliḥ mursalah between Hanafis and Malikis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi arguments against maṣāliḥ mursalah and evaluate the Maliki counterarguments using the passage's reasoning.

Core Idea
No cause is valid without divine consideration; general texts cover all events, and absence of text implies permissibility.

The passage presents a spirited debate: the Maliki school argues that without maṣāliḥ mursalah, many events would be left without rulings, and the Companions practiced them. The Hanafi school responds that general texts and analogies are sufficient, and that the Companions only considered causes with some textual or consensual basis. This lesson examines the arguments and the thamarah al-khilaf in practical jurisprudence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi definition of mursal cause and its division
The passage begins by defining the mursal cause and dividing it into known nullification (rejected) and strange mursal (maṣāliḥ mursalah). The debate focuses on the strange mursal.
This sets the context: both schools agree that known nullification is invalid.
2
Understand the first Maliki argument and the Hanafi response
Malikis argue: without maṣāliḥ mursalah, many events would lack rulings, which is false. Therefore, they must be accepted. Hanafis respond: we deny the implication because general texts of Quran, Sunnah, and analogies from effective and suitable causes cover all events. Also, if no specific source exists, the default is permissibility (ibāḥa).
The Hanafi response relies on the principle of 'istiṣḥāb al-ibāḥah al-aṣliyyah' (default permissibility).
3
Understand the second Maliki argument and the Hanafi response
Malikis argue: the Companions acted according to interests and were not criticized, making it a consensus. Hanafis respond: that they acted on unrestricted interests is denied; rather, they considered only those causes whose type or genus was known to be considered from the Lawgiver.
Hanafis maintain that Companion practice is not an independent source unless it reflects a known principle.
4
Draw the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
The disagreement results in different methodologies: Hanafis do not treat maṣāliḥ mursalah as an independent source, while Malikis do. This affects rulings on new issues where no explicit text or analogy is found.
In Hanafi fiqh, a novel case is resolved by looking for suitable causes or general texts, not by appealing directly to public interest.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن لم يعتبر لا مع الحكم ولو في صورة ما ولا مؤثراً فيه فهو المرسل، وينقسم إلى ما علم الغاؤه) بنص أو جماع كإيجاب الصوم على الملك دون الإعتاق في الكفارة للظهار أو اليمين أو غيرهما (تحصيلاً للمشقة الزاجرة) التي شرعت الكفارة لأجلها ليحصل الزجر وهذه الحكمة ملغاة في اعتبار الشرع بالنص والإجماع. وكذا إثبات النسب ممن خلق من مائه حقيقة، لكن يكون في فراش الغير فإنه ملغى بالنص الولد للفراش وللعاهر الحجر ولذا الحق الإمام ولد المغربية بزوجها المشرقي دون من هي تحته لعدم كونها فراشاً هو عاهر (وهو) أي ما علم الغاؤه (مردود اتفاقاً، ومن ثم أنكر على يحيى بن يحيى (تلميذ مالك) وهو الذي جمع «الموطأ» (افتاؤه بالصوم) في الكفارة لبعض ملوك الغرب معللا بالمشقة بخلاف الإمام عيسى بن أبان منا) فإنه لم ينكر عليه (حيث أفتى والي خراسان (به أي بالصوم (معللاً بفقره لتبعاته التي على ذمته، فأصل فالمال كله مشغول بها فيكون فقيراً فصار غير واجد للعبد ،وغيره، فوجب الصوم بالنص، وليس فيه اعتبار ما علم الغاؤه وإلى ما لم يعلم) عطف على قوله : إلى ما علم فإن لم يعلم فيه أحد اعتبارات الملائم من اعتبار نوعه أو جنسه في جنس الحكم، أو جنسه في عين الحكم ، لكن لم يعلم الغاؤه أيضاً فهو الغريب من المرسل، وهو المسمى بالمصالح المرسلة حجة عند مالك رحمه الله (والمختار عند الجمهور) من أهل الأصول والفقهاء (رده لنا لا دليل بدون الاعتبار من الشارع (وإن كان على سنن العقل فلا يعتبر أصلاً، وهذا لا يتأتى ممن يقول بالإحالة إذ الإخالة تفيد العلية ههنا أيضاً فافهم أصحاب المصالح المرسلة (قالوا : أولاً: لو لم تعتبر المصالح المرسلة (الخلت الوقائع من الأحكام وهو باطل، فوجب قبولها (قلنا) لنا : أن نمنع الملازمة لأن العمومات من الكتاب والسنة (والأقيسة) المأخوذة من المؤثرات والملائمات عامة ) للوقائع كلها على ما يظهر بالاستقراء وأيضاً : عدم المدرك) للحكم بخصوصه في واقعة واقعة مدرك للاباحة الشرعية لدلالة الدليل السمعي عليه كما مر في الأحكام فتذكر (و) قالوا :(ثانياً : الصحابة كانوا يقنعون برعاية المصالح) ولم ينكر عليهم فصار إجماعاً (قلنا) كونهم قانعين عليها ممنوع (بل) إنما اعتبروا من العلل ما اطلعوا على اعتبار نوعه أو جنسه في نوع الحكم أو جنسه (هذا) وعليك بالاستقراء حتى يظهر لك جلية الحال
And if it is not considered along with the ruling even in a single case, nor is it effective, then it is the mursal (unrestricted). It is divided into what is known to be nullified (malghā) by text or consensus, like imposing fasting on the master rather than freeing a slave in expiation for ẓihār or an oath or other things, to achieve a deterrent hardship. The expiation was prescribed for that purpose, but this wisdom (hikmah) is nullified in the consideration of the Lawgiver by text and consensus. Similarly, establishing lineage from someone whose fluid actually created it, but if it is in the bed of another, it is nullified by the text: 'The child belongs to the bed, and the fornicator gets the stone.' Therefore, the imam attributed the child of the Moroccan woman to her eastern husband, not to the one under her because she is not a bed; he is a fornicator. And this type (known nullification) is rejected unanimously. Hence, objection was made to Yaḥyā ibn Yaḥyā (a student of Mālik), who compiled the Muwaṭṭaʾ, for his fatwa of fasting in expiation for some king of the West, citing hardship, unlike Imam ʿĪsā ibn Abān from us, for he was not objected to when he gave a fatwa to the governor of Khurāsān with fasting, citing his poverty due to debts on his liability. Since all his wealth is occupied by debts, he is poor, so he is not possessor of a slave, etc., so fasting became obligatory by text. And in that, there is no consideration of what is known to be nullified. And that which is not known (to be nullified) is an attachment to his statement: 'to what is known.' So if none of the considerations of the suitable cause (mulāʾim) are known—neither consideration of its type or genus in the genus of the ruling, nor its genus in the specific of the ruling—but its nullification is also not known, then it is the strange type of mursal, called maṣāliḥ mursalah (unrestricted interests). It is a proof according to Mālik (may Allah have mercy on him). The chosen view according to the majority of usul scholars and jurists is its rejection, because there is no proof without consideration from the Lawgiver. Even if it is in accordance with reason, it is not considered at all. This is not from those who claim suitability (īḥāla), because suitability indicates causality here as well. So understand. The proponents of maṣāliḥ mursalah said: First, if maṣāliḥ mursalah are not considered, many events would be left without rulings, which is false. Therefore, they must be accepted. We (Hanafis) say: We deny the implication, because the general texts of the Quran and Sunnah, and the analogies based on effective (muʾaththir) and suitable (mulāʾim) causes, are general for all events, as appears by induction. Also, the lack of a specific source (madrak) for a ruling in a particular event is itself a source for permissibility (ibāḥa) according to the evidence of the textual proof, as previously mentioned in the rulings. So remember. And they said: Secondly, the Companions used to act according to interests (maṣāliḥ) and were not criticized, so it became a consensus. We say: That they acted on them is denied; rather, they considered among the causes only those whose type or genus they knew to be considered in the type or genus of the ruling. This is it, and you must through induction until the reality becomes clear.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage discusses the mursal (unrestricted) cause in qiyas. A mursal cause is one that is not explicitly mentioned in the text nor established by consensus, yet it is not known to be invalidated. It is divided into two types: (1) What is known to be nullified (malghā) by definitive evidence, such as using 'hardship' as a cause to skip freeing a slave in expiation, while the text prescribes freeing a slave; or establishing lineage based on biological fact if the child is born in a valid marriage bed. Such causes are unanimously rejected. Examples include Yaḥyā ibn Yaḥyā's fatwa to fast in expiation citing hardship, which was criticized, versus ʿĪsā ibn Abān's similar fatwa based on poverty, which was not criticized because poverty is a valid legal cause (the person is not capable of freeing a slave). (2) What is not known to be nullified, and also no consideration of its type or genus is known: this is called maṣāliḥ mursalah (unrestricted public interest). It is accepted by the Mālikī school but rejected by the majority (including Hanafis). The Hanafi response to the Mālikī arguments is given: first, the general texts and analogies cover all events, so no gap; second, if no specific text, the default is permissibility (ibāḥa). Regarding the claim of Companion practice, the Hanafis argue that the Companions only considered causes that had some textual/consensual support at a general level, not unrestricted interests.

Key Terms
المصالح المرسلة (al-maṣāliḥ al-mursalah): Unrestricted public interests not directly indicated in the sources, used as a basis for rulings.
العمومات (al-ʿumūmāt): General texts of the Quran and Sunnah that are considered to cover all events by Hanafis.
الاباحة الشرعية (al-ibāḥa al-sharʿiyyah): The default ruling of permissibility in the absence of a specific legal source.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi response to the Maliki argument that without maṣāliḥ mursalah many events would be left without rulings?
A) They agree and accept maṣāliḥ mursalah.
B) They deny the implication because general texts and analogies cover all events.
C) They argue that those events are not legally relevant.
D) They say that consensus prohibits the use of maṣāliḥ.

Key Takeaway
Maṣāliḥ mursalah is rejected by Hanafis because no divine consideration is known, and the general texts suffice to cover all events.

Hanafi Definition of al-Mu'assir and Shafi'i Classification of Suitable Descriptions
Definition and classification of mu'assir in Shafi'i and Hanafi usul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi criteria for a description to be mu'assir and distinguish it from the Shafi'i classification by identifying the four types of effect (ta'thir).

Core Idea
A mu'assir must show actual effect in Shari'ah — mere suitability is insufficient for Hanafis.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut presents the Shafi'i classification of suitable descriptions into five types, then contrasts the Hanafi definition of mu'assir. The Hanafis require that the description's effect be evident in Shari'ah, not just rationally suitable. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying qiyas and istihsan in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Shafi'i five categories
Recognize the five types of suitable descriptions as listed in the passage: (1) mula'im, (2) gharib, (3) genus in genus, (4) cancellation unknown, (5) cancellation known. Understand the basis of each.
These are categories from al-Amidi, transmitted in Shafi'i usul.
2
Understand the Shafi'i mula'im and gharib with examples
Study the examples: mula'im – killing by a heavy object (specific in specific, general in general); gharib – intoxication for prohibition (specific only, no text). Note that gharib is accepted as weak by some Shafi'is but rejected by Hanafis.
3
State the Hanafi definition of mu'assir
The Hanafi mu'assir is a description that is suitable (mula'im) to intellects and whose effect appears in Shari'ah. This excludes tautological causes (al-illal al-tardiyya).
The Arabic: المؤثر عندهم الوصف المناسب الملائم للحكم عند العقول الذي ظهر تأثيره شرعا
4
Analyze the four modes of effect
The passage lists four ways a description can show effect: (a) genus affects specific ruling (e.g., inability due to unconsciousness like menstruation); (b) genus affects genus (e.g., hardship drops prayers in traveler and menstruating woman); (c) specific affects genus (e.g., brother from same parents affects guardianship); (d) specific affects specific (common in partial qiyas).
These are the 'basa'it' (simple modes) before combination.
5
Address the objection and refinement
An objection is raised: if effect requires text or ijma, then mu'assir is not separate from textual cause (mannusa). The response is that it is the same cause but considered from the aspect of suitability; thus it is dual-aspect: mannusa by its textual basis, mu'assir by its suitability.

وهذا التقسيم ما عولنا عليه مما في كتب الشافعية، وقد اختلفوا اختلافاً كثيراً) ونقل عن الآمدي الوصف المناسب إن اعتبر بنص أو اجماع، فهو المؤثر وإن اعتبر ترتب الحكم فتسعة فإنه يعتبر إما خصوصه أو عمومه، خصوصه وعمومه معاً في خصوص الحكم أو عمومه أو خصوصه وعمومه معاً، وإن لم يعتبر أصلاً، فأما أن يظهر الغاؤه أو لا يظهر، فهذه جملة الأقسام والواقع منها في الشرع خمسة لا تزيد . أحدها: ما اعتبر خصوص الوصف في خصوص الحكم وعمومه في عمومه ويسمى الملائم، كالقتل بالمثقل، فإنه قتل العمد العدوان، وهو معتبر في قصاص النفس، وعمومه مطلق الجناية اعتبر في القصاص المطلق . وثانيها ما اعتبر الخصوص في الخصوص فقط لا بنص أو إجماع، وهو المناسب الغريب، كالإسكار للتحريم إن لم يكن عليه نص أو إجماع. وثالثها ما اعتبر جنسه في جنس الحكم ولا نص ولا إجماع وهذا من جنس الملائم الغريب، وهو كجنس المشقة المشتركة بين الحائض والمسافر يوجب مطلق التخفيف المتناول لإسقاط كل الصلاة أو شطر الصلاة. ورابعها ما لم يثبت الغاؤه كالتترس المذكور. وخامسها ما ثبت الغاؤه، وهو مطالب بتصحيح الاستقراء في دعوى وقوع هذه الخمسة لا تزيد، بل ربما يشهد الاستقراء بخلافه. قال في المنهاج» المؤثر ما أثر جنسه في نوع الحكم لا غير، والملائم والغريب كما ذكره الآمدي وبعض الشافعية شرطوا شهادة الأصول أيضاً، وهو العرض على الأصول لئلا يظهر بطلانه لمعارضة نص أو إجماع أو تخلف أو اقتضاء وجوده ضده وغير ذلك، فقيل : يجب العرض على الأصول كلها، وقيل: العرض على الاثنين كاف فانظر إلى هذا الاختلاف الذي وقع بينهم (وأما الحنفية فالمؤثر عندهم الوصف المناسب الملائم) للحكم عند العقول فيه احتراز عن العلل الطردية (الذي ظهر تأثيره شرعاً بأن يكون الجنسه تأثير في عين الحكم كإسقاط الصلاة الكثيرة بالإغماء فإن لجنسه الذي هو العجز) عن الأداء من غير حرج تأثيراً في سقوطها كما في الحائض (أو) بأن يكون تأثيراً (في جنسه كإسقاطها عن الحائض) معللاً (بالمشقة، وقد أسقط مشقة السفر الركعتين) فقد أثر جنس في جنس السقوط (أو) بأن يكون (لعينه) تأثير (في جنس الحكم كالأخوة لأب وأم في قياس التقدم في ولاية النكاح وقد تقدم هذا الأخ في الميراث) فقد أثر في مطلق الولاية (أو) يكون لعينه تأثير في عينه) أي عين الحكم (وذلك كثير) في الأقيسة الجزئية المذكورة في الفقه (وأورد عليه أنه لا بد فيه أي في هذا الاعتبار والتأثير من النص أو الإجماع إذ لا اخالة عندهم، وحينئذ لا يكون المؤثر (قسيماً لهما أي للعلة التي ثبتت بالنص أو الإجماع (كما هو المشهور فإنها قسمت في المشهور إلى منصوصة ومؤثرة إلا بالاعتبار) فإنها باعتبار أنها ثبتت بالنص منصوصة وباعتبار أنها مناسبة له مع الاعتبار المذكور مؤثرة (ثم هذه الأربعة بسائط، وقد يتركب بعض من الأقسام (مع بعض وينحصر) المركب في أحد عشر) قسماً (لأن الثنائي ستة) : أحدها ما اعتبر عينه في عين الحكم وجنسه ، كالمرض اعتبر في الافطار، وفي جنسه
And this classification is what we rely upon from the books of the Shafi'is, and they differed greatly. And it is transmitted from al-Amidi: The suitable description (al-wasf al-munasib): if it is considered by text or consensus, it is the mu'assir (effective). And if the ruling is attached to it, then nine types: it is considered either by its specific or its general, its specific and general together in the specific of the ruling or its general, or its specific and general together. And if not considered at all, then either its cancellation appears or does not appear. These are the total categories, and those occurring in the Shari'ah are five, no more. First: that in which the specific of the description is considered in the specific of the ruling and its general in its general, and it is called al-mula'im (suitable), like killing by a heavy object (al-mithqal): it is intentional transgressive killing, and it is considered in the retaliation for life, and its general (absolute homicide) is considered in absolute retaliation. Second: that in which the specific is considered only in the specific, not by text or consensus, and it is the suitable gharib (strange), like intoxication for prohibition if there is no text or consensus. Third: that in which its genus is considered in the genus of the ruling, with no text or consensus, and this is of the class of the suitable gharib, like the genus of hardship shared between the menstruating woman and the traveler, which necessitates absolute alleviation encompassing either dropping all prayer or half of it. Fourth: that whose cancellation has not been established, like the tatarus mentioned. Fifth: that whose cancellation has been established. And there is a need to verify the induction in the claim that these five occur and no more; rather, induction might testify to the contrary. He said in al-Minhaj: The mu'assir is that whose genus affects the type of the ruling, no more. And the mula'im and gharib — as al-Amidi mentioned, and some Shafi'is also stipulated the testimony of the principles (al-usul), i.e., presenting to the principles to ensure it does not become invalid due to opposition of a text or consensus, or inconsistency, or its existence implying its opposite, etc. So it was said: it is obligatory to present to all principles; and it was said: presenting to two is sufficient. So look at this difference that occurred among them. As for the Hanafis, the mu'assir in their view is the suitable description (al-wasf al-mula'im) that appears sound to intellects—this excludes tautological causes (al-illal al-tardiyya)—which has become effective in Shari'ah by having its genus have an effect in the specific ruling, like the dropping of many prayers due to unconsciousness, for its genus (inability to perform without hardship) has an effect in dropping it, as in the menstruating woman. Or by having an effect in its genus, like dropping (prayers) for the menstruating woman, explained by hardship, and the hardship of travel has dropped the two rak'ahs; so a genus affected a genus of dropping. Or by having its specific have an effect in the genus of the ruling, like the brother from the same father and mother in the analogy for priority in marriage guardianship, and this brother has been given precedence in inheritance; so it has affected absolute guardianship. Or by having its specific have an effect in its specific, and that is abundant in the partial analogies mentioned in fiqh. And it was objected that there must be, in this consideration and effect, a text or consensus, since there is no suitability (ikhala) in their view; and then the mu'assir would not be a category alongside those (the cause established by text or consensus) as is well-known, for they are divided in the well-known view into mannusa (textual) and mu'assir (effective), except by consideration: for by virtue of being established by text it is mannusa, and by virtue of being suitable with the mentioned consideration it is mu'assir. Then these four are simple, and sometimes some of the categories combine, and the composite is confined to eleven types, because the binary ones are six: one of them is where its specific is considered in the specific of the ruling and its genus, like illness considered in breaking fast and in its genus...
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage presents the classification of suitable descriptions (al-awsaf al-munasiba) according to Shafi'i usul (especially al-Amidi) and then defines the Hanafi position. The Shafi'i classification yields five categories: (1) al-mula'im – specific description specific ruling, general in general; (2) al-gharib – specific only, no text; (3) genus in genus – like hardship; (4) cancellation unknown; (5) cancellation known. Then the passage contrasts the Hanafi definition: mu'assir is a suitable description that shows actual effect in Shari'ah in one of four ways: (a) genus affects specific ruling (e.g., inability due to unconsciousness like menstruation); (b) genus affects genus (hardship drops prayers in both traveler and menstruating woman); (c) specific affects genus (brother affects guardianship); (d) specific affects specific (common in partial qiyas). The passage notes an objection: that this 'effect' must be textually proven, so the mu'assir is not a separate category from the mannusa (textual cause) but rather a different aspect. Finally, it mentions composite categories from combining the four simple types, up to eleven. The Hanafi approach prioritizes textual effect over mere suitability.

Key Terms
المؤثر (al-mu'assir): A suitable description whose effect is proven by Shari'ah (by text or observed effect)
الملائم (al-mula'im): Description considered in both specific and general of ruling
الغريب (al-gharib): Suitable description with no textual support but not rejected

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in this passage, what is required for a description to be considered 'mu'assir'?
A) It must be universally accepted by all scholars.
B) It must show its effect in Shari'ah, e.g., its genus affecting a ruling.
C) It must be based solely on rational deduction without textual support.
D) It must be a 'gharib' description.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mu'assir is a suitable description whose effect is evident in Shari'ah, distinguishing it from mere rational suitability.

The Five Simple Types of Effective Attributes in Qiyas
Enumeration of five simple attribute types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the five simple categories of effective attributes in qiyas and distinguish between mulā'im, gharīb, and mulā'im gharīb based on how their specificity and generality relate to the ruling.

Core Idea
Attributes in qiyas are classified by whether their specificity and generality are considered in the ruling's specificity and generality.

The author of the commentary begins by enumerating the five types of attributes that actually occur in the Shariah as effective causes for analogical reasoning. These form the basic vocabulary of qiyas, and understanding them is the first step in mastering Hanafi usul al-fiqh. Each type reflects a different relationship between the attribute's particular aspect and its general meaning, and how each maps to the ruling's particular and general aspects.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five categories
Read the first part of the passage where the author lists the five categories: (1) mulā'im, (2) gharīb, (3) mulā'im gharīb, (4) unestablished nullification, (5) established nullification. Note the defining feature of each.
The categories are based on whether the specific or general aspect is considered, and whether there is textual support.
2
Analyze the mulā'im example
The example given for mulā'im is killing with a heavy object (qatl bi al-muthqal). The specific attribute (intentional transgressive killing) is considered in the specific ruling (retaliation for life), and its general attribute (absolute aggression) is considered in the general ruling (absolute retaliation). Understand how this dual consideration works.
Mulā'im is the strongest type because its effect is evident in both specific and general planes.
3
Analyze the gharīb example
The example is intoxication (iskār) for prohibition (tahrīm). Here only the specific attribute (intoxication) is considered in the specific ruling (prohibition), with no supporting text or consensus. Recognize that this type relies solely on appropriateness (munāsaba).
Gharīb is called 'strange' because it lacks explicit textual backing, yet Hanafis accept it.
4
Understand mulā'im gharīb
The example is the genus of hardship (jins al-mashaqqa) shared by the menstruating woman and the traveler, leading to alleviation (takhfīf) in worship. Here the genus of the attribute is considered in the genus of the ruling, again without text or consensus.
This type combines features of mulā'im (genus considered) and gharīb (no text).
5
Distinguish the remaining two types
The fourth type is where the attribute's nullification (ighā') is not established—meaning it is potentially effective but not yet proven invalid. The fifth is where nullification is established, meaning the attribute is definitely not effective. Understand that these are residual categories when induction is incomplete.
The author notes that induction may show more than five types, but he claims these are the only ones occurring.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصل الرابع/ القياس
۳۱۷
أصلاً، فأما أن يظهر الغاؤه أو لا يظهر، فهذه جملة الأقسام والواقع منها في الشرع خمسة لا تزيد .
أحدها: ما اعتبر خصوص الوصف في خصوص الحكم وعمومه في عمومه ويسمى الملائم، كالقتل بالمثقل، فإنه قتل العمد العدوان، وهو معتبر في قصاص النفس، وعمومه مطلق الجناية اعتبر في القصاص المطلق .
وثانيها ما اعتبر الخصوص في الخصوص فقط لا بنص أو إجماع، وهو المناسب الغريب، كالإسكار للتحريم إن لم يكن عليه نص أو إجماع.
وثالثها ما اعتبر جنسه في جنس الحكم ولا نص ولا إجماع وهذا من جنس الملائم الغريب، وهو كجنس المشقة المشتركة بين الحائض والمسافر يوجب مطلق التخفيف المتناول لإسقاط كل الصلاة أو شطر الصلاة.
ورابعها ما لم يثبت الغاؤه كالتترس المذكور.
وخامسها ما ثبت الغاؤه، وهو مطالب بتصحيح الاستقراء في دعوى وقوع هذه الخمسة لا تزيد، بل ربما يشهد الاستقراء بخلافه. قال في المنهاج» المؤثر ما أثر جنسه في نوع الحكم لا غير، والملائم والغريب كما ذكره الآمدي وبعض الشافعية شرطوا شهادة الأصول أيضاً، وهو العرض على الأصول لئلا يظهر بطلانه لمعارضة نص أو إجماع أو تخلف أو اقتضاء وجوده ضده وغير ذلك، فقيل : يجب العرض على الأصول كلها، وقيل: العرض على الاثنين كاف فانظر إلى هذا الاختلاف الذي وقع بينهم (وأما الحنفية فالمؤثر عندهم الوصف المناسب الملائم) للحكم عند العقول فيه احتراز عن العلل الطردية (الذي ظهر تأثيره شرعاً بأن يكون الجنسه تأثير في عين الحكم كإسقاط الصلاة الكثيرة بالإغماء فإن لجنسه الذي هو العجز) عن الأداء من غير حرج تأثيراً في سقوطها كما في الحائض (أو) بأن يكون تأثيراً (في جنسه كإسقاطها عن الحائض) معللاً (بالمشقة، وقد أسقط مشقة السفر الركعتين) فقد أثر جنس في جنس السقوط (أو) بأن يكون (لعينه) تأثير (في جنس الحكم كالأخوة لأب وأم في قياس التقدم في ولاية النكاح وقد تقدم هذا الأخ في الميراث) فقد أثر في مطلق الولاية (أو) يكون لعينه تأثير في عينه) أي عين الحكم (وذلك كثير) في الأقيسة الجزئية المذكورة في الفقه (وأورد عليه أنه لا بد فيه أي في هذا الاعتبار والتأثير من النص أو الإجماع إذ لا اخالة عندهم، وحينئذ لا يكون المؤثر (قسيماً لهما أي للعلة التي ثبتت بالنص أو الإجماع (كما هو المشهور فإنها قسمت في المشهور إلى منصوصة ومؤثرة إلا بالاعتبار) فإنها باعتبار أنها ثبتت بالنص منصوصة وباعتبار أنها مناسبة له مع الاعتبار المذكور مؤثرة (ثم هذه الأربعة بسائط، وقد يتركب بعض من الأقسام (مع بعض وينحصر) المركب في أحد عشر) قسماً (لأن الثنائي

ستة) :
أحدها ما اعتبر عينه في عين الحكم وجنسه ، كالمرض اعتبر في الافطار، وفي جنسه

۳۱۸
فواتح الرحموت شرح مسلم الثبوت الجزء الثاني
وهو التخفيف في مطلق العبادة حتى شرع الصلاة بالتيمم وقاعداً. وثانيها : ما اعتبر عينه وجنسه في جنس الحكم كالطواف أثر في طهارة الماء وجنسه، المخالطة بنجاسة يشق الاحتراز عنها أيضاً علة للطهارة كآبار الفلوات . وهو وثالثها: ما اعتبر العين في العين والجنس في الجنس، كالجنون المطبق أثر في ولاية النكاح وجنسه وهو العجز بسبب عدم العقل أثر في مطلق الولاية.
(
ورابعها ما اعتبر جنسه في النوع وجنسه في الجنس كالصغر أثر جنسه، وهو العجز بسبب ضعف العقل في ولاية المال وأيضاً العجز في مطلق الولاية لا الصغر خصوصه إذ إيجابه للولاية على النكاح مختلف فيه فلا اجماع .
وخامسها ما اعتبر جنسه في نوع الحكم ونوعه في جنسه كخروج النجاسة أعم مما من : أحد السبيلين أثر في ايجاب الوضوء ونوعه وهو خروجها من غير السبيلين في مطلق التطهير، فإن تطهير البدن بخروجها منه واجب .

وسادسها ما اعتبر نوعه في الجنس وجنسه في الجنس كسلب العقل، فإنه مؤثر في سقوط العبادة الذي هو جنس الافطار لكون النية شرطاً فيها وجنسه ، وهو العجز لخلل في إحدى القوى مؤثر في سقوط العبادة كذا قالوا : (والثلاثي أربعة) :
أحدها ما اعتبر نوعه في نوع الحكم، وجنسه في جنسه ونوعه دون نوعه في جنسه، كالحيض أثر في حرمة القربان وجنسه وهو الأذى أثر فيه وفي جنسه، وهو قضاء الشهوة في محل الأذى حتى أثر في حرمة اللواطة . وثانيها : ما اعتبر نوعه في جنسه ونوعه وجنسه في نوعه دون جنسه في جنسه كالحيض : فإنه أثر في حرمة الصلاة وفي جنسه وهو حرمة القراءة وجنسه وهو خروج النجاسة من السبيلين أثر في حرمة الصلاة أيضاً لكنه غير مؤثر في حرمة القراءة.

ورابعها: ما اعتبر نوعه في نوعه وجنسه وجنسه في جنسه، دون جنسه في نوعه، كعدم وجدان الماء إلا ما أعد للشرب، فهو عجز عن الماء، وقد أثر في إيجاب التيمم لقوله تعالى : فَلَمْ تَجِدُوا مَاءً [النساء : ٤٣]، [المائدة: ٦] والأولى أن يقال : بالإجماع وجنسه وهو العجز عن استعمال ما شرط استعماله أثر في سقوط اشتراطه وعدم وجوبه فإنه قد سقط غسل الثوب النجس عند عدم وجدان الماء بالإجماع، وكذا عدم وجدان الماء أثر فيه دفعاً للهلاك، وأما جنسه المذكور فلم يوجب التيمم بخصوصه .
ورابعها ما لم يعتبر نوعه في نوعه، لكن اعتبر في جنسه وجنسه اعتبر في نوعه وجنسه، كخوف فوت صلاة العيد لم يؤثر في إباحة التيمم لا بالنص ولا بالإجماع، لكن جنسه وهو العجز عما شرط استعماله للصلاة أثر في إيجاب التيمم وفي جنسه، وهو سقوط ما شرط استعماله فيه، والنوع وهو العجز عن الماء قد أثر في هذا الجنس أيضاً، كذا قالوا، وفي هذا
The Fourth Principle / Qiyas. 317. [Explanation:] So either its nullification appears or does not appear. These are the sum of the categories, and what actually occurs in the Sharī‘ah is five, no more. First: that in which the specificity of the attribute is considered in the specificity of the ruling, and its generality in its generality, and it is called al-mulā’im (suitable), like killing with a heavy object, for it is intentional transgressive killing, and it is considered in retaliation for life, and its generality, absolute aggression, is considered in absolute retaliation. Second: that in which specificity is considered in specificity only, without a text or consensus, and it is the gharīb (strange) appropriate, like intoxication for prohibition if there is no text or consensus on it. Third: that in which its genus is considered in the genus of the ruling, and there is no text or consensus, and this is of the kind of mulā’im gharīb, like the genus of hardship shared between the menstruating woman and the traveler, necessitating absolute alleviation covering dropping all of the prayer or half of the prayer. Fourth: that whose nullification has not been established, like the mentioned tatarruṣ (using human shields). Fifth: that whose nullification has been established, and he [the author] is required to correct the induction in the claim that these five occur and no more; rather induction may witness the contrary. He said in al-Minhāj: 'Al-mu’aththir (effective attribute) is that whose genus affects the type of the ruling, nothing else, and al-mulā’im and al-gharīb.' As al-Āmidī mentioned, and some Shāfi‘īs also stipulated the testimony of the principles (al-uṣūl), which is presenting to the principles to avoid its invalidity becoming apparent due to opposition of text or consensus or lag or requiring its opposite, etc. So it was said: presenting to all principles is obligatory, and it was said: presenting to two is sufficient. So look at this disagreement that occurred among them. (As for the Ḥanafīs, al-mu’aththir according to them is the attribute that is appropriate (al-munāsib al-mulā’im) for the ruling in the intellects, thereby guarding against merely formal (ṭardiyya) causes, which has its effect manifested in the Sharī‘ah, either by its genus having an effect in the specific ruling, like dropping many prayers due to unconsciousness, for its genus which is incapability of performance without difficulty has an effect in dropping it as in the menstruating woman; or by having an effect in its genus, like dropping it for the menstruating woman justified by hardship, and hardship of travel has dropped two rak‘ahs, so a genus has effected a genus of dropping; or by its specific essence having an effect in the genus of the ruling, like the brother by both parents in analogy for precedence in the guardianship of marriage, and this brother has preceded in inheritance, so it has effected in absolute guardianship; or its specific essence having an effect in its specific essence, i.e., the specific ruling, and that is abundant in the partial analogies mentioned in fiqh. (It was objected that in this consideration and effect, text or consensus is necessary, since they have no free consideration, and then al-mu’aththir would not be a counterpart to them, i.e., to the cause established by text or consensus, as is well-known, for they are divided in the well-known view into manṣūṣa (text-based) and mu’aththira (effective), except by consideration: for it is manṣūṣa by virtue of being established by text, and mu’aththira by virtue of being appropriate to it with the mentioned consideration. (Then these four are simple, and some of the categories may combine with others, and the composite is limited to eleven) categories (because the binary is six): First: that in which its specific essence is considered in the specific ruling and its genus, like illness is considered in breaking the fast, and in its genus, which is alleviation in absolute worship, so much so that prayer is prescribed with tayammum and sitting. Second: that in which its specific essence and its genus are considered in the genus of the ruling, like ṭawāf (circumambulation) affected purity of water and its genus, mixing with impurity that is hard to avoid is also a cause for purity, like wells in deserts. Third: that in which the specific essence is considered in the specific ruling and the genus in the genus, like continuous insanity affected guardianship of marriage and its genus, which is incapability due to lack of intellect, affected absolute guardianship. Fourth: that in which its genus is considered in the type and its genus in the genus, like minority, its genus, which is incapability due to weak intellect, affected guardianship of property, and also incapability in absolute guardianship, not minority specifically, since its requiring guardianship over marriage is disputed, hence no consensus. Fifth: that in which its genus is considered in the type of the ruling and its type in its genus, like the exit of impurity, more general than what comes from the two passages, affected the obligation of wuḍū’, and its type, which is its exit from other than the two passages, in absolute purification, for purifying the body by its exit is obligatory. Sixth: that in which its type is considered in the genus and its genus in the genus, like deprivation of intellect, for it is effective in dropping worship, which is the genus of breaking the fast, because intention is a condition in it, and its genus, which is incapability due to a defect in one of the faculties, is effective in dropping worship, thus they said. (And the ternary is four): First: that in which its type is considered in the type of the ruling, and its genus in its genus and its type without its type in its genus, like menstruation affected the prohibition of approach, and its genus, which is harm, affected it and in its genus, which is the satisfaction of desire in the place of harm, so much so that it affected the prohibition of sodomy. Second: that in which its type is considered in its genus and its type and its genus in its type, without its genus in its genus, like menstruation: for it affected the prohibition of prayer and in its genus, which is the prohibition of recitation, and its genus, which is the exit of impurity from the two passages, affected the prohibition of prayer also but it does not affect the prohibition of recitation. Third: that in which its type is considered in its type and its genus and its genus in its genus, without its genus in its type, like the non-finding of water except what is prepared for drinking, so it is incapability of water, and it affected the obligation of tayammum due to His statement: 'and you do not find water' [al-Nisā’: 43, al-Mā’idah: 6], and it is better to say: by consensus, and its genus, which is incapability of using what is prescribed to use, affected the dropping of its prescription and its non-obligation, for indeed washing a najis garment when water is not found is dropped by consensus, and likewise non-finding of water affected it to repel destruction. But the mentioned genus did not necessitate tayammum specifically. Fourth: that in which its type is not considered in its type, but it is considered in its genus and its genus is considered in its type and its genus, like fear of missing the Eid prayer does not affect the permissibility of tayammum neither by text nor consensus, but its genus, which is incapability of what is prescribed to use for prayer, affected the obligation of tayammum and in its genus, which is dropping what is prescribed to use in it, and the type, which is incapability of water, has affected this genus also, thus they said. Commentary
This passage is a detailed classification of the types of effective attributes (al-mu’aththir) in qiyas, according to the Hanafi school. The author begins by stating that the attributes that can be considered in analogy are five in number, no more, as found in the Shariah. He lists them: (1) mulā’im, where the specific attribute and its general meaning are both considered in the specific ruling and its general application; (2) gharīb, where only the specific attribute is considered without textual support; (3) a type that is like mulā’im gharīb, where the genus is considered in the genus of the ruling; (4) where nullification is not established; and (5) where nullification is established. Then he discusses the criterion for an attribute to be effective (mu’aththir), quoting al-Minhāj and mentioning that some Shāfi‘īs require the testimony of fundamental principles to avoid conflict with texts or consensus. The Hanafi view, however, is that al-mu’aththir is the attribute that is appropriate (munāsib mulā’im) for the ruling according to rational consideration, as opposed to purely formal (ṭardiyya) causes, and whose effect has been manifested in the Shariah—either its genus affects a specific ruling (e.g., inability causing dropping of many prayers), or its genus affects a genus (e.g., hardship dropping parts of worship), or its specific essence affects a genus (e.g., full brother affecting guardianship), or its specific essence affects a specific ruling (common in partial analogies). The author notes an objection that such an attribute must be supported by text or consensus, but he resolves this by saying that the same attribute can be considered both manṣūṣa (text-based) and mu’aththira (effective) from different perspectives. Then the passage moves to the combinatorial classifications: simple attributes are four, and composite ones arise from combining these, yielding eleven types: six binary combinations (where two aspects are considered) and four ternary combinations (where three aspects are considered). For each type, the author provides concrete examples from fiqh, such as illness, circumambulation, insanity, minority, impurity, deprivation of intellect, menstruation, and lack of water. These examples illustrate how the attribute's specific aspect and its genus are considered in the specific ruling and its genus. The explanation follows the classification order, and the teacher should note that the Hanafi emphasis on appropriateness and actual Shariah evidence distinguishes their approach from those who require only formal suitability.

Key Terms
الملائم (al-mulā’im): An attribute whose specific aspect is considered in the specific ruling and whose general aspect is considered in the general ruling.
الغريب (al-gharīb): An attribute considered only in its specific aspect without a supporting text or consensus.
الملائم الغريب (al-mulā’im al-gharīb): An attribute whose genus is considered in the genus of the ruling, but without a text or consensus; combines features of mulā’im and gharīb.
الغاء (al-ighā’): Nullification of an attribute's effect in Shariah; if established, the attribute is not effective.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT one of the five simple types of effective attributes?
A) mulā'im
B) gharīb
C) manṣūṣ (text-based)
D) mulā'im gharīb

Key Takeaway
The five simple types of effective attributes in qiyas are mulā'im, gharīb, mulā'im gharīb, unestablished nullification, and established nullification.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
10 min
The Hanafi Definition of Mu'aththir and the Four Modes of Effect
Definition and exposition of mu'aththir with four modes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of mu'aththir (effective attribute) and identify the four modes in which its effect is manifested in Shariah, using examples from the passage.

Core Idea
Mu'aththir is the appropriate attribute whose effect is evident in Shariah through four modes: genus on specific ruling, genus on genus, specific on genus, and specific on specific ruling.

After listing the five simple types, the passage delves into the key Hanafi definition of what makes an attribute 'effective' (mu'aththir). Unlike the opposing school that requires explicit testimony of principles, Hanafis define mu'aththir as an attribute that is both appropriate (munāsib) and has its effect manifested in the Shariah. This manifests through four distinct modes, each illustrated with concrete fiqh examples. Understanding these modes is crucial for constructing valid analogies.

Guided Path
1
Locate the Hanafi definition
Find the sentence beginning 'وأما الحنفية فالمؤثر عندهم...'. This is the author's statement of the Hanafi position. Note the key components: (1) the attribute must be appropriate (munāsib mulā'im) (2) its effect must be manifested in Shariah (zahara atharuhu shar'an).
The definition excludes purely formal (ṭardiyya) causes that have no rational connection.
2
Understand the first mode
The first mode: the genus of the attribute has an effect on the specific ruling. Example: incapability (al-'ajz) is the genus, and it causes dropping of many prayers due to unconsciousness. The genus (incapability) is seen in the menstruating woman also dropping prayer.
Here the genus (jins) of the attribute affects a particular ruling (ayn al-hukm).
3
Understand the second mode
The second mode: the genus of the attribute has an effect on the genus of the ruling. Example: hardship (mashaqqa) causes dropping of prayer for the menstruating woman (genus of ruling: dropping worship), and hardship of travel also causes dropping of two rak'at. So a genus (hardship) affects a genus (dropping).
This is a broader effect than the first mode.
4
Understand the third mode
The third mode: the specific essence of the attribute has an effect on the genus of the ruling. Example: brother by both parents (al-akh li ab wa umm) is the specific attribute, affecting absolute guardianship (jins al-hukm: general authority). The same brother also has precedence in inheritance, indicating effect on absolute guardianship.
'Ayn al-wasf (specific essence) affects jins al-hukm.
5
Understand the fourth mode
The fourth mode: the specific essence affects the specific ruling. This is very common in partial analogies in fiqh. The passage says 'that is abundant' (wa dhalika kathīr).
This is the most straightforward mode: a specific attribute directly causes a specific ruling.
