الأصل الرابع/ القياس
۳۱۷
أصلاً، فأما أن يظهر الغاؤه أو لا يظهر، فهذه جملة الأقسام والواقع منها في الشرع خمسة لا تزيد .
أحدها: ما اعتبر خصوص الوصف في خصوص الحكم وعمومه في عمومه ويسمى الملائم، كالقتل بالمثقل، فإنه قتل العمد العدوان، وهو معتبر في قصاص النفس، وعمومه مطلق الجناية اعتبر في القصاص المطلق .
وثانيها ما اعتبر الخصوص في الخصوص فقط لا بنص أو إجماع، وهو المناسب الغريب، كالإسكار للتحريم إن لم يكن عليه نص أو إجماع.
وثالثها ما اعتبر جنسه في جنس الحكم ولا نص ولا إجماع وهذا من جنس الملائم الغريب، وهو كجنس المشقة المشتركة بين الحائض والمسافر يوجب مطلق التخفيف المتناول لإسقاط كل الصلاة أو شطر الصلاة.
ورابعها ما لم يثبت الغاؤه كالتترس المذكور.
وخامسها ما ثبت الغاؤه، وهو مطالب بتصحيح الاستقراء في دعوى وقوع هذه الخمسة لا تزيد، بل ربما يشهد الاستقراء بخلافه. قال في المنهاج» المؤثر ما أثر جنسه في نوع الحكم لا غير، والملائم والغريب كما ذكره الآمدي وبعض الشافعية شرطوا شهادة الأصول أيضاً، وهو العرض على الأصول لئلا يظهر بطلانه لمعارضة نص أو إجماع أو تخلف أو اقتضاء وجوده ضده وغير ذلك، فقيل : يجب العرض على الأصول كلها، وقيل: العرض على الاثنين كاف فانظر إلى هذا الاختلاف الذي وقع بينهم (وأما الحنفية فالمؤثر عندهم الوصف المناسب الملائم) للحكم عند العقول فيه احتراز عن العلل الطردية (الذي ظهر تأثيره شرعاً بأن يكون الجنسه تأثير في عين الحكم كإسقاط الصلاة الكثيرة بالإغماء فإن لجنسه الذي هو العجز) عن الأداء من غير حرج تأثيراً في سقوطها كما في الحائض (أو) بأن يكون تأثيراً (في جنسه كإسقاطها عن الحائض) معللاً (بالمشقة، وقد أسقط مشقة السفر الركعتين) فقد أثر جنس في جنس السقوط (أو) بأن يكون (لعينه) تأثير (في جنس الحكم كالأخوة لأب وأم في قياس التقدم في ولاية النكاح وقد تقدم هذا الأخ في الميراث) فقد أثر في مطلق الولاية (أو) يكون لعينه تأثير في عينه) أي عين الحكم (وذلك كثير) في الأقيسة الجزئية المذكورة في الفقه (وأورد عليه أنه لا بد فيه أي في هذا الاعتبار والتأثير من النص أو الإجماع إذ لا اخالة عندهم، وحينئذ لا يكون المؤثر (قسيماً لهما أي للعلة التي ثبتت بالنص أو الإجماع (كما هو المشهور فإنها قسمت في المشهور إلى منصوصة ومؤثرة إلا بالاعتبار) فإنها باعتبار أنها ثبتت بالنص منصوصة وباعتبار أنها مناسبة له مع الاعتبار المذكور مؤثرة (ثم هذه الأربعة بسائط، وقد يتركب بعض من الأقسام (مع بعض وينحصر) المركب في أحد عشر) قسماً (لأن الثنائي
المشقة
ستة) :
أحدها ما اعتبر عينه في عين الحكم وجنسه ، كالمرض اعتبر في الافطار، وفي جنسه

۳۱۸
فواتح الرحموت شرح مسلم الثبوت الجزء الثاني
وهو التخفيف في مطلق العبادة حتى شرع الصلاة بالتيمم وقاعداً. وثانيها : ما اعتبر عينه وجنسه في جنس الحكم كالطواف أثر في طهارة الماء وجنسه، المخالطة بنجاسة يشق الاحتراز عنها أيضاً علة للطهارة كآبار الفلوات . وهو وثالثها: ما اعتبر العين في العين والجنس في الجنس، كالجنون المطبق أثر في ولاية النكاح وجنسه وهو العجز بسبب عدم العقل أثر في مطلق الولاية.
(
ورابعها ما اعتبر جنسه في النوع وجنسه في الجنس كالصغر أثر جنسه، وهو العجز بسبب ضعف العقل في ولاية المال وأيضاً العجز في مطلق الولاية لا الصغر خصوصه إذ إيجابه للولاية على النكاح مختلف فيه فلا اجماع .
وخامسها ما اعتبر جنسه في نوع الحكم ونوعه في جنسه كخروج النجاسة أعم مما من : أحد السبيلين أثر في ايجاب الوضوء ونوعه وهو خروجها من غير السبيلين في مطلق التطهير، فإن تطهير البدن بخروجها منه واجب .
،
وسادسها ما اعتبر نوعه في الجنس وجنسه في الجنس كسلب العقل، فإنه مؤثر في سقوط العبادة الذي هو جنس الافطار لكون النية شرطاً فيها وجنسه ، وهو العجز لخلل في إحدى القوى مؤثر في سقوط العبادة كذا قالوا : (والثلاثي أربعة) :
أحدها ما اعتبر نوعه في نوع الحكم، وجنسه في جنسه ونوعه دون نوعه في جنسه، كالحيض أثر في حرمة القربان وجنسه وهو الأذى أثر فيه وفي جنسه، وهو قضاء الشهوة في محل الأذى حتى أثر في حرمة اللواطة . وثانيها : ما اعتبر نوعه في جنسه ونوعه وجنسه في نوعه دون جنسه في جنسه كالحيض : فإنه أثر في حرمة الصلاة وفي جنسه وهو حرمة القراءة وجنسه وهو خروج النجاسة من السبيلين أثر في حرمة الصلاة أيضاً لكنه غير مؤثر في حرمة القراءة.
أحد
ورابعها: ما اعتبر نوعه في نوعه وجنسه وجنسه في جنسه، دون جنسه في نوعه، كعدم وجدان الماء إلا ما أعد للشرب، فهو عجز عن الماء، وقد أثر في إيجاب التيمم لقوله تعالى : فَلَمْ تَجِدُوا مَاءً [النساء : ٤٣]، [المائدة: ٦] والأولى أن يقال : بالإجماع وجنسه وهو العجز عن استعمال ما شرط استعماله أثر في سقوط اشتراطه وعدم وجوبه فإنه قد سقط غسل الثوب النجس عند عدم وجدان الماء بالإجماع، وكذا عدم وجدان الماء أثر فيه دفعاً للهلاك، وأما جنسه المذكور فلم يوجب التيمم بخصوصه .
ورابعها ما لم يعتبر نوعه في نوعه، لكن اعتبر في جنسه وجنسه اعتبر في نوعه وجنسه، كخوف فوت صلاة العيد لم يؤثر في إباحة التيمم لا بالنص ولا بالإجماع، لكن جنسه وهو العجز عما شرط استعماله للصلاة أثر في إيجاب التيمم وفي جنسه، وهو سقوط ما شرط استعماله فيه، والنوع وهو العجز عن الماء قد أثر في هذا الجنس أيضاً، كذا قالوا، وفي هذا
The Fourth Principle / Qiyas. 317. [Explanation:] So either its nullification appears or does not appear. These are the sum of the categories, and what actually occurs in the Sharī‘ah is five, no more. First: that in which the specificity of the attribute is considered in the specificity of the ruling, and its generality in its generality, and it is called al-mulā’im (suitable), like killing with a heavy object, for it is intentional transgressive killing, and it is considered in retaliation for life, and its generality, absolute aggression, is considered in absolute retaliation. Second: that in which specificity is considered in specificity only, without a text or consensus, and it is the gharīb (strange) appropriate, like intoxication for prohibition if there is no text or consensus on it. Third: that in which its genus is considered in the genus of the ruling, and there is no text or consensus, and this is of the kind of mulā’im gharīb, like the genus of hardship shared between the menstruating woman and the traveler, necessitating absolute alleviation covering dropping all of the prayer or half of the prayer. Fourth: that whose nullification has not been established, like the mentioned tatarruṣ (using human shields). Fifth: that whose nullification has been established, and he [the author] is required to correct the induction in the claim that these five occur and no more; rather induction may witness the contrary. He said in al-Minhāj: 'Al-mu’aththir (effective attribute) is that whose genus affects the type of the ruling, nothing else, and al-mulā’im and al-gharīb.' As al-Āmidī mentioned, and some Shāfi‘īs also stipulated the testimony of the principles (al-uṣūl), which is presenting to the principles to avoid its invalidity becoming apparent due to opposition of text or consensus or lag or requiring its opposite, etc. So it was said: presenting to all principles is obligatory, and it was said: presenting to two is sufficient. So look at this disagreement that occurred among them. (As for the Ḥanafīs, al-mu’aththir according to them is the attribute that is appropriate (al-munāsib al-mulā’im) for the ruling in the intellects, thereby guarding against merely formal (ṭardiyya) causes, which has its effect manifested in the Sharī‘ah, either by its genus having an effect in the specific ruling, like dropping many prayers due to unconsciousness, for its genus which is incapability of performance without difficulty has an effect in dropping it as in the menstruating woman; or by having an effect in its genus, like dropping it for the menstruating woman justified by hardship, and hardship of travel has dropped two rak‘ahs, so a genus has effected a genus of dropping; or by its specific essence having an effect in the genus of the ruling, like the brother by both parents in analogy for precedence in the guardianship of marriage, and this brother has preceded in inheritance, so it has effected in absolute guardianship; or its specific essence having an effect in its specific essence, i.e., the specific ruling, and that is abundant in the partial analogies mentioned in fiqh. (It was objected that in this consideration and effect, text or consensus is necessary, since they have no free consideration, and then al-mu’aththir would not be a counterpart to them, i.e., to the cause established by text or consensus, as is well-known, for they are divided in the well-known view into manṣūṣa (text-based) and mu’aththira (effective), except by consideration: for it is manṣūṣa by virtue of being established by text, and mu’aththira by virtue of being appropriate to it with the mentioned consideration. (Then these four are simple, and some of the categories may combine with others, and the composite is limited to eleven) categories (because the binary is six): First: that in which its specific essence is considered in the specific ruling and its genus, like illness is considered in breaking the fast, and in its genus, which is alleviation in absolute worship, so much so that prayer is prescribed with tayammum and sitting. Second: that in which its specific essence and its genus are considered in the genus of the ruling, like ṭawāf (circumambulation) affected purity of water and its genus, mixing with impurity that is hard to avoid is also a cause for purity, like wells in deserts. Third: that in which the specific essence is considered in the specific ruling and the genus in the genus, like continuous insanity affected guardianship of marriage and its genus, which is incapability due to lack of intellect, affected absolute guardianship. Fourth: that in which its genus is considered in the type and its genus in the genus, like minority, its genus, which is incapability due to weak intellect, affected guardianship of property, and also incapability in absolute guardianship, not minority specifically, since its requiring guardianship over marriage is disputed, hence no consensus. Fifth: that in which its genus is considered in the type of the ruling and its type in its genus, like the exit of impurity, more general than what comes from the two passages, affected the obligation of wuḍū’, and its type, which is its exit from other than the two passages, in absolute purification, for purifying the body by its exit is obligatory. Sixth: that in which its type is considered in the genus and its genus in the genus, like deprivation of intellect, for it is effective in dropping worship, which is the genus of breaking the fast, because intention is a condition in it, and its genus, which is incapability due to a defect in one of the faculties, is effective in dropping worship, thus they said. (And the ternary is four): First: that in which its type is considered in the type of the ruling, and its genus in its genus and its type without its type in its genus, like menstruation affected the prohibition of approach, and its genus, which is harm, affected it and in its genus, which is the satisfaction of desire in the place of harm, so much so that it affected the prohibition of sodomy. Second: that in which its type is considered in its genus and its type and its genus in its type, without its genus in its genus, like menstruation: for it affected the prohibition of prayer and in its genus, which is the prohibition of recitation, and its genus, which is the exit of impurity from the two passages, affected the prohibition of prayer also but it does not affect the prohibition of recitation. Third: that in which its type is considered in its type and its genus and its genus in its genus, without its genus in its type, like the non-finding of water except what is prepared for drinking, so it is incapability of water, and it affected the obligation of tayammum due to His statement: 'and you do not find water' [al-Nisā’: 43, al-Mā’idah: 6], and it is better to say: by consensus, and its genus, which is incapability of using what is prescribed to use, affected the dropping of its prescription and its non-obligation, for indeed washing a najis garment when water is not found is dropped by consensus, and likewise non-finding of water affected it to repel destruction. But the mentioned genus did not necessitate tayammum specifically. Fourth: that in which its type is not considered in its type, but it is considered in its genus and its genus is considered in its type and its genus, like fear of missing the Eid prayer does not affect the permissibility of tayammum neither by text nor consensus, but its genus, which is incapability of what is prescribed to use for prayer, affected the obligation of tayammum and in its genus, which is dropping what is prescribed to use in it, and the type, which is incapability of water, has affected this genus also, thus they said. And in this...
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage is a detailed classification of the types of effective attributes (al-mu’aththir) in qiyas, according to the Hanafi school. The author begins by stating that the attributes that can be considered in analogy are five in number, no more, as found in the Shariah. He lists them: (1) mulā’im, where the specific attribute and its general meaning are both considered in the specific ruling and its general application; (2) gharīb, where only the specific attribute is considered without textual support; (3) a type that is like mulā’im gharīb, where the genus is considered in the genus of the ruling; (4) where nullification is not established; and (5) where nullification is established. Then he discusses the criterion for an attribute to be effective (mu’aththir), quoting al-Minhāj and mentioning that some Shāfi‘īs require the testimony of fundamental principles to avoid conflict with texts or consensus. The Hanafi view, however, is that al-mu’aththir is the attribute that is appropriate (munāsib mulā’im) for the ruling according to rational consideration, as opposed to purely formal (ṭardiyya) causes, and whose effect has been manifested in the Shariah—either its genus affects a specific ruling (e.g., inability causing dropping of many prayers), or its genus affects a genus (e.g., hardship dropping parts of worship), or its specific essence affects a genus (e.g., full brother affecting guardianship), or its specific essence affects a specific ruling (common in partial analogies). The author notes an objection that such an attribute must be supported by text or consensus, but he resolves this by saying that the same attribute can be considered both manṣūṣa (text-based) and mu’aththira (effective) from different perspectives. Then the passage moves to the combinatorial classifications: simple attributes are four, and composite ones arise from combining these, yielding eleven types: six binary combinations (where two aspects are considered) and four ternary combinations (where three aspects are considered). For each type, the author provides concrete examples from fiqh, such as illness, circumambulation, insanity, minority, impurity, deprivation of intellect, menstruation, and lack of water. These examples illustrate how the attribute's specific aspect and its genus are considered in the specific ruling and its genus. The explanation follows the classification order, and the teacher should note that the Hanafi emphasis on appropriateness and actual Shariah evidence distinguishes their approach from those who require only formal suitability.

Key Terms
المؤثر (al-mu’aththir): An attribute that is appropriate and whose effect is evident in the Shariah, either on the specific ruling or its genus.
المناسب (al-munāsib): The attribute that is suitable for the ruling in a rational sense, as opposed to formal (ṭardiyy) causes.
شهادة الأصول (shahādat al-uṣūl): The requirement that an attribute be presented to the fundamental principles of Shariah to ensure it does not contradict text, consensus, or other established principles.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition in the passage, which of the following is a necessary condition for an attribute to be mu'aththir?
A) It must be explicitly mentioned in the Quran or Sunnah.
B) It must be appropriate (munāsib) and its effect must be manifested in Shariah.
C) It must be agreed upon by all scholars.
D) It must be a formal (ṭardiyy) cause.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mu'aththir is the appropriate attribute whose effect is manifest in Shariah through one of four modes: genus on specific ruling, genus on genus, specific on genus, or specific on specific ruling.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
12 min
Composite Effective Attributes: Binary and Ternary Combinations
Classification of composite attribute combinations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and classify composite effective attributes into binary (six types) and ternary (four types) combinations, and provide fiqh examples for each.

Core Idea
Simple effective attributes combine in binary and ternary ways to cover all analogical reasoning scenarios.

After defining the four simple types of effective attributes, the passage explains how these simple categories combine to form composite ones. The author states that there are eleven composite types: six binary (where two aspects are considered) and four ternary (where three aspects are considered). Each combination involves the specific essence ('ayn) and/or genus (jins) of the attribute being considered in the specific or general aspect of the ruling. This lesson unpacks these combinations with the detailed examples provided.

Guided Path
1
Understand the four simple types
Before tackling composites, recall the four simple types from earlier: (Type 1) 'ayn considered in 'ayn, (Type 2) 'ayn in jins, (Type 3) jins in 'ayn, (Type 4) jins in jins. These are the building blocks.
These four simple types are the basis for all combinations.
2
Identify the six binary combinations
In the passage, the author lists six binary types. Each is a combination of two of the simple types. For example, type 1 of binary: 'ayn considered in 'ayn and jins considered in jins (like illness considered in breaking fast and in alleviation). Work through each of the six examples given.
The binary combinations are formed by pairing two different modes of consideration.
3
Analyze examples for each binary type
For each binary type, note the specific fiqh example: Type 1: illness (marad) affects breaking fast (ayn) and alleviation (jins). Type 2: ṭawāf affects water purity (jins of ruling) and also mixing with hard-to-avoid impurity is a cause for purity. Type 3: continuous insanity affects guardianship of marriage (ayn) and absolute guardianship (jins). Type 4: minority affects property guardianship (jins) and absolute guardianship (jins again). Type 5: exit of impurity affects wuḍū obligation (jins) and purification (type). Type 6: deprivation of intellect affects dropping worship (jins) and again dropping worship (jins).
Recognize that some combinations involve the same plane (e.g., jins in jins for both) while others mix.
4
Identify the four ternary combinations
The ternary combinations involve three aspects. The passage gives four examples using menstruation, lack of water, and fear of missing Eid prayer. Focus on the first example: menstruation affects prohibition of approach (type), genus of harm (jins), and also affects prohibition of sodomy (type again). Understand how three different considerations are combined.
Ternary combinations are more complex and often involve overlapping effects.
5
Practice classifying a new case
Using the patterns, try to classify a new attribute, such as 'poverty' for zakat exemption. Determine which simple types apply and then see if it forms a binary or ternary combination.
This step solidifies the classification skill.

الأصل الرابع/ القياس
۳۱۷
أصلاً، فأما أن يظهر الغاؤه أو لا يظهر، فهذه جملة الأقسام والواقع منها في الشرع خمسة لا تزيد .
أحدها: ما اعتبر خصوص الوصف في خصوص الحكم وعمومه في عمومه ويسمى الملائم، كالقتل بالمثقل، فإنه قتل العمد العدوان، وهو معتبر في قصاص النفس، وعمومه مطلق الجناية اعتبر في القصاص المطلق .
وثانيها ما اعتبر الخصوص في الخصوص فقط لا بنص أو إجماع، وهو المناسب الغريب، كالإسكار للتحريم إن لم يكن عليه نص أو إجماع.
وثالثها ما اعتبر جنسه في جنس الحكم ولا نص ولا إجماع وهذا من جنس الملائم الغريب، وهو كجنس المشقة المشتركة بين الحائض والمسافر يوجب مطلق التخفيف المتناول لإسقاط كل الصلاة أو شطر الصلاة.
ورابعها ما لم يثبت الغاؤه كالتترس المذكور.
وخامسها ما ثبت الغاؤه، وهو مطالب بتصحيح الاستقراء في دعوى وقوع هذه الخمسة لا تزيد، بل ربما يشهد الاستقراء بخلافه. قال في المنهاج» المؤثر ما أثر جنسه في نوع الحكم لا غير، والملائم والغريب كما ذكره الآمدي وبعض الشافعية شرطوا شهادة الأصول أيضاً، وهو العرض على الأصول لئلا يظهر بطلانه لمعارضة نص أو إجماع أو تخلف أو اقتضاء وجوده ضده وغير ذلك، فقيل : يجب العرض على الأصول كلها، وقيل: العرض على الاثنين كاف فانظر إلى هذا الاختلاف الذي وقع بينهم (وأما الحنفية فالمؤثر عندهم الوصف المناسب الملائم) للحكم عند العقول فيه احتراز عن العلل الطردية (الذي ظهر تأثيره شرعاً بأن يكون الجنسه تأثير في عين الحكم كإسقاط الصلاة الكثيرة بالإغماء فإن لجنسه الذي هو العجز) عن الأداء من غير حرج تأثيراً في سقوطها كما في الحائض (أو) بأن يكون تأثيراً (في جنسه كإسقاطها عن الحائض) معللاً (بالمشقة، وقد أسقط مشقة السفر الركعتين) فقد أثر جنس في جنس السقوط (أو) بأن يكون (لعينه) تأثير (في جنس الحكم كالأخوة لأب وأم في قياس التقدم في ولاية النكاح وقد تقدم هذا الأخ في الميراث) فقد أثر في مطلق الولاية (أو) يكون لعينه تأثير في عينه) أي عين الحكم (وذلك كثير) في الأقيسة الجزئية المذكورة في الفقه (وأورد عليه أنه لا بد فيه أي في هذا الاعتبار والتأثير من النص أو الإجماع إذ لا اخالة عندهم، وحينئذ لا يكون المؤثر (قسيماً لهما أي للعلة التي ثبتت بالنص أو الإجماع (كما هو المشهور فإنها قسمت في المشهور إلى منصوصة ومؤثرة إلا بالاعتبار) فإنها باعتبار أنها ثبتت بالنص منصوصة وباعتبار أنها مناسبة له مع الاعتبار المذكور مؤثرة (ثم هذه الأربعة بسائط، وقد يتركب بعض من الأقسام (مع بعض وينحصر) المركب في أحد عشر) قسماً (لأن الثنائي

ستة) :
أحدها ما اعتبر عينه في عين الحكم وجنسه ، كالمرض اعتبر في الافطار، وفي جنسه

فواتح الرحموت شرح مسلم الثبوت الجزء الثاني
وهو التخفيف في مطلق العبادة حتى شرع الصلاة بالتيمم وقاعداً. وثانيها : ما اعتبر عينه وجنسه في جنس الحكم كالطواف أثر في طهارة الماء وجنسه، المخالطة بنجاسة يشق الاحتراز عنها أيضاً علة للطهارة كآبار الفلوات . وهو وثالثها: ما اعتبر العين في العين والجنس في الجنس، كالجنون المطبق أثر في ولاية النكاح وجنسه وهو العجز بسبب عدم العقل أثر في مطلق الولاية.
(
ورابعها ما اعتبر جنسه في النوع وجنسه في الجنس كالصغر أثر جنسه، وهو العجز بسبب ضعف العقل في ولاية المال وأيضاً العجز في مطلق الولاية لا الصغر خصوصه إذ إيجابه للولاية على النكاح مختلف فيه فلا اجماع .
وخامسها ما اعتبر جنسه في نوع الحكم ونوعه في جنسه كخروج النجاسة أعم مما من : أحد السبيلين أثر في ايجاب الوضوء ونوعه وهو خروجها من غير السبيلين في مطلق التطهير، فإن تطهير البدن بخروجها منه واجب .
،
وسادسها ما اعتبر نوعه في الجنس وجنسه في الجنس كسلب العقل، فإنه مؤثر في سقوط العبادة الذي هو جنس الافطار لكون النية شرطاً فيها وجنسه ، وهو العجز لخلل في إحدى القوى مؤثر في سقوط العبادة كذا قالوا : (والثلاثي أربعة) :
أحدها ما اعتبر نوعه في نوع الحكم، وجنسه في جنسه ونوعه دون نوعه في جنسه، كالحيض أثر في حرمة القربان وجنسه وهو الأذى أثر فيه وفي جنسه، وهو قضاء الشهوة في محل الأذى حتى أثر في حرمة اللواطة . وثانيها : ما اعتبر نوعه في جنسه ونوعه وجنسه في نوعه دون جنسه في جنسه كالحيض : فإنه أثر في حرمة الصلاة وفي جنسه وهو حرمة القراءة وجنسه وهو خروج النجاسة من السبيلين أثر في حرمة الصلاة أيضاً لكنه غير مؤثر في حرمة القراءة.
أحد
ورابعها: ما اعتبر نوعه في نوعه وجنسه وجنسه في جنسه، دون جنسه في نوعه، كعدم وجدان الماء إلا ما أعد للشرب، فهو عجز عن الماء، وقد أثر في إيجاب التيمم لقوله تعالى : فَلَمْ تَجِدُوا مَاءً [النساء : ٤٣]، [المائدة: ٦] والأولى أن يقال : بالإجماع وجنسه وهو العجز عن استعمال ما شرط استعماله أثر في سقوط اشتراطه وعدم وجوبه فإنه قد سقط غسل الثوب النجس عند عدم وجدان الماء بالإجماع، وكذا عدم وجدان الماء أثر فيه دفعاً للهلاك، وأما جنسه المذكور فلم يوجب التيمم بخصوصه .
ورابعها ما لم يعتبر نوعه في نوعه، لكن اعتبر في جنسه وجنسه اعتبر في نوعه وجنسه، كخوف فوت صلاة العيد لم يؤثر في إباحة التيمم لا بالنص ولا بالإجماع، لكن جنسه وهو العجز عما شرط استعماله للصلاة أثر في إيجاب التيمم وفي جنسه، وهو سقوط ما شرط استعماله فيه، والنوع وهو العجز عن الماء قد أثر في هذا الجنس أيضاً، كذا قالوا، وفي هذا
The Fourth Principle / Qiyas. 317. [Explanation:] So either its nullification appears or does not appear. These are the sum of the categories, and what actually occurs in the Sharī‘ah is five, no more. First: that in which the specificity of the attribute is considered in the specificity of the ruling, and its generality in its generality, and it is called al-mulā’im (suitable), like killing with a heavy object, for it is intentional transgressive killing, and it is considered in retaliation for life, and its generality, absolute aggression, is considered in absolute retaliation. Second: that in which specificity is considered in specificity only, without a text or consensus, and it is the gharīb (strange) appropriate, like intoxication for prohibition if there is no text or consensus on it. Third: that in which its genus is considered in the genus of the ruling, and there is no text or consensus, and this is of the kind of mulā’im gharīb, like the genus of hardship shared between the menstruating woman and the traveler, necessitating absolute alleviation covering dropping all of the prayer or half of the prayer. Fourth: that whose nullification has not been established, like the mentioned tatarruṣ (using human shields). Fifth: that whose nullification has been established, and he [the author] is required to correct the induction in the claim that these five occur and no more; rather induction may witness the contrary. He said in al-Minhāj: 'Al-mu’aththir (effective attribute) is that whose genus affects the type of the ruling, nothing else, and al-mulā’im and al-gharīb.' As al-Āmidī mentioned, and some Shāfi‘īs also stipulated the testimony of the principles (al-uṣūl), which is presenting to the principles to avoid its invalidity becoming apparent due to opposition of text or consensus or lag or requiring its opposite, etc. So it was said: presenting to all principles is obligatory, and it was said: presenting to two is sufficient. So look at this disagreement that occurred among them. (As for the Ḥanafīs, al-mu’aththir according to them is the attribute that is appropriate (al-munāsib al-mulā’im) for the ruling in the intellects, thereby guarding against merely formal (ṭardiyya) causes, which has its effect manifested in the Sharī‘ah, either by its genus having an effect in the specific ruling, like dropping many prayers due to unconsciousness, for its genus which is incapability of performance without difficulty has an effect in dropping it as in the menstruating woman; or by having an effect in its genus, like dropping it for the menstruating woman justified by hardship, and hardship of travel has dropped two rak‘ahs, so a genus has effected a genus of dropping; or by its specific essence having an effect in the genus of the ruling, like the brother by both parents in analogy for precedence in the guardianship of marriage, and this brother has preceded in inheritance, so it has effected in absolute guardianship; or its specific essence having an effect in its specific essence, i.e., the specific ruling, and that is abundant in the partial analogies mentioned in fiqh. (It was objected that in this consideration and effect, text or consensus is necessary, since they have no free consideration, and then al-mu’aththir would not be a counterpart to them, i.e., to the cause established by text or consensus, as is well-known, for they are divided in the well-known view into manṣūṣa (text-based) and mu’aththira (effective), except by consideration: for it is manṣūṣa by virtue of being established by text, and mu’aththira by virtue of being appropriate to it with the mentioned consideration. (Then these four are simple, and some of the categories may combine with others, and the composite is limited to eleven) categories (because the binary is six): First: that in which its specific essence is considered in the specific ruling and its genus, like illness is considered in breaking the fast, and in its genus, which is alleviation in absolute worship, so much so that prayer is prescribed with tayammum and sitting. Second: that in which its specific essence and its genus are considered in the genus of the ruling, like ṭawāf (circumambulation) affected purity of water and its genus, mixing with impurity that is hard to avoid is also a cause for purity, like wells in deserts. Third: that in which the specific essence is considered in the specific ruling and the genus in the genus, like continuous insanity affected guardianship of marriage and its genus, which is incapability due to lack of intellect, affected absolute guardianship. Fourth: that in which its genus is considered in the type and its genus in the genus, like minority, its genus, which is incapability due to weak intellect, affected guardianship of property, and also incapability in absolute guardianship, not minority specifically, since its requiring guardianship over marriage is disputed, hence no consensus. Fifth: that in which its genus is considered in the type of the ruling and its type in its genus, like the exit of impurity, more general than what comes from the two passages, affected the obligation of wuḍū’, and its type, which is its exit from other than the two passages, in absolute purification, for purifying the body by its exit is obligatory. Sixth: that in which its type is considered in the genus and its genus in the genus, like deprivation of intellect, for it is effective in dropping worship, which is the genus of breaking the fast, because intention is a condition in it, and its genus, which is incapability due to a defect in one of the faculties, is effective in dropping worship, thus they said. (And the ternary is four): First: that in which its type is considered in the type of the ruling, and its genus in its genus and its type without its type in its genus, like menstruation affected the prohibition of approach, and its genus, which is harm, affected it and in its genus, which is the satisfaction of desire in the place of harm, so much so that it affected the prohibition of sodomy. Second: that in which its type is considered in its genus and its type and its genus in its type, without its genus in its genus, like menstruation: for it affected the prohibition of prayer and in its genus, which is the prohibition of recitation, and its genus, which is the exit of impurity from the two passages, affected the prohibition of prayer also but it does not affect the prohibition of recitation. Third: that in which its type is considered in its type and its genus and its genus in its genus, without its genus in its type, like the non-finding of water except what is prepared for drinking, so it is incapability of water, and it affected the obligation of tayammum due to His statement: 'and you do not find water' [al-Nisā’: 43, al-Mā’idah: 6], and it is better to say: by consensus, and its genus, which is incapability of using what is prescribed to use, affected the dropping of its prescription and its non-obligation, for indeed washing a najis garment when water is not found is dropped by consensus, and likewise non-finding of water affected it to repel destruction. But the mentioned genus did not necessitate tayammum specifically. Fourth: that in which its type is not considered in its type, but it is considered in its genus and its genus is considered in its type and its genus, like fear of missing the Eid prayer does not affect the permissibility of tayammum neither by text nor consensus, but its genus, which is incapability of what is prescribed to use for prayer, affected the obligation of tayammum and in its genus, which is dropping what is prescribed to use in it, and the type, which is incapability of water, has affected this genus also, thus they said. Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage is a detailed classification of the types of effective attributes (al-mu’aththir) in qiyas, according to the Hanafi school. The author begins by stating that the attributes that can be considered in analogy are five in number, no more, as found in the Shariah. He lists them: (1) mulā’im, where the specific attribute and its general meaning are both considered in the specific ruling and its general application; (2) gharīb, where only the specific attribute is considered without textual support; (3) a type that is like mulā’im gharīb, where the genus is considered in the genus of the ruling; (4) where nullification is not established; and (5) where nullification is established. Then he discusses the criterion for an attribute to be effective (mu’aththir), quoting al-Minhāj and mentioning that some Shāfi‘īs require the testimony of fundamental principles to avoid conflict with texts or consensus. The Hanafi view, however, is that al-mu’aththir is the attribute that is appropriate (munāsib mulā’im) for the ruling according to rational consideration, as opposed to purely formal (ṭardiyya) causes, and whose effect has been manifested in the Shariah—either its genus affects a specific ruling (e.g., inability causing dropping of many prayers), or its genus affects a genus (e.g., hardship dropping parts of worship), or its specific essence affects a genus (e.g., full brother affecting guardianship), or its specific essence affects a specific ruling (common in partial analogies). The author notes an objection that such an attribute must be supported by text or consensus, but he resolves this by saying that the same attribute can be considered both manṣūṣa (text-based) and mu’aththira (effective) from different perspectives. Then the passage moves to the combinatorial classifications: simple attributes are four, and composite ones arise from combining these, yielding eleven types: six binary combinations (where two aspects are considered) and four ternary combinations (where three aspects are considered). For each type, the author provides concrete examples from fiqh, such as illness, circumambulation, insanity, minority, impurity, deprivation of intellect, menstruation, and lack of water. These examples illustrate how the attribute's specific aspect and its genus are considered in the specific ruling and its genus. The explanation follows the classification order, and the teacher should note that the Hanafi emphasis on appropriateness and actual Shariah evidence distinguishes their approach from those who require only formal suitability.

Key Terms
المركب (al-murakkab): A composite effective attribute that combines two or more of the simple types.
النوع (al-naw'): In this context, often synonymous with the specific aspect of the ruling or attribute, as opposed to the genus (jins).

Key Terms from Source Passage

How many composite types of effective attributes does the passage identify?
A) 5

D) 15

Key Takeaway
Simple effective attributes combine to form eleven composite types: six binary and four ternary, covering all possible analogical reasoning patterns.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
15 min
Classification of the Effective Cause in Qiyas and Its Acceptance
Taxonomy of 'illah attributes and debate on qiyas validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the six types of 'illah based on essence/genus/species and evaluate the Hanafi dispute on the validity of considering the genus in the genus of the ruling.

Core Idea
The effective cause may be its essence, genus, or species; Hanafis accept all combinations as valid qiyas, but debate remains on genus in genus.

Qiyas relies on identifying an effective cause ('illah) that connects the original ruling to a new case. But what exactly constitutes the 'illah? Is it the specific textual attribute, its broader genus, or an intermediate species? This passage from Musallam al-Thubut presents a meticulous classification of the 'illah and explores a key dispute: does considering the genus of the 'illah in the genus of the ruling produce valid qiyas? Understanding this taxonomy sharpens your ability to assess analogical reasoning in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish essence, genus, and species
Identify the three levels of the 'illah: 'ayn (specific attribute in the text), jins (broader category), and naw' (intermediate species). The passage uses these to classify how the 'illah relates to the ruling.
For example, intoxication (sukr) is an 'illah; its genus is 'source of enmity'.
2
Enumerate the six initial types
The text lists six patterns (second through seventh) of how 'illah and ruling interact in terms of essence/genus/species. For each, identify the pattern and its fiqh example (e.g., circumambulation affecting water purity).
These cover combinations like 'essence in essence' or 'genus in genus'.
3
Analyze the threefold and fourfold divisions
The passage then presents threefold (four subtypes) and fourfold (one subtype) classifications. Work through each with the examples: menstruation, lack of water, fear of missing Eid prayer, and intoxication.
Note how intoxication is used as a comprehensive example.
4
Examine the scholarly dispute
Identify the two opposing views: some Hanafis reject considering genus in genus; the majority accept it. Ibn al-Humam reduces genus-in-essence to essence-in-essence. Understand the reasoning behind each position.
The dispute centers on whether an explicit original (asl) is necessary for qiyas.
5
Evaluate the majority position and its implications
The majority (جمهور الحنفية) accepts all combinations, including genus in genus, as valid qiyas. The author critiques the view that such 'illah is a pure legal cause without need for an original. See the child's deposit example for practical application.
This flexibility allows broader analogy without requiring an identical text.

Fourth: that which its genus is considered in the species and its genus in the genus, like minority affecting its genus, which is incapacity due to weakness of intellect in guardianship of wealth, and also incapacity in absolute guardianship, not the specificity of minority, since its requirement of guardianship over marriage is disputed, so no consensus. Sixth: that which its species is considered in the genus and its genus in the genus, like the removal of intellect, for it affects the falling of worship which is the genus of breaking fast because intention is a condition in it, and its genus, which is incapacity due to a flaw in one of the faculties, affects the falling of worship. Second: that which its species is considered in its genus and its species and its genus in its species but not its genus in its genus, like menstruation: it affects the prohibition of prayer and in its genus which is the prohibition of recitation, and its genus which is the exit of impurity from the two passages affects the prohibition of prayer as well but is not effective in the prohibition of recitation. Third: that which its species is considered in its species and its genus and its genus in its genus, but not its genus in its species, like the lack of finding water except that prepared for drinking, so it is incapacity for water, and it has effect in obligating tayammum by His saying: 'If you do not find water' [4:43, 5:6], and it is better to say: by consensus, and its genus which is incapacity to use what is conditioned for use has effect in dropping its being a condition and its non-obligation, for washing a najis garment when water is not found has been dropped by consensus, and similarly the lack of finding water has effect in it to ward off destruction; as for its mentioned genus, it did not obligate tayammum specifically. Fourth: that which its species is not considered in its species, but is considered in its genus, and its genus is considered in its species and its genus, like the fear of missing the Eid prayer did not affect the permissibility of tayammum neither by text nor by consensus, but its genus, which is incapacity for what is conditioned for use for prayer, had effect in obligating tayammum and in its genus, which is the dropping of what is conditioned for use in it, and the species, which is incapacity for water, had effect in this genus as well. Thus they said, and in this is consideration, for it is assumed first as fear of missing, and later as incapacity for water which is effective in tayammum; if it is exactly the fear of missing, then the consideration of species in species is established; if it is other, as is apparent, then the incapacity in fear of missing is a specific incapacity due to disruption of speech. Then the truth is that the meaning in His statement, and Allah knows best, 'If you do not find water', is the lack of finding for prayer, so it includes the incapacity due to fear of missing. If he does not find water sufficient for prayer, then the species has affected the species. So understand. (And) the section (the fourfold is only one) and the author restricted himself to its example because it encompasses the sections, so its example encompasses all examples, as he indicated by his saying: (And its example, as if for all, is intoxication), considered in prohibition, i.e., the prohibition of intoxicants, not only wine, for its prohibition with us is specifically not caused by intoxication due to his saying, peace be upon him and his family and companions, 'Every intoxicant is prohibited' narrated by Muslim, and its genus, which is the source of enmity and hatred, is considered in it, i.e., the prohibition of intoxicants, by text and consensus. Then intoxication is considered in the prohibition of the source of enmity, which is the genus of the prohibition of drinking, for it is more specific, and the source of enmity, its genus is considered in the prohibition of slander, which is another species of the source of enmity, just as it is considered in the prohibition of drinking. So ponder. Then among them one who negated the genus in the genus, and perhaps he assumed that the cause is not effective then, and that the effective cause is only the genus not otherwise. And among them one who restricted consideration to this, and although this is attributed to Imam Fakhr al-Islam, but no justification appears for it. And Shaykh Ibn al-Humam, may Allah have mercy on him, dropped the consideration of the genus in the essence because, i.e., the consideration of the genus is only by making the essence a cause by virtue of its inclusion of the genus which is the cause, because the genus does not exist in the essence of the ruling except within the species in which it is found, so it has no effect except within it. So the consideration of the genus in the essence returns to the consideration of the essence in the essence. I say: It is possible that the species, as a species, i.e., from the aspect of specificity, is more suitable to the ruling, even if the effect established by text or consensus is for the genus, then the presumption, i.e., the presumption of causation, is stronger. So understand. And the majority of the Hanafis are that reasoning by the whole from each one of the divisions of singularity and combination is acceptable: if it is its essence or its genus, i.e., considering its essence or its genus in the essence of the ruling, then it is qiyas by agreement due to the existence of the original which contains the essence of the cause, so the essence of the ruling is transferred from it. And if the effect of its essence or its genus is in its genus, i.e., the genus of the ruling, then it is said: this is also qiyas, and it is chosen by the two Imams Shams al-A'imma and Fakhr al-Islam, except that the original may be mentioned or may be left due to its clarity, as in the issue of the deposit of a child, meaning if a man deposits his wealth with a child, if he consumes it, he does not guarantee because he is authorized by the owner to destroy it, so he does not guarantee, like something permitted for consumption. So this original may be mentioned or may be left. So there is no simple reasoning then in the genus at all, otherwise it would not be qiyas due to the absence of the cause in the species of the ruling in an original to transfer to the branch. And there is something in it. Because this claim must be verified by induction and has not been established yet; how, when Shaykh Ibn al-Humam explicitly stated that the suitable mursal is accepted by the Hanafis, so there is no original there containing the considered essence of the ruling, even if the effect is for the genus. So understand. And it is said: This is not qiyas, but rather a legal cause established by opinion, confirming the ruling, so it is like a text that does not need an original to be analogized upon. I say: This, as you see, is corrupt, for there is no room for opinion in comprehending rulings; how, we do not have a fifth source for comprehending rulings. And they may say: That a child with the essence of the cause...
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage is a detailed Hanafi usul exposition on the classification of the effective cause (al-'illah) in qiyas (analogical reasoning) based on how the 'illah relates to the ruling in terms of its essence (عين), genus (جنس), and species (نوع). The commentary expands on the categories presented in the matn of Musallam al-Thubut. The author begins by listing six types (the second through sixth, as the first is on the previous page), each with examples from fiqh. For instance, the second type considers both the essence and genus of the 'illah in the genus of the ruling, exemplified by circumambulation affecting water purity. The third type considers essence in essence and genus in genus, like continuous insanity affecting guardianship of marriage. Then the threefold division (الثلاثي) is introduced with four subtypes, each describing permutations of which aspect of the 'illah (type, genus) is considered in which aspect of the ruling. Examples include menstruation affecting prohibition of approach, lack of water leading to tayammum, and fear of missing Eid prayer. The author also examines the fourfold division (الرباعي) with a single example: intoxication (السكر) as an 'illah for the prohibition of intoxicants, considering its genus (source of enmity) in various rulings like prohibition of drinking and slander. The passage then turns to a scholarly dispute: some Hanafis reject considering genus in genus, while others accept all forms. Ibn al-Humam drops the consideration of genus in essence, arguing it reduces to essence in essence. The majority (جمهور الحنفية) accept all these types as valid qiyas, though some require an explicit original (أصل) for analogy. The author critiques the view that such 'illah is a pure legal cause without need for an original, asserting that opinion (رأي) alone cannot establish rulings. The discussion is cut off mid-sentence, likely continuing with the example of a child's deposit.

Key Terms
العلة (al-'illah): The effective cause in qiyas that is considered for extending a ruling from an original to a branch.
العين (al-'ayn): The specific essence of the 'illah, as opposed to its genus or species.
الجنس (al-jins): The general category or genus of the 'illah, broader than its specific essence.
النوع (al-naw'): The species or specific type of the 'illah, intermediate between 'ayn and jins.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning; extending a ruling from an original case to a branch due to a shared effective cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the position of the majority of Hanafis on considering the genus of the 'illah in the genus of the ruling?
A) It is unanimously rejected.
B) It is accepted as valid qiyas.
C) Only the two Imams (Shams al-A'imma and Fakhr al-Islam) accept it.
D) It is accepted only if the 'illah's essence is also present in the original.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts all classifications of the 'illah (essence, genus, species) as valid bases for qiyas, with the majority considering even genus-in-genus as valid analogy.

The Fourth Type of Qiyas: The Example of Intoxicants
Defines the fourth type of qiyas with the example of intoxicants

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the fourth type of qiyas and apply it to the example of intoxicants by tracing the ‘illah of sukr through its genus and species levels.

Core Idea
The fourth type of qiyas uses an ‘illah that is a genus or species affecting another genus or species, as with intoxication (sukr) prohibiting all intoxicants.

This passage from *Fawatih al-Rahamut* explains the fourth type of qiyas (qiyas rubā‘ī) using the example of intoxicants. The core idea is that the legal cause (‘illah) – intoxication (sukr) – is not limited to a single species (wine) but extends to the genus of intoxicants. This example demonstrates how the ‘illah can operate at multiple hierarchical levels (species, genus, higher genus) to derive rulings for various acts. Understanding this type of qiyas is essential for grasping how Hanafi jurists analogically extend rulings based on broad effective causes.

Guided Path
1
Locate the fourth type of qiyas in the passage
The text explicitly mentions 'the fourth section' (القسم الرباعي). Identify that the author gives only one example for this section, stating it is comprehensive of all examples.
The fourth type involves an 'illah that is a genus affecting a species, or a species affecting a genus, and so on.
2
Identify the key 'illah (legal cause) mentioned
The 'illah is 'sukr' (intoxication). The text says 'intoxication is considered in prohibition' (السكر اعتبر في الحرمة). Note that the prohibition of wine is not specifically based on wine itself but on the broader ‘illah of intoxication, as supported by the hadith.
Avoid the common mistake of thinking the 'illah is limited to wine. The hadith 'Every intoxicant is prohibited' makes sukr the generic cause.
3
Trace the hierarchy of the 'illah
The passage explains that sukr (species) is considered in the prohibition of intoxicants (genus). Then the genus of sukr (i.e., intoxication as a broader concept) is considered in the prohibition of the cause of enmity (موقع العداوة). Then that genus (cause of enmity) is considered in the prohibition of slander (another species). This shows the 'illah moving from species to genus to another genus and then to another species.
This hierarchical movement is the hallmark of the fourth type of qiyas.
4
Verify the textual basis
The hadith 'كل مسكر حرام' (Every intoxicant is prohibited) is cited as the dalil. This hadith, though ahad in transmission, has clear and definitive meaning (qat‘i al-dalalah). It establishes that the 'illah is the essential property of causing intoxication, not the specific substance wine.
The 'illah is derived from the hadith's explicit statement, making it a clear case of qiyas where the 'illah is textually identified.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصل الرابع/ القياس المثال نظر فإنه فرض أو لا خوف الفوت، وآخراً العجز عن الماء وهو مؤثر في التيمم فإن كان هو بعينه خوف الفوت، فقد ثبت اعتبار النوع في النوع وإن كان غيره، كما هو الظاهر فإن العجز في خوف الفوت عجز خاص لختل الكلام، ثم الحق أن المراد في قوله تعالى والله أعلم فلم تجدوا ماءً، عدم الوجدان للصلاة، فيشمل العجز لخوف الفوت، فإن لم يجد ماء بحيث يكفي للصلاة فقد أثر النوع في النوع فافهم (و) القسم (الرباعي واحد فقط) واقتصر المصنف على مثاله لكونه جامعاً للأقسام فمثاله جامع الأمثلة الكل كما أشار إليه بقوله : (ومثاله وكأنه للكل السكر) اعتبر في الحرمة) أي حرمة المسكر لا الخمر فقط فإن حرمتها عندنا بعينها غير معللة بالسكر لقوله عليه وعلى آله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام كل مسكر حرام رواه مسلم وجنسه وهو موقع العداوة والبغضاء) اعتبر (فيها) أي حرمة المسكر بالنص والإجماع (ثم السكر) اعتبر في حرمة موقع العداوة وهو جنس حرمة (الشرب فإنها أخص (وموقع العداوة جنسه اعتبر (في حرمة (القذف التي هي نوع آخر من موقع العداوة (كما) اعتبر (فيها) أي في حرمة الشرب فتدبر
The fourth principle: qiyas example: consider: is it obligatory or not? Fear of missing (prayer). And lastly, inability to find water, which affects tayammum. If it is exactly fear of missing, then the influence of the species on the species is confirmed. If it is something else, as is apparent, then the inability due to fear of missing is a specific inability causing confusion. Then the truth is that what is intended in the verse 'and you do not find water' (Allah knows best) is not finding water for prayer, so it includes inability due to fear of missing. If he does not find water sufficient for prayer, then the species has influenced the species, so understand. (And) the (fourth) section: only one example, and the author limited himself to its example because it encompasses all sections, so its example is comprehensive of all examples, as he indicated by saying: (and its example is as if it is for everything: intoxication) is considered in prohibition, i.e., the prohibition of intoxicants, not only wine, because its prohibition according to us is not specifically based on intoxication due to his saying, peace be upon him and his companions: 'Every intoxicant is prohibited' reported by Muslim. And its genus, which is the cause of enmity and hatred) is considered (in it), i.e., the prohibition of intoxicants by text and consensus. (Then) intoxication is considered in the prohibition of the cause of enmity which is the genus of the prohibition of drinking, for it is more specific. (And the cause of enmity its genus is considered) in the prohibition of slander, which is another type of cause of enmity, (just as) it is considered (in it), i.e., in the prohibition of drinking, so reflect.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage defines the fourth type of qiyas (rubā‘ī) and provides the example of intoxicants (sukr). The fourth type involves the 'illah (legal cause) being a genus or species affecting the genus or species of the ruling. The example: the prohibition of wine is based on the 'illah of intoxication (sukr), which is a specific type. But the hadith 'Every intoxicant is prohibited' extends the 'illah to the genus of intoxication. This genus (sukr) is then used to prohibit other things like the cause of enmity (which is a genus), and from there to specific acts like drinking and slander. Thus the 'illah operates at different levels of genus and species, illustrating the fourth type. The author emphasizes that this example covers all forms of the fourth type.

Key Terms
سكر (sukr): Intoxication, the 'illah for prohibition of intoxicants.
مسكر (musakir): Intoxicant, anything that causes intoxication.
حرمة (hurma): Prohibition, the ruling that attaches to intoxicants.
القياس الرباعي (al-qiyas al-ruba‘i): The fourth type of qiyas, where the 'illah is a genus affecting a species, a species affecting a genus, or a genus affecting another genus, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the hadith 'كل مسكر حرام' establish regarding the 'illah for the prohibition of intoxicants?
A) The 'illah is limited to wine.
B) The 'illah is the specific substance of each intoxicant.
C) The 'illah is intoxication (sukr) itself, which applies to all intoxicants.
D) The 'illah is the cause of enmity and hatred.

Key Takeaway
The fourth type of qiyas is illustrated by the 'illah of intoxication (sukr) that operates across genus and species levels to derive the prohibition of all intoxicants, drinking, and slander.

'Illah as 'Ayn or Jins: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Presents Hanafi disagreement on whether 'illah is specific or generic in qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the 'ayn and jins conceptions of 'illah in Hanafi qiyas and evaluate the validity of qiyas when the 'illah is a genus.

Core Idea
The 'illah in qiyas can be either specific ('ayn) or generic (jins), and both yield valid qiyas according to the majority of Hanafis.

This passage explores a subtle but important dispute within the Hanafi school: is the effective cause ('illah) in qiyas restricted to a specific attribute ('ayn), or can it be a broader genus (jins)? The answer determines whether certain analogies are valid. We will examine the arguments of the different Hanafi scholars and the majority position that accepts both. By the end, you will be able to identify each position and apply the Hanafi framework to classify types of qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Map the Positions
List the three views: some deny jins in jins (only 'ayn effective), some restrict to jins only (Fakhr al-Islam's attributed view), and the majority accepts both 'ayn and jins as valid 'illah.
The majority view is the mufta bihi.
2
Analyze Ibn al-Humam's Critique
Ibn al-Humam argues that considering jins in 'ayn reduces to 'ayn in 'ayn, but the species may have stronger suitability. Understand his reasoning that genus cannot exist outside a species.
This is a refinement, not a rejection.
3
Understand Mursal al-Mula'im
The acceptance of mursal al-mula'im shows that an explicit original is not always needed, supporting the use of jins as 'illah.
This is a key Hanafi principle in qiyas.
4
Examine the Examples
Work through the examples: deposit with a child, necessity in carrion, tawaf, tayammum, etc. See how a genus (darura) yields different rulings in different contexts.
Each example shows the 'illah is the genus producing species-specific effects.
5
Evaluate the Tarjih
The text concludes 'والحق أنه قياس' – the truth is it is qiyas. Understand why the majority view prevails and the opposing views are considered weak.
The tarjih is based on inductive verification and acceptance of mursal al-mula'im.

الأقسام المذكورة كلها معتبرة فالمؤثر وثلاثة من الملائم وثلاثة من ملائم المرسل في عرف الشافعية كلها مقبول ومؤثر عند الحنفية كما ظهر لك عن قريب دون الغريب من المرسل بل الغريب مطلقاً لعدم ظهور تأثيره شرعاً) بوجه من الوجوه، ولا بد منه (ثم المذكور في كتب الحنفية أن التأثير عندنا بالنص أو الإجماع والإخالة أو العرض على (الأصول وقد مر تفصيله عند الشافعية شرط لوجوب العمل وأما الجواز) للعمل فيثبت بالملاءمة فقط فإن الوصف شاهد والتأثير ونحوه عدالة، وبفقدانها لا العمل، لكن يجوز كما أنه لو قضى القاضي بالشهود الغير العدول نفذ قضاؤه (أقول : المناسبة فقط) بدون التأثير ونحوه تفيد ظن الاعتبار أولاً، والأول واجب العمل به لأن الاتباع بالظن واجب (والثاني ممتنع عمله لأن ما لا يظن كونه حكم الله فحرام العمل فتدبر).
Then among them are those who denied the genus in the genus, and perhaps he thought that the 'illah does not have effect then, and that the effective 'illah is only the genus, not other. And among them are those who restricted consideration to this, even though it is attributed to Imam Fakhr al-Islam, but it does not seem to have a basis. And Shaykh Ibn al-Humam (may Allah have mercy on him) dropped consideration of the genus in the species, because that consideration of the genus is nothing but making the species a cause due to its inclusion of the genus which is the cause, because the genus does not exist in the specific ruling except within the type in which it exists, so it has no effect except within it. So consideration of the genus in the species returns to consideration of the species in the species. I say: It is possible that the species as a species, i.e., in terms of specificity, is more suitable to the ruling, even if the effect established by text or consensus is for the genus, thereby producing a stronger probability (zann) of causality, so understand. And the majority of Hanafis are of the view that legal reasoning by the whole (al-kull) from one and the same type of isolated and combined types is acceptable. So if it is its specific or its genus (i.e., considering its specific or its genus in the specific of the ruling), it is qiyas by agreement, because there exists an original (asl) that contains the specific 'illah from which the specific ruling is extended. And if the effect of its specific or its genus (is in its genus, i.e., the genus of the ruling), then it is said that this also is qiyas, and it is chosen by the two Imams (Shams al-A'imma and Fakhr al-Islam), except that the original may be mentioned or may be omitted due to its clarity, as in the case of the deposit of a child: meaning if a man deposits his money with a child, and the child consumes it, he is not liable because he is authorized by the owner to destroy it, so he is not liable like one who is permitted to consume it. So this original may be mentioned or omitted. So there is no legal reasoning (ta'lil) then in the genus as a simple thing at all; otherwise it would not be qiyas due to the absence of the 'illah in the type of ruling in an original to extend to the branch. And there is something in this, because this claim must be verified by induction and has not been established yet. How can it be when Shaykh Ibn al-Humam explicitly stated that the mursal al-mula'im (suitable but disconnected) is acceptable among the Hanafis, so there exists no original that contains the specific ruling in question, even if the effect is for the genus? So understand. And it is said: this is not qiyas but rather a legal cause established by opinion (ra'y) that establishes the ruling, so it becomes like a text that does not require an original to measure against. I say: this, as you see, is corrupt, because there is no room for opinion in understanding rulings; how so when we have no fifth principle for understanding rulings? And they may say: the genus of the ruling established by it is established by the text that came concerning the genus of the ruling, and this reasoning indicates its establishment of the ruling in the original. So reflect on it; perhaps because of this they were labeled as 'people of opinion' (Ahl al-Ra'y). This is something astonishing from those who labeled them, for among them are those who considered suitability (ikhala) and rejected mursal (disconnected) traditions from the sunnah, and among them are those who accepted them, and also al-masalih al-mursalah (unrestricted public interests), and they acted on istishab (presumption of continuity) which is not a proof at all, so they are more deserving to be labeled by this name. So understand. (And the truth is that it is qiyas, not because the original containing the specific 'illah is omitted, for it is not, but because the genus when it passes requires the genus of the ruling, that the effect of the genus in the genus diversifies its requirement in the types with diverse aspects). Meaning the genus requires the 'illah in each type a type of ruling that is suitable for it. So the types of ruling are from the necessities of its realization, i.e., the realization of that genus in the types. So the original in this qiyas is what the 'illah is realized in, necessitating the genus of the ruling. So this genus extends to its branch which is its counterpart in this genus, but it is realized in a type suitable for this place, and the requirement of this genus diversifies in this place. Like necessity (darura) required in dire need the permissibility of eating carrion, because its requirement in it is suitable; and it required in circumambulation (tawaf) the purity of the leftover water of a cat, as that is suitable for tawaf; and it required when only drinking water is available and not other water the permissibility of tayammum, as is suitable, and so on. Similarly, it required in shoes the purity by rubbing, and in wheat and barley purity by division (qisma). That is, necessity is a genus that required alleviation (takhfif), and it has types; in each matter a type of it exists with what is suitable of the types of necessity. So each type of ruling is suitable to be measured upon another if its ruling is textual or agreed upon (mujma' 'alayh). (Yes): if the genus is close, then understanding it is close due to the clarity of the commonality. If it is distant, then precise understanding cannot be obtained except by strong thought. So the manifestation of effect and consideration is the original (asl) in which the genus affected the genus of its textual or agreed-upon ruling. (And this), i.e., equality in the genus of the ruling, is a type of absolute equality considered in absolute qiyas defined as equality of the branch to the original, because the intention is more general than specific or generic. So reflect, it is subtle and rare such that it is known and denied. (And based on what has been mentioned that all the mentioned divisions are considered, the mu'aththir (effective) and three types of mula'im (suitable) and three types of mula'im mursal (suitable but disconnected) in the terminology of the Shafi'is are all accepted and effective among the Hanafis, as has become clear to you recently, except the gharib (remote) of the mursal, rather the gharib in absolute terms, because its effect is not apparent legally in any way, and it is necessary. (Then what is mentioned in the Hanafi books is that effect (ta'thir) according to us is by text, consensus, suitability (ikhala), or presentation upon the usul (principles), and its detailed discussion has passed. According to the Shafi'is, it is a condition for obligation of action. As for permissibility) of action, it is established by mere suitability, because the attribute is a witness, and effect and the like are like justice. Without it, action is not valid, but it is permissible, just as if a judge judges based on witnesses who are not just, his judgement is executed. (I say: mere suitability without effect and the like yields a probability of consideration firstly, and the first is obligatory to act upon because following probability is obligatory; and the second is impermissible to act upon because what is not thought to be Allah's ruling is forbidden to act upon, so reflect.)
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed Hanafi dispute about whether the 'illah in qiyas should be considered as the specific cause ('ayn) or the genus (jins). Some Hanafis denied the genus within the genus, arguing that the effective cause is only the genus. Others, like Fakhr al-Islam, restricted consideration to the genus. Ibn al-Humam dropped the genus in the species, arguing that it reduces to species in species. The majority, however, accept both specific and generic 'illah in qiyas, as long as the effect is established textually or by consensus. Examples include the deposit of a child (wadi'a) and various applications of necessity (darura). The passage also contrasts Hanafi and Shafi'i views on mursal al-mula'im, concluding that Hanafis accept it while Shafi'is have conditions. The final note emphasizes that mere suitability without effect cannot be acted upon, but only considered.

Key Terms
جنس (jins): Genus; a general category that includes specific types (anwa').
عين (ayn): Specific; the particular individual or type within a genus.
علة (illah): Legal cause; the effective attribute that necessitates a ruling.
مرسل ملائم (mursal mula'im): A suitable but disconnected (mursal) attribute that is not explicitly linked to a text but is appropriate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafis, is qiyas valid when the 'illah is a genus affecting the genus of the ruling?
A) No, qiyas is invalid in such cases.
B) Yes, it is considered qiyas and is valid.
C) Only if the genus is close (qarib).
D) Only if there is an explicit text (nass) for the genus.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school, in its majority, accepts both a specific and generic 'illah, allowing qiyas even when the cause is a genus, provided the effect is established textually or by consensus.

The Two Types of 'Illah in Hanafi Usul
Defines 'illah as two types: name and direct attribution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two types of 'illah as defined by the Hanafis and explain how each type relates to the ruling.

Core Idea
The Hanafi 'illah is both a name for the cause and the direct attributor of the ruling – it is the effective element, not just a sign.

In Hanafi legal theory, 'illah (legal cause) is the key to analogical reasoning (qiyas). However, the term itself has a precise definition. This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut presents the Hanafi classification of 'illah into two types: one that names the cause and one that directly attributes the ruling. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly identifying the effective cause in istinbat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
Locate the word 'علة' in the Arabic text. Recognize that this passage is a definition of a key usul term.
2
List the two types of 'illah
The passage states that 'illah is divided into two: (1) علة اسماً – 'illah as a name, placed for its legal effect; (2) العلة التي أضيف إليها الحكم بلا واسطة – 'illah as that to which the ruling is attributed without intermediary.
The phrase 'بلا واسطة' (without intermediary) indicates direct attribution.
3
Understand the hesitation and interpretation
The text says 'الترديد إشارة إلى الاختلاف في التفسير' – the hesitation in phrasing points to a disagreement among scholars on the precise definition. This is a hallmark of Hanafi usul works acknowledging ikhtilaf.
4
Grasp the meaning of 'illah
The passage concludes that the meaning of 'illah is 'تأثيرها في الحكم' (its effect in the ruling) and even 'بل المؤثر فيه' (rather it is the effect in it). This emphasizes that 'illah is not merely a sign but actually brings about the ruling.
This aligns with the Hanafi view that 'illah must be suitable and effective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(تتمة: قسم الحنفية ما يطلق عليه (العلة حقيقة أو مجازاً إلى علة اسماً، الموضوعة لموجبها شرعاً (أو المضاف إليها أي العلة التي أضيف إليها (الحكم بلا واسطة) الترديد إشارة إلى الاختلاف في التفسير (ومعنى وهي تأثيرها في الحكم) بل المؤثر فيه وحكماً
(Appendix: The Hanafis divided what is called 'illah, in reality or metaphor, into: 'illah as a name, the name for its legal effect, or that to which the ruling is attributed without intermediary; the hesitation is an indication of disagreement in interpretation. And its meaning is its effect in the ruling, rather it is the effect in it and a ruling.)
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This appendix provides a concise definition of 'illah (legal cause) from the Hanafi perspective. They divide 'illah into two types: first, as a name (ism) that is placed for its legal effect (i.e., it is the cause that necessitates the ruling); second, as that to which the ruling is attributed without any intermediary (i.e., directly). The hesitation in the phrasing points to a difference in interpretation among scholars. The passage also clarifies that the meaning of 'illah is its effect in the ruling, or rather it is the effect itself and a ruling (hukm). This emphasizes that the 'illah is not just a description but the actual effective element that brings about the ruling.

Key Terms
علة (illah): Legal cause; the attribute from which a ruling is derived, either by name or direct attribution.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many types of 'illah are mentioned?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Four

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of 'illah is twofold: it is both a name for the cause and that which directly attributes the ruling, and its essence is its effective impact on the ruling.
