The Role of Genus (Jins) in Hanafi Qiyas and Types of Mula'im
Explaining the role of jins in qiyas and classification of mula'im

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi concept of qiyas via jins (genus) and classify the types of mula'im (suitable descriptions) accepted or rejected by the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The Hanafis accept all suitable descriptions in qiyas, except those so strange (gharib) that they lack any legal indication.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut clarifies a subtle but crucial point in Hanafi usul: how a genus (jins) can serve as the basis for qiyas without requiring a specific 'illa. It then outlines which types of suitable descriptions (mula'im) are accepted by the Hanafis, contrasting with the Shafi'i position. Understanding this distinction is essential for proper legal analogy in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the concept of jins in qiyas
Understand that the Hanafis do not require the exact 'illa from the asl; rather, the genus of 'illa suffices to extend the ruling. The passage explains that the asl contains the genus of 'illa, not the specific 'illa.
This is a key departure from some other usul schools that demand precise textual effect.
2
Recognize the examples of jins-based qiyas
Study the darura (necessity) examples: carrion, cat's leftover water, tayammum, rubbing sandals, apportioning grains. Notice how necessity as a genus yields different rulings appropriate to each context.
Each example shows the same jins (necessity) producing a specific alleviation.
3
Classify the types of mula'im
Distinguish between mu'aththir (effective), three types of mula'im, and three types of mula'im mursal according to Shafi'i classification. The passage states that Hanafis accept all except gharib mursal and all gharib types.
Gharib mursal has no legal indication whatsoever.
4
Apply the Hanafi criteria for effect
Note the methods of establishing effect (ta'thir): nass (text), ijma' (consensus), ikhala (inferred suitability), or presentation on usul (al-‘ard ‘ala al-usul). These are the Hanafi prerequisites for considering a description effective.
Ikhala is related to istihsan and is a uniquely Hanafi tool.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جنس فواتح الرحموت شرح مسلم الثبوت الجزء الثاني الحكم الثابت بها ثابت بالنص الوارد في جنس الحكم، وهذا التعليل ينبيء عن اثباته الحكم في الأصل فتأمل فيه ولعلهم من ههنا لقبوا بأصحاب الرأي هذا من الملقبين شيء عجيب فإن منهم من اعتبر الإخالة ورد المراسيل من السنن ومنهم من قبلها والمصالح المرسلة أيضاً، وعملوا بالاستصحاب الذي ليس دليلاً أصلاً فهم أولى بأن يلقبوا بهذا الاسم فافهم (والحق أنه قياس لا لأن الأصل) ما يوجد فيه عين العلة وهو (متروك) فإنه قد ما فيه بل لأن الجنس إذا مر اقتضى الجنس ممن الحكم بأن أثر الجنس في الجنس تنوع اقتضاؤه في الأنواع له بفصول منوعة) أي اقتضى الجنس للعلة في كل نوع منها نوعاً من الحكم الذي يناسبه (فأنواع الحكم من لوازم تحققه أي تحقق ذلك الجنس في الأنواع فالأصل في هذا القياس هو ما تحقق فيه العلة موجباً لجنس الحكم. فيتعدى هذا الجنس إلى فرعه الذي هو نظيره في هذا الجنس لكن يتحقق في نوع مناسب لهذا المحل ويتنوع اقتضاء هذا الجنس في هذا المحل كالضرورة اقتضت في الاضطرار حل (الميتة لأن اقتضاءها فيه يناسبه (و) اقتضت (في الطواف طهارة سؤر الهرة كما يناسب الطواف ذلك (و) اقتضت (عند) وجود (ماء الشرب فقط دون غيره من الماء (جواز التيمم كما يناسبه إلى غير ذلك كما أنها اقتضت في النعال الطهارة بالدلك، وفي الحنطة والشعير الطهارة بالقسمة يعني الضرورة جنس اقتضت التخفيف، وله أنواع يوجد في كل مادة نوع منه مع ما يناسبه من أنواع الضرورة، فكل نوع من الحكم يصلح مقيساً عليه لآخران كان حكمه منصوصاً أو مجمعاً عليه (نعم) : إذا كان الجنس قريباً ففهم ذلك قريب) لظهور ما به الاشتراك فيه وإذا كان بعيد فأدق فهمه لا ينال إلا بفكر قوي فالمظهر للتأثير والاعتبار هو الأصل) الذي أثر الجنس في جنس حكمه المنصوص أو المجمع عليه (وهذا) أي التساوي في جنس الحكم (نحو) من المساواة المطلقة المعتبرة في مطلق القياس المعرف بمساواة الفرع للأصل لأن المراد أعم من النوعية أو الجنسية فتدبر إنه دقيق عزيز) حتى يعرف وينكر (وعلى هذا الذي ذكر من أن الأقسام المذكورة كلها معتبرة فالمؤثر وثلاثة من الملائم وثلاثة من ملائم المرسل في عرف الشافعية كلها مقبول ومؤثر عند الحنفية كما ظهر لك عن قريب دون الغريب من المرسل بل الغريب مطلقاً لعدم ظهور تأثيره شرعاً) بوجه من الوجوه، ولا بد منه (ثم المذكور في كتب الحنفية أن التأثير عندنا بالنص أو الإجماع والإخالة أو العرض على (الأصول وقد مر تفصيله عند الشافعية شرط لوجوب العمل وأما الجواز) للعمل فيثبت بالملاءمة فقط فإن الوصف شاهد والتأثير ونحوه عدالة، وبفقدانها لا العمل، لكن يجوز كما أنه لو قضى القاضي بالشهود الغير العدول نفذ قضاؤه (أقول : المناسبة فقط) بدون التأثير ونحوه تفيد ظن الاعتبار أولاً، والأول واجب العمل به لأن الاتباع بالظن واجب (والثاني ممتنع عمله لأن ما لا يظن كونه حكم الله فحرام العمل فتدبر).
Genus - Fawatih al-Rahmut sharh Muslim al-Thubut part two. The ruling established by it is established by the text occurring in the genus of the ruling, and this ta'lil indicates his establishing the ruling in the asl, so reflect. And perhaps for this they were nicknamed 'people of opinion'. This is an astonishing nickname, for among them are those who consider ikhala and reject mursal from the sunan, and among them are those who accept them and also masalih mursala, and they act on istishhab which is not a proof at all, so they are more deserving of this name. Understand. (And the truth is that it is qiyas, not because the asl contains the exact 'illa - that is abandoned - rather because when the genus passes, the genus necessitates from the genus of the ruling in that the effect of the genus in the genus diversifies its requirement in the types for it by differentiating particulars.) That is, the genus necessitates the 'illa in each type a type of ruling that is appropriate. (So the types of ruling are from the necessary consequences of its realization, i.e., the realization of that genus in the types. So the asl in this qiyas is that in which the 'illa is realized causing the genus of the ruling. So this genus extends to its branch which is its counterpart in this genus, but it is realized in a type appropriate to this locus, and the requirement of this genus varies in this locus.) Like necessity necessitated in dire necessity the permissibility of carrion because its requirement therein is appropriate, and it necessitated in tawaf the purity of the leftover water of a cat as tawaf is appropriate for that, and it necessitated when there is only drinking water without other water the permissibility of tayammum as is appropriate, and so on. Also, it necessitated in sandals purification by rubbing, and in wheat and barley purification by apportionment. That is, necessity is a genus that necessitated alleviation, and it has types; in each matter a type is found with the appropriate type of necessity. So each type of ruling is suitable to be measured upon another if its ruling is textually stated or agreed upon. (Yes, if the genus is close, then understanding it is close) due to the clarity of the common element; if it is far, then its fine understanding is not attained except with strong reflection. So the manifestor of effect and consideration is the asl which affected the genus of its ruling that is textually stated or agreed upon. And this, i.e., equality in the genus of the ruling, is a kind of absolute equality considered in absolute qiyas defined as the equality of the branch to the asl, because the intent is more general than specific or generic equality, so reflect. It is delicate and precious, so it is recognized and denied. (And based on what was mentioned, that all the mentioned divisions are considered: al-mu'aththir, three of al-mula'im, and three of mula'im mursal in the terminology of the Shafi'is - all are accepted and effective according to the Hanafis, as appeared to you recently, except for gharib mursal; rather gharib absolutely, due to the lack of its effect being shown legally, in any way, and it is necessary. Then it is mentioned in the books of the Hanafis that effect according to us is by text or consensus, or ikhala, or presentation on the usul. Its detail has passed. According to the Shafi'is, it is a condition for obligatory action. As for permissibility of action, it is established by mula'ama only, for the description is a witness, and effect and the like are integrity, and without it there is no action, but it is permissible. As if a judge judged with non-upright witnesses, his judgment is executed.) I say: suitability alone without effect and the like yields zann of consideration first; the first is obligatory to act upon because following zann is obligatory, and the second is prohibited to act upon because what is not zann to be Allah's law, acting upon it is forbidden. So reflect.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut is an expansion on the role of genus (jins) in qiyas as understood by the Hanafi school. The author begins by noting that the ruling established via jins is rooted in a text, and this indicates that the early Hanafis were called 'people of opinion' (ashab al-ra'y). However, he finds this nickname odd because many of them actually accepted ikhala (inferred suitability) and rejected mursal hadith, while accepting masalih mursala and acting on istishhab. Then the author clarifies that the correct view is that this is a form of qiyas, not because the asl contains the exact 'illa (which is abandoned as a requirement), but because the genre (jins) when present necessitates a genus of ruling that diversifies into specific types appropriate to each case. He illustrates with examples: necessity (darura) as a genus that yields specific alleviations - eating carrion in extreme hunger, purity of cat's leftover water for tawaf (circumambulation), tayammum when only drinking water is available, and even purification of sandals by rubbing or grains by apportionment. In all these, necessity as a genus produces a type of alleviation suitable to each situation. Therefore, the asl in this type of qiyas is the case where the 'illa is realized, causing the genus of the ruling, and from there the ruling extends to branches that share that genus. The passage then states that if the common genus is close, understanding is easy; if far, it requires strong reflection. The key point for the student is that according to the Hanafis, all the divisions of suitable descriptions (al-mula'im) are accepted: al-mu'aththir (effective), three types of mula'im (suitable), and three types of mula'im mursal (suitable without textual reference) - all are considered effective (mu'aththir) at the Hanafis, except the gharib (strange) mursal, and indeed all gharib descriptions are rejected due to the lack of any legal indication of their effect. The Hanafis establish effectiveness (ta'thir) by text (nass), consensus (ijma'), ikhala (inferred suitability, a form of istihsan), or by presenting the description to the established principles (al-‘ard ‘ala al-usul). For the Shafi'is, these requirements are conditions for obligatory action, but for permissibility of action, suitability alone suffices, much like a judge may execute judgment based on non-upright witnesses. The author concludes that sheer suitability without effectiveness yields two possible degrees of zann (speculative belief) about the description being considered: one is stronger (obligatory to follow) and the other weaker (forbidden to act upon). The student should understand that the Hanafi method here is to require a clear indication of the description's effect before employing it in qiyas, rejecting mere suitability without such indication.

Key Terms
الجنس (al-jins): The general category or genus that includes multiple specific types and serves as a basis for qiyas by necessitating a genus of ruling.
الملائم (al-mula'im): A description that is suitable (munasib) for the ruling but does not have explicit textual effect.
المؤثر (al-mu'aththir): A description that has an explicit effect (ta'thir) established by text or consensus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, which type of mula'im do the Hanafis reject in qiyas?

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts all forms of suitable descriptions in qiyas, except those without any legal indication, thus making the genus (jins) a flexible tool for legal analogy.

The Threefold Definition of 'Illah: Ism, Ma'nan, Hukman
Defining 'illah in three aspects with sale examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three Hanafi categories of 'illah (ism, ma'nan, hukman) and apply them to the case of bay' al-khiyar.

Core Idea
An 'illah can be complete (ism+ma'nan+hukman) or partial (ism+ma'nan) when a preventer delays the ruling.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the concept of 'illah (legal cause) is central to qiyas. This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut introduces a tripartite classification: 'illah as name (ism), as meaning (ma'nan), and as ruling (hukman). Understanding this distinction is crucial for analyzing how causes operate when preventers like khiyar (option) are present. The text illustrates with the example of a sale with an option, where the cause is ism and ma'nan but not hukman until the option expires.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories of 'illah
State the three aspects: ism (the cause designated for the ruling), ma'nan (the effective cause), and hukman (the cause with which the ruling is directly connected). Note that the complete 'illah combines all three.
The text uses 'illa isman, 'illa ma'nan, 'illa hukman.
2
Recognize the complete 'illah example
Absolute sale (without option) is a complete 'illah for ownership: it is placed for ownership (ism), effective in ownership (ma'nan), and ownership is connected to it (hukman). This is the 'illa tamma (complete cause).
Shaykh Ibn al-Humam defined 'illa tamma as 'jamlatu ma yatawaqqafu 'alayhi' (the sum of what the effect depends on).
3
Understand the partial 'illah (ism + ma'nan only)
A sale with an option (bay' al-khiyar) is 'illah ism and ma'nan but not hukman because the option (khiyar) is a preventer (mani') that delays the ownership transfer. The 'illa is not fully connected to the ruling until the option is removed.
When the option expires, ownership is retroactively established from the time of the offer (istinad taqdiri).
4
Apply the distinction to the zakat nisab example
The nisab (minimum wealth threshold) for zakat is 'illah ism and ma'nan: it is placed for zakat and effective in obligating zakat, but the ruling (obligation) is connected to the growth (nama') which resembles a cause. This shows a partial 'illah similar to bay' al-khiyar.
The text mentions that the nisab 'has a resemblance to the cause that interposes between it and the ruling.'

Supplement: The Hanafis divided what is called 'illa (cause), truly or metaphorically, into: 'illa as a name, that which is placed for its legal effect, or that to which the ruling is attributed without intermediary—the alternation indicates a difference in interpretation; and 'illa as meaning, which is its effect in the ruling, rather the effective in it; and 'illa as a legal ruling, which is its conjunction with it. Rather, the 'illa with which the ruling is connected, according to the correct saying, they said: the aforementioned combination, which is the 'illa in name, meaning, and ruling, is the true 'illa, like absolute sale from the owner or his agent without an option for either as a cause for ownership. For it is placed for it or attributed to it and effective in it, and ownership is connected to it. And Shaykh Ibn al-Humam said it is the complete 'illa because it is the sum of what it depends on. (And the reality, i.e., the reality of the 'illa, may be realized without it (the conjunction). The cycle is that it is with the 'illa as meaning, in existence and non-existence. Perhaps they meant by the reality of the 'illa that which is effective actually, such that it necessitates the effect, for that is the true 'illa. As for the 'illa as meaning, it only effects after its completion by the existence of conditions and removal of preventers, so understand. (I say: when the 'illa is complete, the effect is connected to it. So the conjunction is not internal to the reality, i.e., the reality of the 'illa, nor to the complete 'illa. So this combination is not a true 'illa nor a complete 'illa, but rather from the necessary concomitants. (Yes) it is (a revealer of completeness) due to its necessary connection to it. So reflect. And this is nothing, for the conjunction is not internal to it as we indicated, rather the 'illa as a ruling is that with which the ruling is connected, and it together with the effective one is a complete 'illa absolutely, as is not hidden. And the Hanafis divided into: 'illa as name and meaning only, not as a ruling, like sale with option for the placement, i.e., for the placement of the sale for ownership, and the attribution, i.e., its being such that ownership is attributed to it, so it is a 'illa as name, and the effect, i.e., its effect in ownership, so it is a 'illa as meaning, and ownership is not connected with it to be a 'illa as a ruling. And the delay, i.e., the delay of the ruling from the effective; the preventer is the option. And it does not necessitate from the absence of the ruling due to a preventer despite the existence of the effective, the specification of the 'illa for those who deny its permissibility because of its incompleteness, i.e., the 'illa according to him with the existence of the preventer. Rather, the effective only achieves its effect by the removal of the preventer. And what was answered in al-Talwih that the disagreement is about the permissibility of specifying the 'illa in descriptive 'illas, not positional 'illas; rather specification is permissible in positional ones by consensus, and the sale is a 'illa by the placement of the Legislator, so it is pure ruling. How not, for the evidences of the two groups are general, as will appear to you soon, God willing. And when the ruling is established upon its removal, i.e., the preventer which is the option, from the time of the offer, the buyer owns the increase, and deserves the pre-emption of the house sold next to it before the fall of the option, and his dispositions are valid, etc. It is known that it is not a cause (sabab), for the ruling of the cause is only established purposefully, not as a basis from the time of its existence; this is the affair of the 'illa. And since it might be imagined from the establishment of the ruling from the time of the offer that it is also a 'illa as a ruling, he said: (And the establishment), i.e., the establishment of the ruling here is not in the way of clarification that the ruling was established from the beginning in actuality, so its establishment appears now as in acknowledgments, so that it would be a 'illa as a ruling also (because the condition), i.e., the condition of the option, is a preventer from the establishment of the ruling in reality, so the ruling was not truly established before its removal. Rather, it is the establishment of the ruling from the time of the offer by way of ascription estimatively only, so reflect. And from it, i.e., 'illa as name and meaning, is the nisab for zakat. For it is placed for it and attributed to it and effective in making zakat obligatory, because wealth is suitable for enrichment, and it is indicated by what is in the two Sahihs: a questioner said, 'God commanded you to take from our rich and distribute to our poor?' The Messenger of God, may God bless him and his family and companions and grant them peace, said: 'O God, yes, except that this has a resemblance to the cause that interposes between it and the ruling, the 'illa, the delay of its ruling to what resembles the 'illa.' It is the growth (nama') which the year was established from it, possible, in its place. And it had a resemblance to the 'illa because in it.. is taken, it is the emancipation (al-i'taq).
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This supplement (tatimma) from Fawatih al-Rahmut deals with the definition of 'illa (cause) in Hanafi usul. The Hanafis divide what is called 'illa into three aspects: (1) 'illa as a name (ism) – that which is designated to bring about its legal effect; (2) 'illa as a meaning (ma'nan) – that which has an actual effect on the ruling; (3) 'illa as a legal ruling (hukman) – that which is directly connected to the ruling. The correct view, according to the text, is that the 'illa that combines all three aspects is the true 'illa. An example is an absolute sale (without option) from the owner or his agent: it is placed as a cause for ownership, attributed to it, effective in it, and ownership is connected to it. Shaykh Ibn al-Humam considered this the 'illa tamma (complete cause) because it includes everything on which the effect depends. The author further explains that the 'illa as meaning only becomes effective after the presence of all conditions and the absence of preventers. The conjunction of the ruling with the 'illa is not part of the essence of the 'illa, but rather a necessary concomitant that reveals its completeness. The Hanafis then identify a type of 'illa that is ism and ma'nan only, not hukman: the example is a sale with an option (khiyar). In such a sale, the contract is placed for ownership (so it is ism) and has an effect on ownership (ma'nan), but ownership is not immediately connected (hukman) because the option prevents it. The ruling (transfer of ownership) is delayed until the option is removed. When the answerer in al-Talwih argues that the disagreement about specifying the 'illa (takhsis al-'illa) concerns descriptive 'illas, not positional 'illas like sale (which is placed by the Legislator), the author agrees that specification is permissible for positional 'illas by consensus. When the option falls, the ruling (ownership) is established from the time of the offer (retroactively), leading to the buyer owning increase, having pre-emption rights, and valid dispositions. This retroactive establishment is not by way of actual prior existence (tabayyun) but by way of estimative ascription (istinad taqdiri). In contrast, a true cause (sabab) would establish the ruling from the time of its existence purposefully. The passage ends with another example: the nisab (minimum threshold) for zakat, which is an 'illa as ism and ma'nan because it is placed for zakat, attributed to it, and effective in making zakat obligatory due to the suitability of wealth for enrichment. The citation from the Sahihs indicates that the Prophet confirmed that zakat is to be taken from the rich, but the nisab is like a cause, though with a resemblance to a cause because growth (nama') is the actual effective factor. The student should note the careful distinction between ‘illa and sabab, and the role of preventers (mawani‘) in delaying the effect.

Key Terms
العلة اسماً (al-'illa isman): The cause that is designated or placed for the ruling, to which the ruling is attributed.
العلة معنى (al-'illa ma'nan): The cause that has an actual effect on the ruling, but may be delayed by a preventer.
العلة حكماً (al-'illa hukman): The cause with which the ruling is directly connected (muqaran), constituting the complete cause.
الخيار (al-khiyar): A preventer (mani') that delays the legal effect of the ‘illa (e.g., ownership in sale) until it is removed.
تخصيص العلة (takhsis al-'illah): Specification of the cause, i.e., restricting its effect to certain cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi classification, what distinguishes an 'illa hukman from an 'illa ma'nan?
A) 'Illa hukman is directly connected to the ruling, while 'illa ma'nan only has an effect that may be delayed.
B) 'Illa hukman is the same as 'illa ma'nan.
C) 'Illa hukman is the cause that is designated for the ruling.
D) 'Illa hukman is the cause that is effective but not connected.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi tripartite division of 'illah into ism, ma'nan, and hukman explains how a cause can be valid even when its effect is delayed by a preventer, as in bay' al-khiyar.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
10 min
The Three Attributes of 'Illa and Its Classification in Hanafi Usul
Classification of 'illa and the zakat nisab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three attributes of a legal cause (ism, ma'na, hukm) and classify any cause into one of the five Hanafi types, including the nisab for zakat.

Core Idea
A cause in Hanafi usul need not have all three attributes; partial causes are legally valid.

The Hanafi school refines the concept of 'illa by analyzing it into three dimensions: whether the cause is linguistically established for the ruling (ism), whether it has a real effect (ma'na), and whether the ruling is actually attached to it (hukm). This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut elaborates on these categories and applies them to the debated case of the nisab for zakat, illustrating why the nisab is a cause by name and meaning only.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three attributes
Understand that 'illa is analyzed by (1) ism: the cause is named after the ruling, (2) ma'na: it has a real effect on the ruling, and (3) hukm: the ruling is actually conjoined with it.
2
Recognize the real cause (al-'illa haqiqa)
When all three attributes are present, the cause is the real cause, e.g., an absolute sale that immediately transfers ownership.
Some scholars equate this with the complete cause (al-'illa al-tamma), but the author distinguishes them.
3
Distinguish partial causes
A cause may have only one or two attributes. Examples: sale with option (ism and ma'na only), last part of composite cause (ma'na and hukm only), travel for rukhsah (ism and hukm only), suspended obligation (ism only).
These are still valid causes in their respective contexts.
4
Apply to the zakat nisab
The nisab is established for zakat (ism) and has an effect (ma'na), but the ruling of obligation is not conjoined until the year passes (hukm absent). Thus it is a cause by name and meaning only.
Contrast with Shafi'i view that nisab is a complete cause.
5
Evaluate the cross-madhhab dispute
Compare Hanafi, Shafi'i, and Maliki positions on whether the nisab is a complete cause, and note the practical implications for prepayment of zakat.
The Hanafi position is supported by the hadith that zakat is due after the year.

للاغناء، ويومىء إليه ما في الصحيحين» أن سائلاً قال : الله أمرك أن ا من أغنيائنا وتقسم على فقرائنا؟ فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم اللهم نعم إلا أن لهذا شبهاً بالسبب الذي يتخلل بينه وبين الحكم العلة التراخي حكمه إلى ما يشبه العلة . وهو النماء الذي أقيم الحول الممكن منه (مقامه وإنما كان له شبه بالعلة لأن فيه نوع مناسبة بإيجاب الصرف، فإن الصرف من الزيادة أيسر، وشكرها ألزم (لا إلى العلة) أي لم يتراخ إلى العلة نفسها فتمحض النصاب سبباً، لأن النماء وصف) في موجب الإغناء (لا يستقل بنفسه ولا يوجب الغنى، فلا يوجب الإغناء، فلا يصلح للعلة (خلافاً للشافعي) رحمه الله تعالى فعنده النصاب علة تامة للوجوب لصحة التعجيل عنده والأداء قبل الوجوب لا يصح فالحول تأجيل عنده تفضلا منه سبحانه وعندنا المؤدي موقوف، فإن بقي النصاب إلى ما بعد الحول يصير المؤدي زكاة، وإلا لا، إذ عند البقاء يثبت الوجوب مستنداً، وعند الهلاك لا وجوب فلا استناد فلا أداء للواجب، بل يصير نقلاً (قلنا : لو كان النصاب (علة تامة) وثبت الوجوب في الذمة الوجبت الزكاة مع الاستهلاك في الحول) كما تجب مع الاستهلاك بعد الحولان وفيه ما فيه لأن وجود العلة كما يستلزم وجود المعلول كذا انتفاؤها انتفاءه، فيرتفع الوجوب بارتفاع النصاب كذا في «الحاشية». وجوابه : أن النصاب إنما هو علة عنده لابتداء الوجوب لا للبقاء، بدليل بقاء الوجوب بعد الاستهلاك، والهلاك بعد الحولان فافهم (و) خلافاً لمالك، فإنّ العلة عنده النصاب مع النماء، فلا يصح التعجيل عنده) أصلاً، إذ لا وجوب قبل الحولان، لا حقيقة ولا استناداً (و) قسم الحنفية إلى علة معنى وحكماً فقط) لا اسماً (كالجزء الأخير من العلة المركبة) فإنه مؤثر والحكم مقترن، لكنه غير موضوع له ولا مضاف إليه (كملك القريب) فإنّ العلة للعتق مجموع القرابة والملك، وهو آخرها (وجعل ما عدا الجزء الأخير كالعدم في الإضافة حتى يضاف الحكم إليه فقط، حتى يكون علة اسماً أيضاً (كما ذهب إليه طائفة) على ما نقل في «التلويح خلاف التحقيق ألا ترى أن الشاهد الأخير إذا رجع لا يضمن الكل بل النصف فهو جزء أخير لعلة ،الإتلاف مع أن الاتلاف لم يضف إليه ولم يضمن إلا النصف (وأن السفينة إذا غرقت بأربعة (1) كر فلكل كر دخل) في الغرق (بالضرورة) فكذا ههنا، فجعل بعض أجزاء العلة في حكم العدم تحكم (نعم) الجزء الأخير كاشف عن الزيادة فإنما هو العلة (ظاهراً في بادىء الرأي لا على الحقيقة (و) قسم الحنفية (إلى علة اسماً وحكماً فقط لا معنى (وهو) كل مظنة أقيمت مقام المؤثر) لكونها موضوعة لها ومضافاً إليها، والحكم مقترن بها من غير تأثير ما فيه كالسفر للترخص إقامة للدليل الذي هو السفر (مقام المدلول) الذي هو المشقة، وهي المؤثرة حقيقة (وكالنوم للحدث إقامة للاسترخاء) أي لاسترخاء المفاصل الذي هو الدليل (مقام) خروج النجس الذي هو المؤثر في الحدث (و) قسم الحنفية إلى علة اسماً فقط لا معنى ولا حكماً كالايجاب المعلق فإن الحكم مضاف إليه، وهو موضوع له، لكن لا تأثير له فيه لما تقدم أن الشرط يمنع السببية ولم يقترن الحكم به أيضاً (وكاليمين قبل الحنث للكفارة باعتبار الإضافة أي هو علة اسماً لإضافة الحكم إليه، كما قال تعالى : فَكَفَرَتُهُ إطْعَامُ عَشَرَةِ مَسَكِينَ ﴾ [المائدة: (۸۹] الآية (لا) باعتبار (الوضع) أي كونه موضوعاً لها (فإنها) وضعت (للبر) والكفارة إنما تجب ستر الذنب الحنث (و) قسم الحنفية
The fourth principle: Qiyas. It is the conjunction of the ruling with it (the cause). Rather, the cause with which the ruling is conjoined, according to the correct view, is the mentioned 'aggregate' (al-majmoo'), which is the cause by name, meaning, and ruling—that is the real cause. Like an absolute sale by an owner or his agent without a right of option for either party is a cause for ownership: it is established for it, added to it, effective in it, and ownership is conjoined with it. Shaykh Ibn al-Humam said that it is the complete cause (al-'illa al-tamma) because it is the sum total of what the ruling depends on. The reality (haqiqa) of the cause may be realized without [conjunction?]. The rotation? ... They likely meant by the real cause that which is actually effective, necessitating the effect, for that is the real cause. As for the cause in meaning (al-'illa ma'nan), it only has effect after its completion by the presence of conditions and removal of preventers, so understand. I say: When the cause is complete, the effect is conjoined with it. Thus conjunction is not part of the reality—i.e., the reality of the cause—nor part of the complete cause. So this aggregate is not a real cause nor a complete cause but rather a necessary concomitant. Yes, it is a revealer of completion (kashif 'an al-tamam) because it entails it. So reflect. ... The Hanafis divided [cause] into: (1) Cause by name and meaning only, not by ruling—like a sale with a right of option, because it is established for ownership (by name), added to ownership (by name), and effective in ownership (by meaning), but ownership is not conjoined with it so it is not a cause by ruling. The preventer is the option. (2) Cause by meaning and ruling only, not by name—like the last part of a composite cause. (3) Cause by name and ruling only, not by meaning—like any indicator (mazannah) set up in place of the effective cause. (4) Cause by name only, not by meaning nor by ruling—like a suspended obligation (al-ijab al-mu'allaq).
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut provides a detailed exposition of the types of legal cause ('illa) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author classifies 'illa according to three attributes: name (ism), meaning (ma'na), and ruling (hukm). These attributes correspond to whether the cause is established for the ruling (nome), has a real effect (meaning), and is actually conjoined with the ruling (hukm). The Hanafi school recognizes that a cause may possess any combination of these attributes, leading to several categories. 

The first category is the 'real cause' (al-'illa haqiqa), which has all three attributes, like an unconditional sale that immediately transfers ownership. The second is cause by name and meaning only (like a sale with a khiyar al-shart option, which is called a 'sale' and has an effect on ownership, but ownership does not take effect until the option is lifted). The third is cause by meaning and ruling only (like the last part of a composite cause, e.g., the final moment of possessing a relative for emancipation—the effect is immediate and conjoined, but the cause is not named after that part). The fourth is cause by name and ruling only (like travel for rukhsah: travel is called a cause and the ruling of rukhsah is conjoined, but the real effect is hardship, not travel itself). The fifth is cause by name only (like a suspended obligation, e.g., a vow before violation: it is called a cause and the ruling of kaffarah is added to it, but it has no real effect until the violation occurs, and the ruling is not conjoined at the moment of the vow). 

The text also discusses the debate with Imam al-Shafi'i regarding whether the nisab for zakat is a complete cause. The Hanafis hold that nisab is a cause by name and meaning only, because the obligation is delayed until the year passes, and additional conditions like growth (nama') are needed. This leads to practical differences, such as the validity of prepaying zakat before the year ends. The Hanafis consider such payment as provisional (mawquf), whereas al-Shafi'i accepts it as valid because he considers nisab a complete cause.

Key Terms
العلة حقيقة (al-'illa haqiqa): The real cause, which has all three attributes: it is established for the ruling, is effective in it, and is conjoined with it.
العلة التامة (al-'illa al-tamma): The complete cause, which is the sum total of what the ruling depends on, including all conditions and absence of preventers.
العلة اسماً (al-'illa isman): The cause by name: the term is used to designate something that is established for the ruling, even if it does not have a real effect.
العلة معنى (al-'illa ma'nan): The cause in meaning: it has a real effect on the ruling, but the ruling may not be conjoined with it due to a preventer.
العلة حكماً (al-'illa hukman): The cause by ruling: the ruling is actually conjoined with it, even if it does not have a name or effect independently.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi classification in this passage, what type of 'illa is the nisab for zakat?
A) 'Illa by name and ruling only
B) 'Illa by name and meaning only
C) 'Illa by meaning and ruling only
D) 'Illa by name, meaning, and ruling (real cause)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school classifies causes based on three attributes (ism, ma'na, hukm), allowing for partial causes that are still legally effective, such as the nisab for zakat being a cause by name and meaning only.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

10 min
The 'Illa for Zakat: Nisab as Sabab or Complete 'Illa?
Dispute on the cause of zakat obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on the 'illa for zakat and distinguish it from the Shafi'i and Maliki views, applying the concept of sabab vs. 'illa.

Core Idea
Nisab is a cause (sabab) for initiating zakat obligation, not the complete 'illa; growth is a condition.

This lesson examines a key dispute over the cause of zakat obligation. Understanding the Hanafi view that nisab alone is insufficient helps clarify rules like advance payment and the effect of consuming nisab. We will explore why Hanafis treat nisab as a sabab, not the complete 'illa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
State the question: What is the 'illa that makes zakat wajib? The Hanafis, Shafi'is, and Malikis differ.
2
State the Hanafi position and its proof
Nisab is not a complete 'illa; it is a sabab. The proof: if nisab were complete, consuming it during the year would not remove obligation, but it does.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i and Maliki positions
Shafi'i: nisab is complete 'illa (allows advance payment). Maliki: nisab + growth is 'illa (disallows advance). Understand their proofs.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafi refutation: nisab is only for initial obligation; consumption removes it. Growth is a condition (shart) not part of 'illa.
5
Extract the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: permissibility of advancing zakat before the year. Hanafis allow with condition, Shafi'is unconditionally, Malikis forbid.
This is the key outcome of the dispute.

(Not to the cause itself) meaning it does not delay to the cause itself, so the nisab becomes a mere cause, because growth is a description) in what necessitates enrichment (it does not subsist by itself nor cause richness, so it does not cause enrichment, thus it is not suitable for being a cause. (Contrary to al-Shafi'i) may Allah have mercy on him, for with him nisab is a complete cause for obligation due to the validity of acceleration with him, and performance before obligation is not valid, so the year is a deferment with him as a favor from Him about Him. With us, the performed is suspended; if the nisab remains after the year, it becomes zakat, otherwise not, because upon remaining, obligation is established based [on the past], and upon destruction, no obligation so no basing, so no performance of the obligatory; rather it becomes a gift. (We said: if the nisab were a complete cause and obligation were established in the liability, then zakat would be obligatory even with consumption during the year) as it would be obligatory with consumption after the year. And therein lies what lies, because existence of the cause necessitates existence of the effect, and similarly its absence necessitates its absence, so obligation is removed by removal of nisab. So in al-Hashiya. Its answer: nisab is only a cause with him for the beginning of obligation, not for continuance, evidenced by the continuance of obligation after consumption and destruction after the year has passed. So understand. (And) contrary to Malik, for the cause with him is the nisab with growth, so acceleration is not valid with him) at all, since there is no obligation before the year, neither in reality nor by basing. (And) the Hanafis divided [the cause] into cause by meaning and effect only) not by name, like the last part of a composite cause, for it is effective and the ruling is attached, but it is not placed for it nor attributed to it. (Like ownership of a relative) for the cause for emancipation is the sum of kinship and ownership, and it [the last part] is the last of them. (And they consider what is other than the last part as non-existent in attribution, so the ruling is attributed to it alone, so that it becomes a cause by name as well (as held by a group) as transmitted in al-Talwih, contrary to verification. Do you not see that if the last witness retracts, he does not guarantee the whole but half, for he is the last part of the cause of damage, although damage was not attributed to him and he only guarantees half. (And that if a ship is sunk by four kars, each kar contributes to sinking necessarily, so here too. So considering some parts of the cause as non-existent is arbitrary. (Yes) the last part reveals the increase, so it is the cause (apparently at first glance, not in reality. (And) the Hanafis divided (into cause by name and effect only, not meaning, (which is) every likely sign set up in place of the effective [cause]) because it is placed for it and attributed to it, and the ruling is attached to it with no effect therein, like travel for license, setting up the evidence which is travel (in place of the inferred) which is hardship, which is truly effective. (And like sleep for ritual impurity, setting up relaxation) i.e., relaxation of joints which is the evidence (in place of) the exit of filth which is the effective in impurity. (And) the Hanafis divided into cause by name only, neither meaning nor effect, like a suspended obligation, for the ruling is attributed to it, and it is placed for it, but there is no effect in it because the condition prevents causality, and the ruling is not attached to it either. (And like an oath before breaking for expiation, from the perspective of attribution, i.e., it is a cause by name because the ruling is attributed to it, as Allah said: 'So its expiation is feeding ten needy' [Quran 5:89] not from the perspective of (placement) i.e., being placed for it, for they were placed for righteousness, and expiation is only obligatory to cover the sin of breaking. (And) the Hanafis divided into cause by meaning only) not by name and effect, like the preceding part of a composite cause (for it has an entry in effectiveness) so it is a cause by meaning, and it was not placed for the ruling nor attributed to it nor attached. (Hence it is not a cause) with Imam Fakhr al-Islam and his noble associates, (contrary to al-Dabusi) Chief Imam Abu Zayd (and) Imam Shams al-A'imma (al-Sarakhsi), who considered that there is no effect before the existence of the later part, but it leads with mediation of the later, and this is the nature of a cause. The more correct is what Fakhr al-Islam said, and therefore they considered the mere existence of measure or genus as a doubt in usury of deferment, so they prevented bartering wheat for barley. (And) he said in al-Talwih: This contradicts what is established) with them that there is no effect for parts of the cause on parts of the effect; rather the complete cause affects the complete effect, so the preceding part has no effect. (I say: Their intent) from what is established is (raising the total obligation, and negating necessity), i.e., it is not necessary that each part of a cause have an effect on each part of its effect, because it is possible that the ruling of the whole differs from the ruling of each of the units, as in dragging a heavy load from a mountain, for the group can do it but each individual cannot drag a part proportional to his share. (Otherwise, sometimes) the effect may be (for parts on parts as for the whole on the whole, like a composite medicine for a composite disease), for each part affects one by one of the disease components. So then there is no contradiction at all, regarding the contribution and effect of the part of the cause (not as being piecemeal such that the part has effect in isolation, but its meaning, i.e., the meaning of the effect of the part, is that it constitutes the effective factor and has effect within the effect of the whole on the effect. This does not contradict its lack of effect individually on a part of the effect. So understand. (And) the Hanafis divided into cause by effect only) not by name and meaning, (like the existence of a condition) for the occurrence of the suspended ruling, (and the last part of a composite cause, because there is no attribution, and placement here is only attachment. (And the more plausible) in my view is that the purchase of a relative) which grants ownership necessitating emancipation, (and every cause of a cause from it, so reflect.) So the categories of what is called 'illa are seven: one triple composite 'illa by name, meaning, and effect; three binary composites: 'illa by name and meaning, 'illa by meaning and effect, 'illa by name and effect; and three singulars: 'illa by name, 'illa by meaning, 'illa by effect.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on the nature of 'illa (cause) in Hanafi usul. It begins with a dispute regarding the 'illa for zakat obligation. According to the Hanafis, the nisab alone is not a complete 'illa because the aspect of growth (nama') is a condition for enrichment; Shafi'is hold nisab as complete, allowing advance payment, while Malik requires both nisab and growth. The Hanafis argue that if nisab were the full 'illa, then consuming the nisab during the year would not remove obligation, but it does; thus nisab is a cause (sabab) not the 'illa. The text then divides 'illa into three aspects: ism (name), ma'na (meaning), and hukm (effect). A composite 'illa has a last part that is effective and attached to the ruling but not designated as the sole 'illa by name; earlier parts contribute only as part of the whole. Examples include the last witness in a case and the last part of a composite cause. The Hanafis further categorize: 'illa by name and effect only (e.g., travel for license, where the true effective is hardship), 'illa by name only (e.g., suspended obligation, where the ruling is attributed but there is no effect due to condition), 'illa by meaning only (e.g., earlier part of a composite cause, which contributes within the whole but is not independently effective). A dispute between Fakhr al-Islam and al-Sarakhsi on whether such parts are causes is resolved in favor of Fakhr al-Islam, supported by examples from riba. The passage concludes with a summary of seven types: one triple, three binary, and three singular, covering all combinations of name, meaning, and effect.

Key Terms
علة ('illa): The cause that is effective in producing a legal ruling.
سبب (sabab): A cause that initiates obligation but does not by itself create a continuous effect.
مظنة (mazannah): A likely sign placed in lieu of the true cause, e.g., travel for license representing hardship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis reject the view that nisab is the complete 'illa for zakat?
A) Because nisab is not mentioned in the Quran.
B) Because consuming nisab during the year removes the obligation, unlike if it were a complete cause.
C) Because the year is not completed.
D) Because the Hanafi school follows a different hadith.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi position distinguishes between sabab (initial cause) and complete 'illa; for zakat, nisab is a sabab and growth is a condition.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
15 min
Hanafi Classification of 'Illa: Name, Meaning, and Effect
Systematic classification of 'illa into seven categories

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the seven types of 'illa in Hanafi usul and apply the categories of ism, ma'na, and hukm to examples.

Core Idea
The 'illa is not monolithic; it can be analyzed by name, meaning, and effect, creating seven possible classifications.

Usul al-fiqh scholars analyze the 'illa (cause) from different angles: its name (ism), its intrinsic meaning (ma'na), and its legal effect (hukm). The Hanafis developed a detailed taxonomy that combines these aspects, including composite causes and signs (mazannah). This lesson unpacks that taxonomy.

Guided Path
1
Understand the three aspects: ism, ma'na, hukm
Ism refers to the name or label; ma'na is the effective meaning; hukm is the legal ruling attached. A complete 'illa has all three, but many have only two or one.
These are not separate 'illas but perspectives on the same attribute.
2
Examine the composite 'illa
A composite 'illa has parts. The last part is the one that triggers the ruling directly (hukm), but earlier parts contribute to the meaning (ma'na). Example: ownership of a relative for emancipation.
The last part is like the last witness or the last kar sinking a ship.
3
Study the 'illa by name and effect only (mazannah)
Examples: travel for license (the true 'illa is hardship) and sleep for ritual impurity (the true 'illa is relaxation of joints). These are signs placed by the lawgiver that are effective by name and effect but not by meaning.
The meaning is absent, but the law still attaches the ruling to the sign.
4
Study the 'illa by name only and by meaning only
'Illa by name only: suspended obligations (e.g., oath before breaking). 'Illa by meaning only: early parts of a composite cause that contribute to effectiveness but are not attributed to the ruling.
This distinguishes contributions from full causation.
5
Memorize the seven types
One triple (all three), three binary (ism+ma'na, ma'na+hukm, ism+hukm), and three singular (ism, ma'na, hukm). Understand examples for each.
This taxonomy is distinctive to Hanafi usul.

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on the nature of 'illa (cause) in Hanafi usul. It begins with a dispute regarding the 'illa for zakat obligation. According to the Hanafis, the nisab alone is not a complete 'illa because the aspect of growth (nama') is a condition for enrichment; Shafi'is hold nisab as complete, allowing advance payment, while Malik requires both nisab and growth. The Hanafis argue that if nisab were the full 'illa, then consuming the nisab during the year would not remove obligation, but it does; thus nisab is a cause (sabab) not the 'illa. The text then divides 'illa into three aspects: ism (name), ma'na (meaning), and hukm (effect). A composite 'illa has a last part that is effective and attached to the ruling but not designated as the sole 'illa by name; earlier parts contribute only as part of the whole. Examples include the last witness in a case and the last part of a composite cause. The Hanafis further categorize: 'illa by name and effect only (e.g., travel for license, where the true effective is hardship), 'illa by name only (e.g., suspended obligation, where the ruling is attributed but there is no effect due to condition), 'illa by meaning only (e.g., earlier part of a composite cause, which contributes within the whole but is not independently effective). A dispute between Fakhr al-Islam and al-Sarakhsi on whether such parts are causes is resolved in favor of Fakhr al-Islam, supported by examples from riba. The passage concludes with a summary of seven types: one triple, three binary, and three singular, covering all combinations of name, meaning, and effect.

Key Terms
علة ('illa): The cause or reason in qiyas; can be considered by name (ism), meaning (ma'na), or effect (hukm) individually or in combination.
سبب (sabab): A cause that is not independently effective but requires additional elements; here, preceding parts of a composite cause are considered sabab by al-Sarakhsi.
مظنة (mazannah): A likely sign placed in lieu of the true effective cause, e.g., travel for license representing hardship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is an example of 'illa by name and effect only (ism + hukm)?
A) The complete composite 'illa for emancipation: kinship + ownership
B) Travel as cause for license to shorten prayer
C) A suspended obligation like an oath before breaking
D) The preceding part of a composite cause

Key Takeaway
Hanafi usul classifies 'illa into seven types based on combinations of name (ism), meaning (ma'na), and effect (hukm); 'illa by name and effect only includes mazannah (likely signs) like travel for license.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
The Condition of Ba'itha: Why the 'Illa Must Be Appropriate
Argues that an 'illa must be munasib (appropriate) to the ruling, otherwise it is a mere sign.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafi usul requires the 'illa to be munasib (appropriate) and distinguish it from the mere tard (consistent co-occurrence), citing the Hanafi proof from circularity.

Core Idea
An 'illa that is merely a sign with no rational link to the ruling leads to circularity and invalidates qiyas.

In Hanafi usul, a valid 'illa for qiyas must be 'ba'itha'—i.e., munasib (appropriate) to the ruling, reflecting the Lawgiver's purpose of achieving benefit or repelling harm. This condition distinguishes the Hanafi approach from the 'ahl al-tard', who accept any consistently occurring attribute as an 'illa. In this passage, the author explains why mere tard is insufficient, citing Ibn al-Hajib's argument from circular reasoning. Understanding this condition is essential for correctly applying qiyas and avoiding arbitrary extensions of rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position on the 'illa
State that the 'illa must be ba'itha (appropriate/munasib) to the ruling, meaning it must have a discernible link to the legislative purpose (maslaha).
The term 'ba'itha' is synonymous with 'munasib'.
2
Recognize the opposing view (ahl al-tard)
Identify that ahl al-tard accept any attribute that consistently accompanies the ruling, even without a known rationale.
This view is rejected by the Hanafis.
3
Analyze the Hanafi refutation based on circularity
Follow Ibn al-Hajib's argument: if the 'illa is a mere sign with no effect, its only function is to identify the ruling in the original case. But the 'illa is derived from that ruling, leading to a vicious circle (knowledge of the ruling depends on the 'illa, and the 'illa depends on knowledge of the ruling).
This proves the 'illa must have a genuine effect beyond identification.
4
Consider the response of ahl al-tard and the Hanafi counter
Ahl al-tard claim the 'illa's benefit is not limited to identification but includes applying the ruling to the original. The Hanafi response dismisses this as obstinacy, arguing a causal connection is necessary.
The text labels this counter as 'mukabara' (obstinacy).
5
Conclude the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis require munasaba for any qiyas, while ahl al-tard would accept analogies based on any constant feature, even if the rationale is unknown.
This affects which analogies are considered valid.

Source Text

ثم ههنا أي في فصل العلة مقصدان : المقصد الأول : في شروطها المتفق عليها والمختلف فيها منها : أن تكون العلة (باعثة أي مناسبة ولو بالاشتمال كما في المظنة لشرع الحكم المقصود منه تحصيل مصلحة أو تكميلها أو دفع مفسدة أو تقليلها كما في العلل المأثورة) من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم وهو المراد بالملائمة في كلام مشايخنا الكرام، وخالف فيه أصحاب الطرد (لأنه (لولاها أي لولا المناسبة لكان (التعليل به (تعبداً) من الحكيم (فلا يقاس عليه لعدم موجب الحكم وهو ظاهر جداً (واستدل) الشيخ ابن الحاجب (في المختصر بأنها لو كانت العلة (مجرد أمارة) ولم يكن لها مناسبة وتأثير في الحكم (لزم الدور لأنها لا فائدة لها إلا تعريف الحكم في الأصل فيكون معرفة حكمه موقوفاً عليها (وهي مستنبطة منه) فتكون متوقفة على معرفته، ولأصحاب الطرد أن يمنعوا انحصار الفائدة فيه، بل فائدتها عندهم فيه على الأصل، لكن يدفع بأنه مكابرة إذ من البين أن ما لا تأثير فيه لا يوجب الحكم (أقول : فيه نظر، أما أولاً : فلأن الأمارة المجردة عن المناسبة (قسيم الباعثة لا مقصود
Then here, i.e., in the chapter of 'illa, there are two objectives: The first objective: Regarding its conditions agreed upon and those differed upon, among them: that the 'illa be ba'itha, i.e., appropriate, even if by inclusion, as in the mazannah, for the legislation of the ruling intended from it to obtain a benefit or complete it or repel an evil or reduce it, as in narrated causes from the Messenger of Allah and his Companions. This is what is meant by suitability in the speech of our honorable masters. The people of tard opposed it. Because if not for it, i.e., the appropriateness, then the ta'lil by it would be a purely devotional act from the Wise, so analogy upon it would not be valid due to lack of basis for the ruling, and this is very clear. And Sheikh Ibn al-Hajib argued in al-Mukhtasar that if the 'illa were a mere sign and had no appropriateness and effect in the ruling, then circularity would follow because its only benefit is to identify the ruling in the original case, so knowledge of its ruling would be dependent on it, and it is deduced from it, thus it would be dependent on knowledge of it. The people of tard could prevent the exclusivity of benefit in that; rather its benefit with them is to [apply] the ruling to the original case. But it is rebutted that it is obstinacy, since it is obvious that what has no effect does not necessitate a ruling. (I say: There is consideration in it. First, because the mere sign without appropriateness is a counterpart of the ba'itha, not the intended...
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage introduces the conditions of a valid 'illa for qiyas. The first condition is that the 'illa must be 'ba'itha' or 'munasib'—meaning it must be appropriate to the ruling and aligned with the legislative purpose of achieving benefit (maslaha) or repelling harm. This is the standard of Hanafi scholars. In contrast, the 'People of Tard' (those who accept mere consistency or 'tard') argue that any attribute that is co-extensive with the ruling suffices as an 'illa, even without discernible appropriateness. The text refutes this by stating that without munasaba, the 'illa becomes a purely devotional (ta'abbudi) identifier—since a wise Lawgiver would not base rulings on arbitrary signs—and thus analogy (qiyas) cannot be extended from it. Ibn al-Hajib's argument from circularity is cited: if the 'illa is merely a sign to identify the ruling in the original, and the 'illa itself is derived from that ruling, then one would need to know the ruling to derive the 'illa and vice versa, creating a vicious circle. The defenders of tard may object that the benefit of the 'illa is not merely identification but applying the ruling to the original; however, this is dismissed as arbitrary, because something with no causal effect cannot ground obligation. The author (likely the commentator) then adds a preliminary objection: the mere sign is a distinct category from the ba'itha, not the subject of this condition. The passage ends mid-argument.

Key Terms
باعثة (ba'itha): An 'illa that is appropriate (munasib) to the ruling, intended by the Lawgiver to achieve a benefit or repel harm.
مناسبة (munasaba): Suitability or appropriateness between the 'illa and the ruling, reflecting a rational connection that aligns with the Lawgiver's purpose.
طرد (tard): Consistent co-occurrence of an attribute with a ruling, without requiring a discernible rationale; accepted by ahl al-tard as sufficient for 'illa.
تعبد (ta'abbud): A ruling or act that is purely devotional, based on obedience without a discernible rationale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafis, why is it invalid to use a mere 'amara (sign) without munasaba as an 'illa?
A) Because it leads to circular reasoning.
B) Because the Shafi'is forbid it.
C) Because it contradicts the Quran.
D) Because it is not based on analogy.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires the 'illa in qiyas to be ba'itha (appropriate), based on the principle that a mere sign without causal effect leads to circular reasoning and cannot ground analogy.

The Part of a Composite 'Illa: Influence or Cause?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the 'illa status of a part of a composite cause

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the disagreement between Fakhr al-Islam and al-Dabusi/al-Sarakhsi regarding the effect of a part of a composite 'illa, and state the Hanafi relied-upon position and its practical consequence in riba al-nasi'a.

Core Idea
A part of a composite 'illa has influence (dakhl) but is not a standalone sabab—this shapes Hanafi rulings on riba al-nasi'a.

The Hanafi tradition on qiyas examines whether a component of a composite cause (like the first part of a two-part 'illa) can be considered a cause on its own. This lesson unpacks the dispute between two Hanafi authorities and its impact on a classic riba scenario. The debate hinges on whether a part independently contributes to the ruling or only within the whole.

Guided Path
1
State the Issue
What is the legal question? The text asks: Does a part of a composite 'illa have any effect (ta'thir) on the ruling, and if so, is it considered a cause (sabab) or merely an 'illa by meaning?
The disagreement is between two major Hanafi figures: Fakhr al-Islam and al-Dabusi/al-Sarakhsi.
2
Identify the Two Positions
Fakhr al-Islam holds that a part has influence (dakhl) but is not a cause; it is 'illa by meaning only. Al-Dabusi and al-Sarakhsi argue that the part functions as a cause because it leads to the effect via the later part.
Fakhr al-Islam's view is preferred in the text: 'al-azhar ma qala Fakhr al-Islam'.
3
Analyze the Proofs
For Fakhr al-Islam: the part does not independently bring about the ruling; only the complete composite does. The part contributes within the whole, like individuals in a group dragging a heavy stone. For the opponents: the part leads to the effect with mediation, similar to a cause.
The example of dragging a stone: group can do what individuals cannot, so the whole is not reducible to parts.
4
Note the Tarjih
The text favours Fakhr al-Islam because the part's influence is not independent. The response addresses an objection from al-Talwih, clarifying that non-necessity of part-effect does not negate possible effect in some cases (e.g., compound medicine).
Thus the mufta bihi is that a part is 'illa by meaning only.
5
Apply the Thamarah
How does this disagreement affect practical rulings? The text mentions that in riba al-nasi'a, the mere existence of measure (kayl) or genus (jins) is considered a doubt (shubha) preventing exchange of wheat for barley. This follows from Fakhr al-Islam's view that a part has influence, not independent causality.
The consequence: even if only one attribute is present, it creates a doubt that forbids the transaction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصل الرابع القياس يجب إلى علة معنى فقط لا اسماً وحكماً كالجزء المتقدم من العلة المركبة فإن له دخلاً في التأثير فيكون علة معنى ولم يوضع للحكم ولم يضف إليه هو ولم يقترن ومن ثمة لم يكن سبباً عند الإمام فخر الإسلام وكرام عشيرته خلافاً للدبوسي القاضي الإمام أبي زيد و الإمام شمس الأئمة السرخسي وهما نظراً إلى أن لا تأثير له قبل وجود الجزء المتأخر، وإنما له الإفضاء مع وساطة المتأخر، وهذا شأن السبب، والأظهر ما قال فخر الإسلام، ولذا اعتبروا وجود الكيل أو الجنس فقط شبهة في ربا النسيئة، حتى منعوا إسلام الحنطة في الشعير و قال في التلويح : هذا يخالف ما تقرر عندهم أن لا تأثير لأجزاء العلة في أجزاء المعلول، وإنما المؤثر تمام العلة في تمام المعلول فلم يكن للجزء المتقدّم تأثير أقول : مرادهم مما تقرّر رفع الإيجاب الكلي، ونفي الوجوب أي لا يجب تأثيراً جزاء كل علة في أجزاء معلولها لجواز مخالفة حكم الكل حكم كل من الآحاد كما في جر الثقيل من الجبل فإنه يقدر عليه الجماعة ولا يقدر واحد واحد على جر جزء جزء بقدر حصصهم وإلا فقد يكون التأثير للأجزاء في الأجزاء كما للتمام في التمام، كالدواء المركب لمرض مركب فإنه يؤثر كل جزء منه في واحد واحد من المرض فحينئذ لا تنافي أصلاً على أن الدخل والتأثير لجزء العلة لا أن يكن بطريق التبعيض بأن يكون للجزء تأثير حال الانفراد بل معناه أي معنى تأثير الجزء أن يكون مقوماً للمؤثر ويكون له تأثير في ضمن تأثير الكل في المعلول، وهذا لا ينافي عدم تأثيره انفراداً في جزء المعلول فافهم و قسم الحنفية إلى علة حكماً فقط لا اسماً ومعنى كوجود الشرط لوقوع الحكم المعلق والجزء الأخير من السبب المركب لعدم الإضافة، والوضع إنما هو ههنا الاقتران والأشبه عندي أن شراء القريب المفيد للملك الموجب للعتق وكل علة العلة منه فتدبر فأقسام ما يطلق عليه العلة سبعة، واحد مركب ثلاثي العلة اسماً ومعنى وحكماً، وثلاثة مركبات ثنائية وهي العلة اسماً ومعنى. والعلة معنى وحكماً والعلة اسماً وحكماً، وثلاثة مفردات وهي العلة اسماً والعلة معنى والعلة حكماً.
The fourth principle: Qiyas. It is necessary ... to an 'illa by meaning only, not by name and ruling, like the preceding part of a composite 'illa, for it has an influence (dakhl) in the effect, so it is an 'illa by meaning, and it was not placed for the ruling nor added to it nor associated with it. Hence it is not a cause (sabab) according to Imam Fakhr al-Islam and his noble group, contrary to al-Dabusi and al-Sarakhsi, who both consider that it has no effect before the existence of the subsequent part, and it only leads [to the effect] with the mediation of the subsequent, and that is the nature of a cause. The more apparent is what Fakhr al-Islam said, and for this reason they considered the mere existence of measure or type as a doubt (shubha) in riba al-nasi'a, so they forbade selling wheat for barley. And [the author] said in al-Talwih: This contradicts what is established with them that parts of the 'illa have no effect on parts of the effect, rather only the complete 'illa affects the complete effect; so the preceding part has no effect. I say: what they mean by what is established is the negation of universal obligation and the negation of necessity, i.e., it is not necessary that each part of a 'illa affect a part of its effect, because it is possible for the ruling of the whole to differ from the ruling of each individual part – like dragging a heavy stone from a mountain; a group can do it but each individual cannot drag a part equal to his share. Otherwise, there may be effect of parts on parts, as of the whole on the whole, like a compound medicine for a compound disease, for each part affects one part of the disease. So then there is no contradiction at all. The influence (dakhl) and effect of a part of the 'illa should not be understood as a fragmentation, such that the part would have effect in isolation, but rather its meaning – i.e., the meaning of the part's effect – is that it constitutes (muqawwim) the effector, and it has an effect within the overall effect on the effect. This does not contradict its having no effect in isolation on a part of the effect. So understand. And the Hanafis divided [the 'illa] into an 'illa by ruling only, not by name and meaning, like the existence of a condition for the occurrence of the suspended ruling, and the last part of a composite cause, due to the absence of attribution; the placement here is only association. And the more apparently correct to me is that the purchase of a relative, which confers ownership and necessitates emancipation [cases?] and all 'illa of 'illa from it, so ponder. Thus the categories of what is called 'illa are seven: one is a triple composite: 'illa by name, meaning, and ruling; three are double composites: 'illa by name and meaning, 'illa by meaning and ruling, 'illa by name and ruling; and three are singles: 'illa by name, 'illa by meaning, 'illa by ruling.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage from the sharh provides a detailed classification of 'illa (cause) in qiyas. The author begins by discussing the status of a part of a composite 'illa. According to Fakhr al-Islam (a Hanafi authority), a part of the 'illa (like the initial part of a composite cause) is considered 'illa by meaning only, not by name or ruling, because it has an influence (dakhl) in the effect but is not independently designated as the cause. The Dabusi and al-Sarakhsi argued that such a part actually functions as a cause (sabab) because it leads to the effect via the later part, but the author prefers Fakhr al-Islam's view. A practical application: in riba al-nasi'a, the mere existence of measure (kayl) or genus (jins) is considered a doubt (shubha) such that exchanging wheat for barley in a spot transaction is forbidden. The author then responds to an objection from al-Talwih, explaining that the non-necessity of each part affecting its specific part does not negate the possibility of such effect in some cases. Finally, the author presents the Hanafi division of 'illa into seven types based on whether it is 'illa by name, meaning, and ruling: one triple composite (by all three), three double composites (pairwise combinations), and three singles (each alone). This classification helps understand how different legal descriptors function in analogical reasoning.

Key Terms
علة ('illa): A descriptor that is the effective cause (mu'aththir) of a ruling in qiyas.
علة معنى ('illa bi ma'na): An 'illa that has influence but is not formally designated as the cause.
سبب (sabab): A cause that directly brings about the ruling; here distinguished from 'illa.
شبهة (shubha): A doubt that triggers a legal precaution; here, the presence of a part of the 'illa creates a shubha.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in this passage, a part of a composite 'illa is:
A) A cause (sabab) by name and ruling.
B) 'Illa by meaning only, with influence but not independent causation.
C) A pure cause that independently produces the ruling.
D) Neither a cause nor an influence.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi is that a part of a composite 'illa has influence but is not an independent cause, affecting the assessment of shubha in riba transactions.

The Sevenfold Classification of 'Illa by Name, Meaning, and Ruling
Taxonomy of 'illa in Hanafi usul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list and distinguish the seven types of 'illa according to Hanafi usul, and classify a given descriptor as 'illa by name, meaning, or ruling.

Core Idea
An 'illa is classified by three attributes: name, meaning, and ruling—their combinations yield seven distinct categories.

This lesson unpacks the systematic classification of 'illa in Hanafi usul al-fiqh, showing how a descriptor can be a cause by its formal designation (ism), its effective influence (ma'na), or the ruling it produces (hukm). The seven types arise from combining these three criteria. Understanding this taxonomy is essential for correctly applying qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Three Attributes
The text identifies three attributes of an 'illa: (1) name (ism) – it is formally called an 'illa; (2) meaning (ma'na) – it has influence in the ruling; (3) ruling (hukm) – the ruling is attached to it. Note these are not mutually exclusive.
A descriptor can have one, two, or all three attributes.
2
Enumerate the Triple Composite
The only 'illa that has all three attributes simultaneously is the complete 'illa that is designated by name, has effective influence, and the ruling is directly attached to it. This is the archetype for qiyas.
Example: intoxication (sukr) for the prohibition of khamr.
3
Enumerate the Three Double Composites
Three combinations: (1) 'illa by name and meaning only (no ruling directly attached); (2) 'illa by meaning and ruling only (not formally named as 'illa); (3) 'illa by name and ruling only (but without effective influence, which is rare).
The text gives an example of a condition as 'illa by ruling only? Actually, it says 'like the existence of a condition for the occurrence of the suspended ruling' as 'illa by ruling only, which is a single, not double. Double composites are explained in the text.
4
Enumerate the Three Singles
A descriptor can be 'illa by only one attribute: (1) by name only (formally called 'illa but no influence or ruling); (2) by meaning only (has influence but not named or ruling); (3) by ruling only (the ruling is attached, but not named and no independent influence).
The text mentions that a condition is 'illa by ruling only.
5
Apply the Classification
Given a legal descriptor (e.g., safar for shortening prayer, or nisab for zakat), determine which category it falls into. For instance, is it 'illa by meaning only? By name and ruling?
This skill helps in verifying the validity of analogical reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage from the sharh provides a detailed classification of 'illa (cause) in qiyas. The author begins by discussing the status of a part of a composite 'illa. According to Fakhr al-Islam (a Hanafi authority), a part of the 'illa (like the initial part of a composite cause) is considered 'illa by meaning only, not by name or ruling, because it has an influence (dakhl) in the effect but is not independently designated as the cause. The Dabusi and al-Sarakhsi argued that such a part actually functions as a cause (sabab) because it leads to the effect via the later part, but the author prefers Fakhr al-Islam's view. A practical application: in riba al-nasi'a, the mere existence of measure (kayl) or genus (jins) is considered a doubt (shubha) such that exchanging wheat for barley in a spot transaction is forbidden. The author then responds to an objection from al-Talwih, explaining that the non-necessity of each part affecting its specific part does not negate the possibility of such effect in some cases. Finally, the author presents the Hanafi division of 'illa into seven types based on whether it is 'illa by name, meaning, and ruling: one triple composite (by all three), three double composites (pairwise combinations), and three singles (each alone). This classification helps understand how different legal descriptors function in analogical reasoning.

Key Terms
علة ('illa): A descriptor that is the effective cause (mu'aththir) of a ruling in qiyas.
علة اسماً ('illa bi al-ism): An 'illa that is formally designated by name as a cause.
علة معنى ('illa bi al-ma'na): An 'illa that has influence on the ruling.
علة حكماً ('illa bi al-hukm): An 'illa that has the ruling attached to it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many types of 'illa are there in the Hanafi classification based on name, meaning, and ruling?
A) 3
B) 7
C) 5
D) 9

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school classifies 'illa into seven types based on whether it includes name (ism), meaning (ma'na), and ruling (hukm), providing a precise taxonomy for qiyas.
